# MMR Audit — Findings & Remediation

_Generated by a 20-reviewer multi-agent audit with adversarial verification of every bug claim, a completeness-critic gap sweep, and a materiality pass on architectural findings._

**Totals:** 130 confirmed bugs, 38 material design findings, 13 refuted, 4 uncertain. Reviewers: 20, gap-probes: 4.

**Confirmed bug severity:** 8 critical · 43 high · 40 medium · 39 low


## Status legend

- [ ] not started  ·  [~] in progress  ·  [x] fixed


## Remediation — first pass (fixed in this branch)

The following capital-safety cluster has been fixed and covered by tests. See
`git log` / the diff for details.

1. **RPC transport desync + latent order redelivery** (`clientserver.py`) — the
   client now matches every reply's `req_id` and, on timeout, drops and recreates
   the DEALER socket (new identity) so a timed-out request can't be redelivered
   later and stale replies can't be misattributed to the next call. Sockets set
   `LINGER=0` + `IMMEDIATE=1` so an order to a down service fails loudly instead
   of being silently queued.
2. **RPC object-graph traversal** (`clientserver.py`) — server dispatch now
   resolves only single-segment names that carry the `@rpcmethod` marker; dotted
   traversal that bypassed the proposal gate is refused.
3. **Concurrent double-approve** (`proposal_store.py`, `sdk.py`) — `approve`/
   `reject` use an atomic compare-and-swap (`try_transition`); same-status
   "transitions" now raise. Exactly one of two racing approvers wins.
4. **approve() marked proposals FAILED while the order may be live** (`sdk.py`) —
   an order-submission timeout now leaves the proposal APPROVED and reports
   UNKNOWN (reconcile with broker) instead of the terminal-FAILED lie; only a
   clean connection failure marks FAILED.
5. **resize left positions naked** (`sdk.py`) — resize now places the delta
   first (existing protectives stay valid on failure), then cancels+recreates
   each protective one at a time with confirmation; unprotected windows are
   surfaced as loud warnings.
6. **to-market oversizing** (`sdk.py`) — uses `orderStatus.remaining`, confirms
   the cancel, and re-checks the fill before placing the market order.
7. **One strategy exception killed the whole tick feed** (`strategy_runtime.py`)
   — per-strategy dispatch is isolated; a raising strategy is set to ERROR and
   skipped while the feed stays alive.
8. **Dead safety gates revived** — open-order count now counts only *working*
   orders (`book.py`); the risk gate is fed `daily_pnl`/`portfolio_value`
   (`trading_runtime.py`); the trading filter fails loudly on a malformed config
   instead of degrading to allow-everything (`trading_filter.py`); the order
   validator rejects malformed quantity/prices instead of returning `True`
   (`order_validator.py`).
9. **Web dashboard** (`web/app.py`, `dashboard.html`) — proposal reasoning is
   sanitized (nh3 if present, else escape-first + URL-scheme filtering) killing
   the stored-XSS zero-click approve; approve/reject require a per-process CSRF
   token; an optional `MMR_WEB_TOKEN` gates access.

Not yet addressed in pass 1 (see pass 2 below and the still-open list):
broker-truth reconciliation on restart, FX normalization, IB reconnect
subscription restoration, proposal expiry, and the wider medium/low list.


## Remediation — second pass (fixed in this branch)

Highs:
- **Non-BRACKET exit rollback** (`trading_runtime.py`) — STOP_LOSS / TRAILING_STOP
  (and the NONE entry) now roll back the staged entry and return failure when a
  leg fails, instead of returning success with a zombie staged order and a
  proposal falsely marked EXECUTED.
- **Data-integrity poisoning** — `write_resolve_overlap` uses `keep='last'`
  (re-downloads correct stale bars) and drops NaN-close bars; `missing()` counts
  only days with real data so interior gaps are re-fetched; the IB history fetch
  in the CLI and data_service now connect+drive on ONE event loop (the old
  per-call `asyncio.run()` bound the socket to a dead loop, timing out and
  fabricating NaN data); `.env` excluded from the Docker image.
- **Executioner** — a market order requested WITH a stop-loss no longer becomes a
  bare stop-entry (wrong-direction trade); it fails loud toward the bracket path.
  Event-store logging can no longer turn a live order into a reported failure.
- **Position-flip guards** — `close --quantity` / `close_position` clamp to the
  held size so an oversized close can't flip the position.
- **Risk math** — correlation clustering revived (three API-signature bugs fixed,
  reads the history DB by conId, correlates on returns not price levels, logs
  instead of swallowing); ADV/ATR sizing reads the history DB by conId (was the
  trading DB by ticker — always empty, adjustments inert).
- **LLM-loop safety** — the monitor emits a "MONITORING DEGRADED" alert on a
  missing price instead of silently skipping the stop-loss check; the `approve`
  helper gets subprocess headroom and surfaces an explicit UNKNOWN/reconcile
  warning instead of a clean-looking failure.

Mediums: strict BUY/SELL action validation; sizing + trading-filter configs fail
loud on parse error; empty-string env vars no longer clobber YAML config; pycron
restart window uses `total_seconds()`; DuckDB upsert wrapped in a transaction;
frozen `DateRange` defaults fixed; `data refresh` reports real per-job success;
backtester Sortino uses proper downside deviation and trade P&L nets buy-side
commission; sizer block-reason and unknown-`--group` surfaced on the proposal;
daily-loss aggregation flags NaN PnL gaps; zero-volume names no longer bypass the
min-volume liquidity filter.

Still open after pass 2 — most cleared in pass 3 below.


## Remediation — third pass (low-severity sweep, fixed in this branch)

Correctness one-liners: `trader_exception` argument order (every exception's
`.message` was a bool); bool config coercion (bool-before-int, was crashing on
env override); warrant filter no longer drops SNOW/DOW/LOW; `find_symbol` treats
numeric strings as tickers not conIds; Sharpe-CI annualisation decodes the stored
bar-size string (`BarSize.parse_str`) instead of always throwing → 252; `group
--budget` is always a percentage (was turning 1% into 100%); `reject --all`
honours the per-proposal result; `propose --group` uppercases the symbol so it
matches budget tracking; project-root probe uses `pyproject.toml`.

Fail-loud / no-fake-data: group-budget analysis logs instead of swallowing;
idea-scanner per-symbol resolution failures log at WARNING; idea-scanner news
sentiment no longer attributes a co-mentioned ticker's sentiment to the scanned
one; `exchange_hint` NameError in the IB scanner path fixed.

Robustness: `connect()` backoff actually retries now (connection errors propagate
un-wrapped; AccountNotPinnedError stays fatal); strategy_service SIGINT no longer
calls `run_until_complete` inside the running loop; `MMRHelpers.cli()` uses
`shlex.split`; parallel `backtest_sweep` survives a timed-out child; VWAP resets
on the ET trading day, not UTC midnight.

Deliberately NOT changed (rationale): `total_trades` counts fills, not round-trips
— an intentional, test-enforced semantic; next_open slippage lookahead only
affects non-default impact models; sweep SIGINT-restore needs a risky 66-line
re-indent for a REPL-only impact; `date_summary` per-bar-size coverage needs a
store-API change.

Still open (need live-IB validation or a larger refactor): IB reconnect
subscription restoration (`trading_runtime.py:711`, `:579`,
`strategy_runtime.py:280`), order-success from IB ack vs local echo
(`trading_runtime.py:956`), FX normalization across resize/risk (`sdk.py:68`),
idea-scanner location→exchange resolution, IB daily-bar UTC-vs-exchange-tz keying,
universe resolver-cache invalidation, strategy enabled-state persistence,
`strategy_runtime.run()` EADDRINUSE restart-safety, ibreactive market-data
line/subscription leaks, and a few narrow CLI lows (options `--json` stdout, sweep
exception safety).


## Critical bugs


### [x] CRITICAL — Concurrent approve from two shells double-executes a proposal (silent same-status no-op defeats the state machine)

- **Location:** `trader/data/proposal_store.py:177`  ·  _reviewer: wrong-thing_

- **Mechanism:** MMR.approve (trader/sdk.py:1352-1364) does a read-then-act: it reads the proposal, checks status != 'PENDING', then calls update_status(id, 'APPROVED') and proceeds to place_expressive_order. The state machine in update_status is supposed to make this safe, but proposal_store.py:177-178 returns silently when current == status ('if current == status: return'), directly contradicting its own docstring ('Idempotent updates to the same terminal state are rejected too'). So when two processes both read PENDING, the loser's PENDING->APPROVED call is a silent success instead of an InvalidProposalTransition, and both processes go on to call place_expressive_order. The race window is not just the tiny read/update gap: shell B only needs to read the proposal before shell A writes APPROVED; B's update_status can land any time during A's multi-second RPC execution and still silently pass. The second EXECUTED write is also silently absorbed, so no error ever surfaces.

- **Failure scenario:** LLM loop and human both run `mmr approve 42` within ~1s of each other (or `approve --all` in two shells). Both read status=PENDING. Shell A sets APPROVED and starts the RPC (seconds). Shell B calls update_status(42,'APPROVED') -> current==status -> silent return; B then also calls place_expressive_order. Two identical live market orders are placed on account U26774889 — double position size, and if it was a bracket, two overlapping bracket groups.

- **Suggested fix:** Make update_status raise (or return a boolean the caller must check) on same-status 'transitions', or better: implement approve as an atomic compare-and-swap ('UPDATE ... SET status=APPROVED WHERE id=? AND status=PENDING' returning rows-changed) and abort execution when 0 rows changed.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. proposal_store.py:177-178 (`if current == status: return`) short-circuits before the legality check at 179-183; since _ALLOWED_TRANSITIONS['APPROVED'] (lines 26-30) excludes 'APPROVED', a duplicate PENDING→APPROVED by a second process resolves to APPROVED==APPROVED and returns silently instead of raising InvalidProposalTransition. In sdk.py:approve, update_status(id,'APPROVED') at line 1364 sits OUTSIDE the try (begins 1366), so a raise would abort execution — the silent return defeats that. approve is a read(get,1357)/check(1360)/update(1364) with no compare-and-swap, and per CLAUDE.md execute_atomic uses short-lived, released-between-queries connections with IOException retry, so two `mmr approve` processes interleave: both read PENDING, A writes APPROVED and starts the multi-second place_expressive_order RPC (1402), B's update(APPROVED) silently passes and B also places the order — double live orders / overlapping brackets. Critical: capital-safety failure exactly of the class the state machine exists to prevent; requires a concurrency window but the LLM-loop + human scenario is plausible.


### [x] CRITICAL — RPC client never validates req_id, so one timeout permanently desynchronizes all subsequent request/reply pairs on the socket

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:400`  ·  _reviewer: messaging_

- **Mechanism:** _SyncMethodCall.__call__ generates a req_id (line 372) and sends it, but on receive it takes whatever frame arrives next (recv_multipart at line 397) and returns response.get('result') without ever comparing response['req_id'] to the one it sent. The lock serializes calls, but after a TimeoutError (line 396) the server's late reply stays buffered in the DEALER socket. The next RPC call sends its request, poll() fires immediately on the stale buffered reply, and it is returned as the result of the new call — and because the new call's real reply is now buffered, every subsequent reply is off-by-one forever until the process restarts. _convert_return_type then coerces the wrong payload into the expected type (e.g. SuccessFail(*tuple)), producing garbage results or misattributed order confirmations. The SDK (sdk.py) uses a single long-lived RPCClient for the entire CLI REPL / LLM-loop session, so one slow IB call poisons the whole session.

- **Failure scenario:** In the mmr REPL, `approve 42` calls place_expressive_order; IB is slow and the 30s client timeout fires (order is still placed server-side and a SuccessFail reply arrives late). The user then runs `portfolio` — the client returns the stale place_expressive_order SuccessFail as the portfolio result; the next command gets the portfolio payload; every later command in the session returns the previous command's data. An LLM loop reading these misattributed responses records wrong order IDs / wrong risk state and keeps trading on them.

- **Suggested fix:** After recv, loop discarding any response whose req_id != the one just sent (and only count discards against the timeout budget). Alternatively, on TimeoutError close and recreate the DEALER socket so the stale pipe (and its identity) is dropped.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. Client sends req_id (clientserver.py:372,377) but the receive path (lines 397-413) returns response['result'] and never checks req_id. On timeout, line 396 raises TimeoutError inside the lock without draining or closing the DEALER socket; RPCClient.connect (528) makes one long-lived socket with no recreation on timeout. The server stamps and echoes req_id in every reply (481,485,492) with no knowledge of client timeouts, so a late reply buffers in the DEALER queue. The next call's poll() fires immediately on the stale frame (391-397) and returns it — permanent off-by-one desync. The REPL shares one MMR/RPCClient across all commands (mmr_cli.py:10001-10043), so one slow IB call poisons the session, feeding misattributed order confirmations/portfolio/risk to the LLM loop. The server echoing req_id shows correlation was intended but unimplemented. Precondition (a timeout firing) is uncommon, but the resulting silent, session-wide capital-affecting corruption is critical.


### [x] CRITICAL — Timed-out RPC requests stay queued in the DEALER pipe and execute later — 'failed' orders can silently fire when the server comes back

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:396`  ·  _reviewer: messaging_

- **Mechanism:** On timeout, _SyncMethodCall raises TimeoutError but does nothing to the socket or the in-flight message. With ZMQ's default ZMQ_IMMEDIATE=0, socket.send() at line 381 succeeds even when trader_service is down or unreachable — the message is queued in the DEALER pipe (up to SNDHWM) and is delivered automatically when the TCP connection (re)establishes. Nothing ever cancels it. The SDK's execute-proposal path (sdk.py:1403-1427) catches this TimeoutError in its generic `except Exception` and marks the proposal FAILED in the proposal store, so the system's state says the trade never happened while the order request is still latent in the pipe.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service is restarting when the user runs `approve 42`. place_expressive_order is queued in the client's DEALER pipe, the call times out, the proposal is marked FAILED. The user re-proposes and approves the same trade (proposal 43). When trader_service finishes starting, ZMQ delivers the buffered request from proposal 42 — a second, untracked bracket order is placed. The book now holds double the intended position, and proposal 42's records say it FAILED.

- **Suggested fix:** Set ZMQ_IMMEDIATE=1 and a small SNDHWM on the client socket, and on TimeoutError close+reopen the socket (new identity drops the queued pipe). Server-side, consider rejecting order-placing requests whose req_id timestamp is older than a staleness bound.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. Client socket is a plain DEALER (clientserver.py:528) with only RCVTIMEO/SNDTIMEO set — no ZMQ_IMMEDIATE, no SNDHWM, no LINGER (531-532; grep shows nothing else). So send() at line 381 queues the request when trader_service is down. On timeout, line 396 raises TimeoutError only; self.socket is never closed/recreated, so the message stays in the DEALER pipe and DEALER auto-flushes it on reconnect. The server has no req_id dedup or staleness check — _handle_request executes whatever arrives (461-489). SDK's approve path catches the TimeoutError in the generic `except Exception` and marks the proposal FAILED (sdk.py:1425-1427). In REPL mode the MMR/socket is long-lived (mmr_cli.py:10112-10119), so a trader_service restart mid-session delivers the buffered place_expressive_order after the proposal is recorded FAILED — a latent, untracked bracket order. Severity: critical for a capital-safety-first system — system state says FAILED while a live order fires; low frequency but high consequence.


### [x] CRITICAL — RPC client never matches response req_id, so any timeout permanently desyncs the request/reply stream

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:397`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** _SyncMethodCall.__call__ generates a req_id and the server echoes it back ({'req_id': req_id, ...} at line 481), but the client never compares the received response's req_id to the one it sent. On TimeoutError (line 396) the client raises and returns, leaving the late reply queued on the DEALER socket. The socket is never drained or reconnected. The next RPC call on the same MMR client sends a new request, sees POLLIN immediately (the stale frame), and recv_multipart returns the PREVIOUS call's reply as this call's result. Every subsequent call on that client is then off-by-one forever. The SDK's MMR object is long-lived (LLM trading loop, CLI REPL), and sdk.py methods routinely mix order-placement RPCs with data RPCs on the same client.

- **Failure scenario:** mmr.approve(42) calls place_expressive_order; IB is slow and the 30s client timeout fires (order still placed server-side). The LLM loop next calls mmr.portfolio() -> get_portfolio_summary, which receives the late SuccessFail[list[Trade]] from the order placement and _convert_return_type coerces it into garbage 'portfolio' rows; the real portfolio reply is then delivered to the NEXT call. A later place_order_simple call can receive a stale get_snapshot reply and interpret it as its order result, reporting success/failure for the wrong operation while real orders go untracked.

- **Suggested fix:** Loop on recv until response['req_id'] == req_id, discarding stale frames; or on TimeoutError close and recreate the DEALER socket so the queue is flushed.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. clientserver.py:372 sends a req_id; server echoes it (line 481); but client response handling (lines 400-413) never checks it. On timeout, line 396 raises without draining/recreating the DEALER socket (connect() at line 528 is the only socket creation; grep shows no reconnect/drain path). The socket+lock are shared and long-lived: sdk.py:179 builds one self._client (timeout=30) reused for both order-placement (place_expressive_order, line 803) and data RPCs (line 465). A late reply queues; the next call's poller sees POLLIN immediately (line 391) and recv_multipart NOBLOCK (line 397) returns the prior call's frame, coerced via _convert_return_type. Off-by-one persists permanently. Critical on a live-money system: a timed-out-but-executed order desyncs the stream, mis-attributing order success/failure and leaving real orders untracked. Only mitigant: requires a 30s timeout to actually fire.


### [x] CRITICAL — to-market re-places the ORIGINAL order quantity, ignoring partial fills, and never confirms the cancel

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:779`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** The CLI `to-market` command (trader/mmr_cli.py:1931) calls MMR.to_market(), which reads `quantity = float(order.totalQuantity)` from the existing trade. In the IB API, totalQuantity is the original order size; the unfilled portion is `trade.orderStatus.remaining`. The method then calls `self.cancel(order_id)` without checking the returned SuccessFail (or waiting for cancel confirmation) and immediately places a new market order for the full original quantity via place_expressive_order. Two mechanisms produce oversized positions: (a) partial fills are double-counted, and (b) if the cancel fails or the resting limit fills in-flight, both orders execute.

- **Failure scenario:** A limit BUY for 100 AAPL has filled 60 shares. Operator runs `mmr to-market <id>` to get the rest done. The 40-share remainder is cancelled, but the replacement market order is placed for 100 shares, leaving the account long 160 shares instead of 100 — a 60% oversized position on a live account. Separately, if the cancel is rejected because the order just filled, the market order still fires and doubles the position to 200.

- **Suggested fix:** Use `trade.orderStatus.remaining` (falling back to totalQuantity - filled) as the replacement quantity, verify the cancel result (and ideally wait for Cancelled status) before placing the market order, and abort with an error if remaining <= 0.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. trader/sdk.py:779 sets quantity = float(order.totalQuantity) — IB's ORIGINAL order size. Line 793 self.cancel(order_id) discards its SuccessFail return; lines 802-810 place a MARKET order for that full original quantity via place_expressive_order (which uses the passed quantity verbatim). No use of orderStatus.remaining/filled despite those fields being read elsewhere in the same file (sdk.py:635-636), and no remaining<=0 guard, cancel-confirmation, or Cancelled-status wait. Both harms occur: (a) a partially-filled limit (60/100) is re-placed at 100 → 160 shares long; (b) a discarded cancel result means a cancel rejected because the order just filled still fires the market order, doubling the position. tests/test_sdk.py:489 hard-asserts quantity==100.0 and never covers partial fills or cancel failure, so the bug is baked into expected behavior. On a live account this silently produces oversized positions — a capital-safety defect, hence critical despite being operator-triggered rather than autonomous.


### [x] CRITICAL — execute_resize_plan cancels protective orders first and never re-creates them if the delta order fails, leaving live positions unprotected

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1646`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** The per-position sequence is: (1) cancel all protective stops/TPs (failures only produce warnings, flow continues), (2) place the delta market order, (3) re-create protectives at target quantity. If step 2 fails or raises (order rejected by risk gate/trading filter, RPC TimeoutError, IB rejection), the code appends to results['failures'] and `continue`s -- skipping step 3 entirely. The protective orders were already cancelled in step 1, so the position is left at full original size with no stop-loss/trailing-stop. The inverse hole also exists: if a step-1 cancel fails (warning only), step 3 still runs, producing TWO live protective SELL orders (old qty + new qty) whose combined fills exceed the position and flip it short.

- **Failure scenario:** resize-positions --max-bound 500000 on a book with GTC trailing stops. For NVDA the delta SELL is rejected by the risk gate (daily order-rate limit hit mid-plan). Its TRAIL stop was already cancelled; the code continues to the next symbol. NVDA now sits unprotected overnight; a gap-down that the trailing stop would have caught produces an unbounded loss. Alternatively, a cancel that fails (order in transient state) followed by re-creation leaves STP SELL 100 + STP SELL 50 on a 50-share position; both trigger and the account goes short 100.

- **Suggested fix:** Reorder to place the delta first, then cancel/replace protectives one at a time; on any step-2 failure, re-place the original protective orders at original quantities before continuing. Abort re-creation for a symbol whose cancel did not confirm.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed by direct control-flow trace in trader/sdk.py:1583-1679. Step 1 (1601-1612) cancels protectives, treating cancel failures as warnings only. Step 2 (1614-1649) places the delta; on soft failure (1642-1646) or exception (1647-1649) it appends to failures and `continue`s. That `continue` skips Step 3 (1651-1677), so protectives already cancelled are never re-created — the position sits unprotected. Both risk-gate/filter rejections (SuccessFail.fail) and RPC/IB exceptions reach this path. The inverse hole also holds: a failed cancel is warning-only, yet Step 3 still re-creates, yielding two live protective orders (old+new qty) that can flip the position short. No compensating re-placement or unconfirmed-cancel abort exists. Severity critical for a live-money system: capital-safety consequence is unbounded gap loss or an unintended short, far outweighing the fact that it needs an operator-run resize plus a mid-plan failure.


### [x] CRITICAL — One strategy exception permanently kills tick dispatch for ALL strategies, logged only at DEBUG

- **Location:** `trader/strategy/strategy_runtime.py:247`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** on_ticker_next() calls strategy.on_prices(), event_store.append() and zmq_messagebus_client.write() with no try/except. The pubsub delivery chain is: TopicPubSub._subscriber_loop -> _Handler.on_message -> Subject.on_next -> AutoDetachObserver.on_next -> on_ticker_next. Any exception propagates back into _subscriber_loop's generic `except Exception` (clientserver.py:850), which calls handler.on_throw(ex) -> subject.on_error -> AutoDetachObserver.on_error, which sets is_stopped=True and dispose()s the observer, permanently detaching it from the subject. The subscriber loop keeps recv'ing, but the subject has no observers left, so every subsequent tick is silently dropped. The only trace is on_ticker_error's logging.debug('StrategyRuntime.on_error') — invisible at default log level. This violates both strategy exception isolation and the fail-loudly principle.

- **Failure scenario:** Two strategies are enabled; one has a live position it manages with SELL exit signals. The other strategy raises (e.g. pandas IndexError on a short tick window, or vectorbt on a NaN close) on any tick. From that moment, no strategy ever receives another tick until service restart: exit signals never fire, the open position is unmanaged through an adverse move, and the service appears healthy in `status`.

- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the per-strategy on_prices call (and the event-store/messagebus writes) in try/except inside on_ticker_next; log at ERROR, set only the offending strategy to StrategyState.ERROR, and keep the pipeline alive. Make on_ticker_error log at ERROR and re-subscribe.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. on_ticker_next (strategy_runtime.py:246-247) calls strategy.on_prices() with no try/except. AutoDetachObserver.on_next (reactivex autodetachobserver.py:28) forwards without catching; Subject._on_next_core (subject.py:65-66) has no guard; so the exception propagates to _subscriber_loop's except (clientserver.py:850), which calls handler.on_throw -> PubSubSubject.on_error (clientserver.py:250) -> AutoDetachObserver.on_error (autodetachobserver.py:33-38) sets is_stopped=True and dispose()s, permanently detaching the sole observer. The loop keeps recv'ing but drops every subsequent tick. Only trace is on_ticker_error's logging.debug (strategy_runtime.py:270). No recovery: observer created once in run() (line 666-671); _reconcile never re-subscribes it. One strategy's raise silently disables all strategy tick dispatch (exit/stop signals never fire) while status looks healthy — a capital-safety-critical isolation + fail-loudly violation.


### [x] CRITICAL — Stored XSS: proposal reasoning rendered as unsanitized raw HTML marked \| safe

- **Location:** `web/app.py:56`  ·  _reviewer: web_

- **Mechanism:** _render_md() runs proposal reasoning through Python-Markdown (_MD.convert) and returns the result, which fetch_proposals stores as r['reasoning_html'] (line 171) and the template emits with `{{ p.reasoning_html \| safe }}` (dashboard.html:268). Python-Markdown is explicitly NOT a sanitizer: by default it passes block-level and inline raw HTML straight through unescaped, and it does not filter javascript: hrefs. The code comment (lines 40-42) rationalizes the reasoning as 'trusted', but reasoning text originates from an LLM (prompt-injectable) and from news scraping (attacker-controlled headlines). The reasoning_html for every proposal is injected into the initial server-rendered document (inside display:none modals that are always present in the DOM), so an <img src=x onerror=...> or <script> payload executes on page load without any click.

- **Failure scenario:** A news headline / LLM output feeds a proposal reasoning of `<img src=x onerror="fetch('/proposals/'+PENDING_ID+'/approve',{method:'POST'})">`. When the operator opens http://127.0.0.1:7424/, the browser tries to load the broken image, fires onerror, and same-origin POSTs to the approve endpoint (no auth/CSRF), placing a live order automatically. Any operator viewing the dashboard is compromised.

- **Suggested fix:** Sanitize the rendered HTML (e.g. bleach.clean with an allowlist of tags/attrs and safe URL schemes) before marking it safe, or drop \| safe and render reasoning as escaped plain text. Enable Markdown's safe_mode/HTML-escaping and forbid javascript: URIs.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. web/app.py:45-56 builds a Python-Markdown converter (fenced_code/tables/sane_lists/nl2br/magiclink) with no sanitizer; Python-Markdown explicitly is not a sanitizer and passes raw block/inline HTML through unescaped (safe_mode was removed in 3.0). fetch_proposals stores that output as reasoning_html (app.py:171) and dashboard.html:268 emits it with `{{ p.reasoning_html \| safe }}`. reasoning is stored as a raw VARCHAR with zero sanitization (proposal_store.py:51,110). The modal wrapping it is always server-rendered into the DOM, only CSS-hidden (`.modal { display:none }`, dashboard.html:57), so an `<img src=x onerror=...>` still loads and fires onerror on page load — no click needed. The approve endpoint (app.py:222) is a same-origin POST with no CSRF token or auth, so the payload can auto-approve a pending proposal, placing a live order. Content originates from LLM output/news headlines. Critical: arbitrary JS in the operator's browser triggering unattended live-order approval on a real-money book.


## High bugs


### [x] HIGH — Live IB credentials (.env) are baked into the Docker image

- **Location:** `.dockerignore:1`  ·  _reviewer: ops_

- **Mechanism:** .dockerignore does not exclude '.env' (entries: .git, .cache, .venv, temp, scratch, data, logs, ...). Dockerfile line 59 runs 'COPY --chown=trader:trader ./ /home/trader/mmr/', so the repo-root .env — containing TWS_USERID, TWS_PASSWORD, VNC_SERVER_PASSWORD and IB_ACCOUNT for a live login that also manages a 32M master account — is copied into an image layer at /home/trader/mmr/.env on every build. Anyone with access to the Docker daemon, image cache, registry push, or a 'docker save' tarball can extract the credentials; they persist in layer history even if later deleted. Compounding: docker.sh writes .env via 'cat >' with no chmod (current mode 0644, world-readable) — there is no chmod anywhere in docker.sh.

- **Failure scenario:** The image is pushed to any registry, exported for debugging, or the laptop's Docker VM is shared/backed up. 'docker run --rm mmr-mmr cat /home/trader/mmr/.env' (or extracting the layer tar) yields the live IBKR username/password with full trading permission (READ_ONLY_API defaults to 'no'), giving an attacker order-placement access to the live account and visibility into the master account.

- **Suggested fix:** Add '.env' (and '*.env', 'secrets.env') to .dockerignore; chmod 600 .env when docker.sh writes it. Credentials are only needed by the ib-gateway container via env_file, never inside the mmr image.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. .dockerignore (repo root, full contents) has no .env entry; .gitignore ignoring .env does not affect the Docker build context. Dockerfile:59 `COPY --chown=trader:trader ./ /home/trader/mmr/` with docker-compose.yml:49 `context: .` (repo root, where /Users/joelpob/dev/mmr/.env exists at mode 0644) bakes .env into an image layer at /home/trader/mmr/.env. The file contains TWS_USERID, TWS_PASSWORD, IB_ACCOUNT, VNC_SERVER_PASSWORD, and READ_ONLY_API=no (full trading). docker.sh:470 writes it via `cat >` with no chmod anywhere (grep confirms none), so it stays world-readable. Anyone with Docker daemon/registry/image-tarball access can `docker run mmr cat /home/trader/mmr/.env`. High, not critical: exploitation requires image/daemon access rather than remote reach, but for this live-money system the leaked credentials grant live order placement plus master-account visibility.


### [x] HIGH — Position monitor swallows all price-fetch failures — stop-loss alerting silently disables during data outages, and tracked state is memory-only

- **Location:** `skills/mmr-loop-skill/scripts/loop_engine.py:416`  ·  _reviewer: llm-loop_

- **Mechanism:** _check_tracked_positions wraps the batch snapshot in 'except Exception:' falling back to per-symbol snapshots each wrapped in 'except Exception: pass'; a symbol with no resolvable price is then silently 'continue'-d (line 429). If IB market data is gated, the Gateway is down, or the exchange/currency hint is wrong (note the fallback also uses one global config exchange/currency for ALL tracked symbols, so mixed US+ASX tracking guarantees wrong hints for one side), the monitor produces zero alerts and zero errors — the LLM believes its stops are being watched. This directly violates the 'fail loudly' design principle for the one component whose whole job is loss protection. Compounding this, tracked_positions lives only in TradingLoop._state (class attribute, line 75): a process crash/restart erases every tracked stop with no persistence and no reconciliation against the broker portfolio, and these 'stops' are alert-only — no real STP order exists at IB.

- **Failure scenario:** LLM enters BHP LONG 350@50.15 with stop_pct=-1.5 and tracks it. Overnight the IB market-data farm breaks (snapshot times out → JSON error payload → price_map empty). BHP gaps down 6% at the ASX open. Every 180s the monitor runs, gets no prices, returns no alerts, and the hook goes back to sleep. The LLM is never told the stop was breached or that monitoring is blind; the position bleeds 4x past the configured stop.

- **Suggested fix:** When any tracked symbol fails to price for N consecutive monitor passes, inject a loud '[Position Monitor] BLIND: cannot price BHP for 9 min — stop-loss monitoring is NOT active' alert. Persist tracked_positions to disk (or derive them from the actual portfolio each pass), and prefer placing real protective STP orders via place_standalone_order instead of alert-only stops.

- **Verifier:** Every claim traces in code. loop_engine.py:407 wraps the batch snapshot in `except Exception:` and loop_engine.py:415 wraps per-symbol fallback in `except Exception: pass`; any symbol absent from price_map hits `if last_price is None: continue` (line 428-429), producing no alert and no error. exchange/currency are single global config values (lines 394-395) applied to ALL symbols in both the batch and fallback calls, so mixed US+ASX tracking guarantees a wrong hint for one side. tracked_positions is a class-attribute dict (line 75) with no disk persistence and no portfolio reconciliation — grep shows the only writes are track/untrack; a restart erases all stops. The monitor only returns alert strings (lines 441-452); no real STP order is placed. SKILL.md:104 promises the LLM "is alerted" at stops and that "monitoring happens silently," so a blind data outage silently voids the one loss-protection component — a direct "fail loudly" violation. Severity high: for a low-frequency live-money system, silent failure of the stop-watcher risks uncapped drawdown.


### [x] HIGH — approve()/buy()/sell() timeout kills the CLI mid-order, leaving a possibly-live order the LLM is told never happened

- **Location:** `skills/mmr-skill/scripts/mmr_helpers.py:3006`  ·  _reviewer: llm-loop_

- **Mechanism:** MMRHelpers.approve(), buy(), and sell() all run through _run_cli(..., timeout=30), which uses subprocess.run(timeout=30) and on expiry returns the string 'ERROR: Command timed out after 30s — trader_service may be unresponsive (check IB Gateway connectivity)'. Killing the CLI subprocess does NOT cancel the work: the ZMQ RPC has typically already been dispatched to trader_service, which places the order regardless of client death (and subprocess.run only kills the direct 'uv' child, not necessarily the python grandchild). Worse, sdk.approve() (trader/sdk.py:1364) marks the proposal APPROVED before resolving the contract, and for amount-based proposals (the loop's default — auto-sizing stores an amount, not a quantity) it then issues a get_snapshot RPC that the codebase itself documents as taking up to 30s when market data is gated, plus ~1-2s Python startup — so the helper's 30s budget is routinely smaller than approve's own legitimate execution path. After a timeout: (a) the proposal is stuck in APPROVED (re-approve returns 'is APPROVED, not PENDING' — a dead end), (b) order_ids were never recorded, (c) the returned error text affirmatively blames connectivity, and (d) SKILL.md instructs 'create a new proposal rather than try to re-approve'.

- **Failure scenario:** The trading loop proposes AAPL BUY auto-sized to $10,000 (amount-based). The LLM calls MMRHelpers.approve(42). The CLI subprocess spends 2s starting, 3s resolving, 24s on the snapshot RPC (slow market data), then sends place_expressive_order — at t=30s subprocess.run kills the uv process. trader_service completes the market buy. The helper returns 'ERROR: Command timed out... trader_service may be unresponsive'. Proposal 42 is APPROVED with no order_ids; re-approve is refused; following the documented recovery the LLM creates and approves proposal 43 for the same trade → two $10k live AAPL positions, only one of which the LLM knows about.

- **Suggested fix:** For order-mutating helpers (approve/buy/sell/cancel), raise the subprocess timeout well above the worst-case internal RPC chain (e.g. 90s), and change the timeout message to state explicitly that the order MAY have been placed and that orders()/trades()/proposal_show() must be checked before any retry or replacement proposal. In sdk.approve, record the intent (e.g. metadata 'order_submitted') before the place RPC so a limbo APPROVED proposal is distinguishable from one that never reached the broker.

- **Verifier:** Traceable end-to-end. approve/buy/sell run via _run_cli(timeout=30) (mmr_helpers.py:3006,885,931); on subprocess timeout it returns a message that affirmatively blames connectivity (mmr_helpers.py:37-39). sdk.approve marks the proposal APPROVED (sdk.py:1364) BEFORE resolving, snapshotting, and placing (place at :1402). Auto-sizing stores amount not quantity (sdk.py:1160-1176), so approve takes the get_snapshot RPC branch (:1374-1377), which is documented to cap at 30s when market data is gated (mmr_helpers.py:714-716) plus ~1-2s startup — the legit path can exceed the 30s budget. Killing the CLI cannot cancel an already-dispatched ZMQ place_expressive_order. Result: proposal stuck APPROVED (re-approve refused, sdk.py:1360-1361; SKILL.md:237 says create a new proposal), no order_ids, misleading message. The double-live-position outcome is real but requires a narrow timing window (place RPC sent just before the kill, server completes it); the common case is a benign limbo/detour, so high rather than critical.


### [x] HIGH — write_resolve_overlap uses keep='first' so stored bars can never be corrected by re-downloads (stale/partial data wins forever)

- **Location:** `trader/data/data_access.py:513`  ·  _reviewer: stores_

- **Mechanism:** `write_resolve_overlap` concatenates `[existing_data, data_frame]` and drops duplicated index rows with `keep='first'`, so for any timestamp that already exists in the DB the OLD row wins and the freshly downloaded row is discarded. The merged frame is then written via DuckDBDataStore.write(), whose DELETE-then-INSERT re-persists the old values. This makes every re-download of an overlapping range a silent no-op for existing timestamps — including `data refresh` jobs with `force: true`, whose entire purpose is to refetch and replace the window.

- **Failure scenario:** A midday `data download AAPL --bar-size '1 day'` (CLI path mmr_cli.py:7448) stores today's PARTIAL daily bar (close = midday price, half the volume). The evening cron refetches the completed bar, but keep='first' discards it and re-persists the partial bar permanently. Similarly, after a stock split, re-downloaded split-adjusted history is discarded for all overlapping dates, leaving a mixed adjusted/unadjusted series. Backtests and live strategies then compute indicators on wrong closes/volumes — violating the project's own 'wrong data is worse than no data' principle.

- **Suggested fix:** Prefer fresh data: use `pd.concat([data_frame, existing_data])` with keep='first' (or keep='last' with current order), so newly fetched rows overwrite stored rows for overlapping timestamps.

- **Verifier:** Mechanism confirmed. data_access.py:512-513 does `pd.concat([existing_data, data_frame])` then `~temp_df.index.duplicated(keep='first')`, so for any duplicated timestamp the existing (old) row wins and the fresh row is discarded. I reproduced this with pandas: existing close=100/vol=500 survives, corrected close=110/vol=999 is dropped. The merged (stale) frame is then persisted by duckdb_store.py:265-288 via DELETE-then-INSERT, re-writing the old values. The CLI download path uses this write (mmr_cli.py:7448), and `--force`/`force:true` (mmr_cli.py:7381, 7683) deliberately refetches the full overlapping window — its stated purpose (comment 7378-7379) is to re-fetch existing days, yet keep='first' makes that a silent no-op for existing timestamps. Split-adjusted re-downloads and completed-vs-partial bars thus can't overwrite stored data, feeding wrong closes/volumes into backtests and live indicators. Severity high (data integrity, silent, permanent) but frequency-limited: normal incremental cron uses tick_data.missing() (7385) to skip covered ranges, so overlap only arises on force/manual re-downloads; test_data_access.py:255 even encodes the keep='first' outcome.


### [x] HIGH — write_resolve_overlap keeps stale existing bars over freshly downloaded data (keep='first')

- **Location:** `trader/data/data_access.py:513`  ·  _reviewer: data-access_

- **Mechanism:** write_resolve_overlap concatenates [existing_data, data_frame] and dedups with index.duplicated(keep='first'), so for any timestamp already in the store the OLD row wins and the newly downloaded row is silently discarded. Every path in the data-refresh loop (mmr_cli.py:7448) writes through this method. Consequence 1: an intraday `mmr data refresh` (window end = dt.datetime.now(), mmr_cli.py:7328) stores today's PARTIAL daily bar; any later refetch of that day is thrown away, freezing the wrong close/high/low/volume forever. Consequence 2: ib_history_worker injects NaN placeholder rows for days where a chunk returned no data (ib_history_worker.py:312-331) — e.g. during an IB outage — and those NaN bars permanently block the real bars from a retry. Consequence 3: the `--force` flag, whose comment says it exists to re-fetch existing days (mmr_cli.py:7378), is a silent no-op for any already-stored timestamp. Verified empirically: existing close=100 survives, corrected close=110 is dropped, including across mixed dateutil/pytz tz representations of the same instant.

- **Failure scenario:** User runs `mmr data refresh us_top20_daily` at 2pm; AAPL's daily bar for today is stored with the 2pm partial close. The nightly cron re-runs after the close; missing() reports today covered (or --force refetches but keep='first' discards the corrected bar). The partial bar is permanent. A daily strategy / backtest / ATR-based position sizer computes signals off a close that is wrong by the entire afternoon move — wrong trade sizes and entries on the live account.

- **Suggested fix:** Use keep='last' so incoming data wins (existing rows only fill timestamps the download didn't cover), or simply rely on DuckDBDataStore.write's range-DELETE upsert and drop the merge entirely for the ranges being written.

- **Verifier:** Code-level defect verified end-to-end. data_access.py:512-513 concats [existing, incoming] then dedups with keep='first', so for any already-stored timestamp the OLD row wins and fresh data is silently dropped. Verified empirically (100 survives, 110 discarded) including across mixed dateutil/pytz reps of the same UTC instant. The refresh loop writes through this at mmr_cli.py:7448, and --force (mmr_cli.py:7381) only bypasses the missing() guard — it still calls write_resolve_overlap, so corrections to existing timestamps are a no-op. Consequence 2 is purely code and clearly reachable: ib_history_worker.py:312-331 injects NaN placeholder rows for no-data days; keep='first' then permanently blocks real bars on retry. The existing test even pins this behavior (test_data_access.py:255 asserts the stale close is kept). High severity is right: frozen/partial closes feed daily signals and ATR position sizing on a live account — a data-integrity failure, exactly the 'wrong data is worse than no data' hazard. Fix: keep='last'.


### [x] HIGH — TickData.missing() cannot detect interior gaps: resample('D').first() marks every day between min and max as present

- **Location:** `trader/data/data_access.py:621`  ·  _reviewer: data-access_

- **Mechanism:** missing() builds the set of covered dates via `df.resample('D').first().index.date`. Pandas resample generates a bin for EVERY calendar day between the first and last stored bar (empty bins become NaN rows but still appear in the index) — verified empirically: with bars on Jan 2, 3, 5, 8, the missing session Jan 4 appears in the covered-dates list. So `d not in dates` is only ever true for sessions before the first stored bar or after the last one; interior holes are invisible. Additionally, NaN placeholder rows (injected by ib_history_worker for no-data days) count as coverage. missing() is the sole freshness/gap guard for: strategy_service warm-up backfill (strategy_runtime.py:550), the cron data-refresh loop (mmr_cli.py:7385), data_service downloads (data_service.py:263/339/413), and ib_history_batch.

- **Failure scenario:** A week of AAPL 1-min bars failed to download mid-history (IB outage). Every subsequent `mmr data refresh` and every strategy_service restart calls missing(), which reports zero gaps because bars exist before and after the hole. The strategy warms up and trades on a rolling window whose indicators (EMA/ATR) silently span a 5-session hole — signals and position sizes computed from wrong data, with no error ever surfaced (violates fail-loudly).

- **Suggested fix:** Drop all-NaN rows, then compare the set of dates that actually have bars (e.g. df.dropna(subset=['close']).index.normalize().unique()) against calendar sessions instead of the resampled index.

- **Verifier:** Verified empirically: with bars on Jan 2/3/5/8, `df.resample('D').first().index.date` (data_access.py:621) yields every calendar day Jan 2-8 including the missing Jan 4. The gap loop at data_access.py:632-633 only flags a session when `d not in dates`, so it detects gaps solely before the first or after the last stored bar; interior holes are never seen. `missing()` is the sole gap guard across data_service.py:263/339/413, mmr_cli.py:7385, ib_history_batch.py:83, market_data.py:214, and strategy_runtime.py:550. In strategy_runtime.py:566-571 an empty return is treated as "cache hit — skipping IB fetch," so an interior hole is never backfilled and the strategy warms up / sizes positions on discontinuous data with no error surfaced (fail-loudly violation). Severity high: silent wrong data into live indicators/sizing, though it requires a pre-existing interior download failure.


### [x] HIGH — update_status silently accepts same-state transitions, enabling concurrent double-approval and duplicate live orders

- **Location:** `trader/data/proposal_store.py:177`  ·  _reviewer: stores_

- **Mechanism:** In `_update`, `if current == status: return` makes a same-state 'transition' a silent success instead of an error — directly contradicting the docstring five lines above ('Idempotent updates to the same terminal state are rejected too'). The caller `TraderSDK.approve()` (trader/sdk.py:1352-1420) relies on `update_status(id, 'APPROVED')` raising `InvalidProposalTransition` as its only atomic guard against concurrent approval: its `p.status != 'PENDING'` pre-check at line 1360 is a non-atomic read outside the DB lock. If two approvers both read PENDING, the first transitions PENDING→APPROVED; the second's `update_status(id, 'APPROVED')` hits `current == status` and returns with no exception, so the second caller also proceeds to `place_expressive_order` and places the trade a second time. Both then mark EXECUTED (the second again via the silent same-state path).

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM agent loop and a human (or a double-submitted CLI/RPC call) both run `approve 42` within the get→update_status window while proposal 42 is PENDING. Approver A transitions to APPROVED and places a $10k market BUY; approver B's update_status silently no-ops, B also places the same $10k market BUY. The live account U26774889 ends up with double the intended position, with no error surfaced anywhere.

- **Suggested fix:** Make same-state updates raise InvalidProposalTransition (as the docstring claims), or have update_status return whether it actually performed the transition and make approve() abort unless it won the PENDING→APPROVED compare-and-swap.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. proposal_store.py:177 `if current == status: return` silently no-ops; removing it would route APPROVED→APPROVED into the raise at 181-183 (APPROVED's allowed set = {EXECUTED,FAILED,REJECTED}). sdk.py:1357-1364 does a non-atomic get()+status-check then a separate update_status('APPROVED'). Two concurrent `approve 42` both read PENDING, pass the 1360 check; DuckDB serializes the writes, A does PENDING→APPROVED, B's update_status sees current==status and returns without raising, so B falls into the try (1366) and calls place_expressive_order (1402) again — a duplicate live order with no error. Line 1364 is outside the try, so a raise would abort B, confirming the fix is sound. tests/test_proposal_store.py:154-165 encodes the no-op as intended, and the docstring (156) is contradicted. High: low likelihood (tight race window) but severe impact — undetected duplicate order on live account.


### [x] HIGH — pull_ib connects IB on one event loop then drives requests on another — every request times out and fabricates data

- **Location:** `trader/data_service.py:201`  ·  _reviewer: history-workers_

- **Mechanism:** _ib_work runs in asyncio.to_thread. `with IBHistoryWorker(...)` calls the sync connect(), which goes through ib_async util.run/getLoop: in a non-main thread this creates a fresh event loop L1, runs connectAsync to completion on it, and stops L1. The socket transport/protocol stay bound to L1. Then `asyncio.run(worker.get_contract_history(...))` creates a second loop L2. Inside, `self.connected` is True so no reconnect happens; reqHistoricalDataAsync creates its future on L2 and the request bytes go out via the optimistic direct socket send, but the reply can only be dispatched by L1 — which never runs again. ib_async's reqHistoricalDataAsync (timeout=60) catches the TimeoutError, logs a warning, and returns an EMPTY BarDataList with no exception and no error callback (self.error_code stays 0). get_contract_history then takes its empty-result branch and injects all-NaN 'null rows' for every day, one 60-second timeout per day-step, and returns a frame of pure NaN rows. _download_ib_one sees len(df)>0, writes the NaN rows to DuckDB, and returns {'ok': True, 'rows': N} — counted as completed.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr history ib --universe asx --bar_size '1 day' --prev_days 5` via data_service: each security burns ~6x60s of timeouts, then writes 6 all-NaN daily bars per conid into tick_data and reports success. missing() subsequently sees those dates as covered, so the range is never re-fetched; backtests, the sweep freshness guard, and `data status` all see rows that contain no prices.

- **Suggested fix:** Do all IB work on a single loop: make _ib_work create one event loop per thread and run connect_async + get_contract_history inside the same `asyncio.run` (drop the sync __enter__/connect), or run the worker on the service's main loop since get_contract_history is already async.

- **Verifier:** The cross-loop bug is real. `_ib_work` runs in `asyncio.to_thread` (data_service.py:210). `IBHistoryWorker.__enter__`→`connect()` (ib_history_worker.py:74,102) drives IB's sync `IB.connect`→`util.run`→`getLoop()`, which in a non-main thread creates and sets a NEW loop L1 (util.py:512-516) and binds the socket transport to it (connection.py:37-38). Then `asyncio.run(get_contract_history)` (data_service.py:201) creates loop L2; `self.connected` is True so no reconnect, and `reqHistoricalDataAsync` creates its future on L2 while L1 (the only loop reading the socket) never runs again. After the 60s timeout, ib_async clears bars and returns an EMPTY BarDataList with no exception and error_code=0 (ib.py:2369-2374). `get_contract_history` then takes the `else` branch and injects all-NaN null rows (ib_history_worker.py:304-331). `_download_ib_one` writes them (duckdb_store.py doesn't drop NaN OHLCV) and returns `ok:True`. Live path: mmr_cli.py:8008→sdk→RPC→pull_ib; no test covers it. Severity high not critical: confined to international IB history (US uses Massive/twelvedata), writes NaN (not fake prices, which the backtester drops), but silently poisons `missing()`/freshness coverage.


### [x] HIGH — Empty/timed-out IB responses are converted into persisted NaN bars that permanently mark days as covered

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ib_history_worker.py:312`  ·  _reviewer: history-workers_

- **Mechanism:** When reqHistoricalDataAsync returns nothing (which includes the silent 60s-timeout path in ib_async — no exception, no error callback, error_code stays 0), get_contract_history cannot distinguish 'market closed / no trades' from 'request failed'. It injects NaN null rows for every calendar day in the chunk (lines 304-331) and returns them; callers (data_service._download_ib_one, mmr_cli write path) persist them to DuckDB and count the symbol as completed. Because TickData.missing() treats any stored row on a date as coverage, a transient IB stall (pacing violation, HMDS farm hiccup, gateway restart) permanently poisons that date range with price-less bars that are never re-downloaded. Additionally, a real error can be masked before the check at line 253: __handle_error clears the shared error_code whenever a benign info code (2104/2106/2158) arrives after a genuine 162, so the failure is re-classified as 'no data' and the same NaN fabrication runs.

- **Failure scenario:** IB pacing delays a 1-day ASX history reply past 60s. ib_async returns empty bars silently; the worker writes a NaN bar for that session; `mmr data status` and the sweep freshness guard see the row and report the symbol fresh; missing() never re-fetches it; a backtest on that conid silently drops the NaN bar and computes indicators across a hole it doesn't know exists.

- **Suggested fix:** Raise (or at least skip persisting) when a request produces no bars and no explicit IB 'no data' error — pass a nonzero timeout awareness through (ib_async re-raisable timeout or check `bars is empty and error_code == 0` as failure). Only write null-marker rows for dates confirmed as non-sessions via the exchange calendar. Make error state per-request rather than a shared mutable field cleared by unrelated info codes.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. Installed ib_async reqHistoricalDataAsync catches asyncio.TimeoutError, logs a warning, bars.clear(), returns empty — no exception, no error callback, so IBHistoryWorker.error_code stays 0. At ib_history_worker.py:253 the error branch is skipped; :276 `if result:` is False → else (:304-307) then :312-331 fabricate NaN rows for the chunk's calendar days. data_service.py:212-213 writes whenever len(df)>0 and returns ok=True with no NaN filtering. data_access.py:621 missing() marks a session covered if ANY row exists on that date (resample('D').first()), NaN or not, so the range is never re-fetched. A transient IB stall permanently poisons those sessions with price-less bars the backtester silently drops. Cannot refute. High for a capital-safety-weighted system: silent, self-perpetuating data corruption feeding strategy/backtest inputs on the IB/international path; frequency-limited (needs a timeout; US uses Massive), which slightly softens it.


### [x] HIGH — @rpcmethod marker never enforced and dotted-path getattr traversal exposes the entire object graph, bypassing the proposal-approval order gate

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:474`  ·  _reviewer: messaging_

- **Mechanism:** RPCServer._handle_request dispatches by walking `for part in method_name.split('.'): obj = getattr(obj, part)` and calling the result. The `_is_rpc_method` attribute set by the rpcmethod decorator (line 184) is never read anywhere in the codebase, so the decorator is purely decorative. Any client can therefore invoke any attribute path on the API instance: `trader.place_order_simple(...)` reaches the Trader method directly and skips the require_proposal_approval gate that exists only in TraderServiceApi.place_order_simple (trader_service_api.py:84); `trader.client.ib.reqGlobalCancel()`, `trader.risk_gate.limits.__setattr__(...)`, `trader.cancel_all()` etc. are all reachable. Combined with the default-on dill ExtType fallback for arguments, the unauthenticated localhost socket is effectively a full remote control of the live-account Trader object, and the documented 'hard' order gates are advisory.

- **Failure scenario:** require_proposal_approval=true is set to force all trades through propose→approve. A misbehaving LLM loop (or any local process/script) calls client.rpc().trader.place_order_simple(contract, 'BUY', ...) — the getattr chain resolves TraderServiceApi.trader → Trader.place_order_simple and places a live order with no proposal, no review, and skip_risk_gate semantics chosen by the caller.

- **Suggested fix:** In _handle_request, resolve only single-segment method names on the API instance and require getattr(method, '_is_rpc_method', False); return an error response for anything else.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. clientserver.py:474-477 dispatches via dotted getattr traversal and calls the result with no marker check. `_is_rpc_method` (set at :184) is read nowhere (grep confirms only the definition line), so @rpcmethod is decorative. The served instance is TraderServiceApi(self) with self=live Trader (trading_runtime.py:243-245); TraderServiceApi.trader exposes the whole Trader (trader_service_api.py:28). The approval gate exists ONLY in the wrapper (trader_service_api.py:84). A request with method="trader.place_order_simple" resolves instance.trader→Trader.place_order_simple (exists, :118) and executes it, bypassing require_proposal_approval and letting the caller choose skip_risk_gate; trader.cancel_all/risk_gate.limits are also reachable. Mitigation: socket binds 127.0.0.1 only (:436), so attacker must be same-host/container — but that is exactly the LLM-loop actor the gate is meant to constrain. In a live-money system this defeats a documented capital-safety control; high stands.


### [x] HIGH — RPC client never matches responses to req_id — after a timeout, the next call returns the previous call's stale reply

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:397`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** _SyncMethodCall.__call__ generates a req_id and sends it, but on receive it takes frames[-1] from the DEALER socket and returns response['result'] without checking response['req_id']. If a call raises TimeoutError (line 396), the server's late reply stays queued on the socket (it is never drained). The next RPC call sends a new request and then recv's the FIRST queued message — the stale reply to the timed-out call — and returns it as the result of the new call. Every subsequent call is off-by-one. strategy_runtime uses this exact client for resolve_symbol during reconcile/startup, and 'RPC timed out mid-operation' is precisely the trader_service-restarting scenario that the reconcile loop is designed to ride through.

- **Failure scenario:** During a reconcile while trader_service is slow, resolve_symbol(conId_A) times out; the reply arrives 2s later. The next tick's resolve_symbol(conId_B) returns conId_A's SecurityDefinition list; subscribe() then registers strategy-for-B against contract A and publishes A's ticker stream to it — the strategy silently computes signals on the wrong instrument (direct 'precision over convenience' violation). The same desync affects every RPC consumer, including the CLI approve path.

- **Suggested fix:** Loop on recv until response['req_id'] == req_id (discarding stale replies), or drain the socket after a timeout before releasing the lock.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed at code level. clientserver.py:372 mints req_id and :381 sends it, but :397-398 returns frames[-1]/response['result'] with no req_id check (:407 is unconditional). On timeout (:396) the request was already sent and the socket is never drained; the DEALER socket is long-lived and reused (:528, :535). strategy_runtime.py:481-482 swallows TimeoutError without reconnecting, so a late resolve_symbol reply stays buffered and desyncs the next call — subscribe() (:477) then binds a strategy to the wrong contract. Same client backs the approve path. No test covers the timeout-then-next-call path. Severity high for a capital-safety system: silent wrong-instrument trading, and the trigger (RPC timeout) is exactly the trader_service-restart case reconcile is meant to survive. It is intermittent/state-dependent, not deterministic, so not critical.


### [x] HIGH — RPC client never checks response req_id, so a timed-out call poisons every subsequent call on the socket with stale responses

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:397`  ·  _reviewer: architecture_

- **Mechanism:** _SyncMethodCall.__call__ generates a req_id and the server echoes it back, but the client never compares it: after polling, it does recv_multipart() and unconditionally treats frames[-1] as the reply to the current call. If a call raises TimeoutError (line 396), the server's late reply remains queued on the shared DEALER socket. The next RPC call on the same client (the SDK/CLI reuses one RPCClient for all commands, and trader_service's zmq_strategy_client does too) polls, sees POLLIN immediately, and consumes the previous call's response as its own result — every call thereafter is off-by-one. The req_id plumbing exists on both sides but validation was never wired up (classic half-migrated pattern).

- **Failure scenario:** LLM loop calls approve → place_expressive_order over RPC; IB is slow so the 30s client timeout fires and the proposal is marked FAILED. The delayed SuccessFail([trades]) response then sits in the socket. The next command on the same session (e.g. a second approve, or get_portfolio_summary) receives that stale SuccessFail as its own result — the second proposal is marked EXECUTED with the first proposal's order ids, or portfolio data is silently replaced by an unrelated object, and all subsequent calls stay desynchronized.

- **Suggested fix:** In _SyncMethodCall, loop on recv until response['req_id'] == req_id (discarding/logging stale replies), and drain the socket of stale frames before sending a new request. Add a test that times out one call and verifies the next call still gets its own result.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed. clientserver.py:397-398 takes frames[-1] as the reply and never checks response['req_id'] against the req_id sent (line 372/377), though the server echoes it (line 481). On timeout (line 396) the socket is not drained, so the server's late reply stays queued on the reused DEALER. Traced concretely: `mmr approve --all` (mmr_cli.py:2539) loops mmr.approve(); if #1's place_expressive_order times out (sdk.py:1402→1425, #1→FAILED), #2's next RPC consumes #1's stale SuccessFail → #2 marked EXECUTED with #1's order_ids (sdk.py:1419). Also hits the REPL (one reused RPCClient, mmr_cli.py:10001) and trader_service zmq_strategy_client (trading_runtime.py:262). One-shot single-call `mmr` invocations are immune (fresh socket per process, closed at exit), but the reused-socket paths are real. Severity high (critical defensible): capital-safety correctness — wrong proposals marked executed / portfolio data silently swapped — but gated on an RPC-timeout precondition, not every call.


### [ ] HIGH — Option (and equity) orders report success on the local placeOrder echo, never observing IB rejection

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/trader_service_api.py:105`  ·  _reviewer: probe-0:Options live-order path: contract constr_

- **Mechanism:** buy_option/sell_option -> place_order_simple. In subscribe_place_order (ibreactive.py:423-429) the returned Observable is `rx.of(trade_result).concat(live_stream)`, where trade_result is the Trade object returned synchronously by ib.placeOrder (status typically 'PendingSubmit'). The RPC wrapper's on_next (trader_service_api.py:103-106) sets result=SuccessFail.success on the FIRST emission and sets the event, so place_order_simple returns as soon as the local echo arrives — before IB accepts, rejects, or fills. Asynchronous IB rejections (error 201 margin, no options-trading permission, contract not tradeable, illiquid/halted) arrive later on the live stream after the function already returned success. This violates the fail-loudly principle.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr options buy AAPL -e 3m -s 250 -r C -q 5 --market` on an account without options permission (or a strike IB rejects for margin). ib.placeOrder returns a PendingSubmit Trade; on_next reports success with status 'PendingSubmit'; _print_trade_result prints 'BUY ...: success'. IB then cancels/rejects the order asynchronously. The user/LLM believes the option position was opened when no order is live.

- **Suggested fix:** Have on_next ignore transient statuses (PendingSubmit/PreSubmitted) and only resolve the SuccessFail on a terminal orderStatus (Filled/Submitted/Cancelled/Inactive) or an error event; propagate IB rejections as failure.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. buy_option/sell_option (sdk.py:2924,2971) call RPC place_order_simple, whose on_next resolves SuccessFail.success on the FIRST emission (trader_service_api.py:103-106). That first emission is trade_result = ib.placeOrder(...) returned synchronously in subscribe_place_order and replayed via rx.of(...).concat(xs) (ibreactive.py:423-429); its orderStatus is 'PendingSubmit'. rx.of emits synchronously at subscribe, so task.wait() returns immediately and the RPC reports success before IB accepts, rejects, or fills. Synchronous guards (account pinning executioner.py:81-92, risk gate, sanity check) do fail loud, but async IB rejections (error 201 margin, no options permission, un-tradeable contract) arrive later on the live stream after return. The user/LLM sees success with no live order — a genuine violation of the stated fail-loudly principle. High: it corrupts the LLM loop's state assessment for live-money decisions, though no capital is directly misdirected (under-reports failures rather than placing wrong orders).


### [x] HIGH — data download/refresh --source ib reuses one IBHistoryWorker across multiple asyncio.run calls — everything after the first fetch times out and writes NaN bars

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:7432`  ·  _reviewer: history-workers_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_data_download creates a single IBHistoryWorker before the symbol loop and calls `asyncio.run(worker.get_contract_history(...))` per missing range. The first call connects inside asyncio.run's loop L1 (connect_async sets worker.connected=True) and works; asyncio.run then CLOSES L1 on return, leaving the IB transport bound to a closed loop. Every subsequent asyncio.run creates a new loop, skips reconnect (connected=True, isConnected() still True), and each reqHistoricalDataAsync silently times out after 60s returning empty bars — which the worker converts to NaN null rows (see companion finding) that write_resolve_overlap persists and counts as rows written. _handle_data_refresh (the pycron data_refresh_asx job) delegates to this exact function, so the daily ASX refresh only genuinely refreshes the first stale symbol.

- **Failure scenario:** Monday cron run of `mmr data refresh asx_daily` with 20 ASX symbols each missing Friday's session: symbol 1 downloads correctly; symbols 2-20 each stall 60s then persist an all-NaN daily bar for Friday and report 'wrote N rows'. The job exits success; missing() considers Friday covered for all 20 symbols; ASX backtests and the freshness guard run on price-less bars.

- **Suggested fix:** Create one event loop for the whole download (loop.run_until_complete per range on the same loop), or reconnect the worker per asyncio.run call (worker.shutdown() + fresh connect inside the coroutine), and never persist frames whose OHLC columns are entirely NaN.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed mechanism. mmr_cli.py:7298 builds one IBHistoryWorker, then 7432 runs asyncio.run(worker.get_contract_history) per symbol/range. ib_async connection.py:38 binds the socket transport to the first loop via asyncio.get_running_loop()+create_connection; asyncio.run closes that loop. Worker.connected is reset only in shutdown()/connectivity codes (ib_history_worker.py:103,148,179), and IB.isConnected() (ib.py:410) returns a stale isReady() flag, so connect_async is skipped and the dead L1-bound transport is reused — responses land on the closed L1 selector, never reaching the new loop. Decisive corroboration: the only other two IB-history callers (data_service.py:196, ib_history_batch.py:141) deliberately create a fresh worker per asyncio.run inside a with-block to avoid exactly this. Refresh (7710-7724) funnels all job symbols through one _handle_data_download, so the ASX cron truly refreshes only the first symbol. Nuance: with IB.RequestTimeout=0 the likelier symptom is an indefinite hang on reqHistoricalDataAsync rather than a clean 60s empty→NaN write, but either outcome is a real data/freshness defect. Severity high not critical: it only affects the IB/international path (US uses twelvedata/massive) and degrades research data + fools the freshness guard, not the live-order path.


### [x] HIGH — `close --quantity` larger than the position flips it into an opposite-side position at market

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:2774`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_close computes `close_qty = args.quantity if args.quantity else abs(pos_size)` for the prompt, and sdk.close_position() (sdk.py:1462) uses `close_qty = abs(quantity)` with `action = 'SELL' if pos_size > 0 else 'BUY'`. Neither layer clamps the requested quantity to \|pos_size\|, so a 'close' can sell more shares than are held. The risk gate does not enforce reduce-only semantics for this path, and for shorts the same overshoot buys past flat into an unintended long.

- **Failure scenario:** Portfolio holds 80 NVDA. User types `close 3 --quantity 800` (fat-fingered extra zero), sees 'Close #3: NVDA (800 shares) at market? [y/N]', confirms without noticing. The CLI submits a market SELL for 800 — the account goes from +80 to -720 NVDA short on a live account, with margin and unlimited-downside exposure the user never intended.

- **Suggested fix:** In close_position, cap quantity at abs(pos_size) (`close_qty = min(abs(quantity), abs(pos_size))`) or fail loudly when the requested quantity exceeds the position, since a 'close' must never open the opposite side.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end with no clamp at any layer. CLI _handle_close (mmr_cli.py:2774) sets close_qty=args.quantity with no cap; --quantity is documented as a "partial close" (mmr_cli.py:510,514). SDK close_position (sdk.py:1462) uses abs(quantity) with action='SELL' if pos_size>0 else 'BUY' and submits a market order for the full requested qty — no clamp to abs(pos_size). risk_gate.evaluate (risk_gate.py:38-83) has no reduce-only logic; its only relevant guard is notional concentration (>10% of portfolio), which on the referenced 17k–32M accounts an oversized flip easily clears. So a "close" for more than the held quantity flips into an opposite-side (naked short / unlimited-downside) position at market. The confirmation prompt does echo the quantity, giving one chance to catch a fat-finger, but nothing enforces reduce-only semantics. High severity is justified for a live-money system where capital safety dominates.


### [x] HIGH — approve() floors quantity to 1 share, overriding the risk-computed dollar size by up to orders of magnitude

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1395`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** In approve(), when a proposal carries a dollar amount, quantity is computed as `qty = round(proposal.amount / price)` followed by `if qty < 1: qty = 1`. If the sized amount is smaller than half the share price, the computed quantity is 0 and the code silently promotes it to 1 full share. All position-sizing limits (min/max position, max_position_pct, exposure cap, ATR scaling) were applied to the *amount* at propose time; none are re-checked against the actual 1-share notional at execution time, and place_expressive_order is then called with that quantity.

- **Failure scenario:** Auto-sizer produces a $500 (min_position_usd) proposal for a high-priced stock, e.g. one trading at $4,000/share: round(500/4000)=0 -> qty forced to 1 -> a $4,000 market order is placed, 8x the risk-computed size and potentially above max_position_pct. For an extreme case like a ~$700k/share instrument, a $500 proposal becomes a $700k live order.

- **Suggested fix:** When round(amount/price) == 0, fail the proposal (mark FAILED with 'amount below one share price') instead of flooring to 1; or use floor() and require qty >= 1 naturally.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. sdk.py:1394-1396 computes qty=round(amount/price) then floors qty<1 to 1, so a $500 proposal on a $4,000 stock becomes a $4,000 order (8x). The claim that sizing limits aren't re-checked holds: trading_runtime.py:939-942 calls risk_gate.evaluate() without portfolio_value/position_value, so the max_position_pct concentration guard (risk_gate.py:61, gated on position_value>0) never fires. position_sizing.yaml:10 min_position_usd=$500 with no amount>=price check makes sub-one-share amounts reachable for any stock priced above the sized amount. Partial mitigation only: the whatIfOrder leverage check (trading_runtime.py:907-928) can block catastrophic margin blowouts but is best-effort (skipped if whatIfOrder throws, line 903) and misses moderate oversizing within margin. High for a live-money account; low frequency, real capital-safety impact, unguarded on the common path.


### [x] HIGH — ADV and ATR sizing inputs read the wrong database with the wrong key — volatility adjustment and liquidity cap are silently inert

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1135`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** propose()'s auto-sizing enrichment does `ds = DuckDBDataStore(cfg.get('duckdb_path'))` then `ds.read(symbol, start=start, bar_size='1 day')` with the raw ticker string. But OHLCV history is written to `history_duckdb_path` (mmr_history.duckdb per config_defaults/trader.yaml:46), and it is keyed by `str(conId)` (data_access.py:_to_symbol line 356-365; _handle_data_download resolves symbols to conId keys). So `hist` is empty on every call: liq.avg_daily_volume stays 0 and vol_info stays None. The ADV cap (max_adv_pct) and the ATR-inverse volatility multiplier — the headline safety features of the sizing pipeline per CLAUDE.md ('volatile stocks automatically get smaller positions') — never activate; the sizer just appends 'no volatility data' to the reasoning and sizes volatile and stable names identically.

- **Failure scenario:** LLM proposes a high-ATR small-cap (e.g. 8% ATR, thin volume). Intended size would be base x vol_scale_min (0.25x) and capped at 2% of ADV; instead it gets the full base x confidence size — up to 4x the intended dollar risk and possibly a large fraction of daily volume — because ds.read('XYZ', ...) against the trading DB returns an empty frame every time.

- **Suggested fix:** Read from history_duckdb_path (falling back to duckdb_path) and resolve the symbol to its conId key (as _handle_data_query does at mmr_cli.py:7160-7176) before reading; warn loudly in sizing_result when no history is found.

- **Verifier:** Both defects verified. sdk.py:1131-1135 reads OHLCV from `duckdb_path`, but bars live in the separate `history_duckdb_path` file (trader.yaml:45-46; canonical readers use history path, mmr_cli.py:7156/7257). And DuckDBDataStore.read filters `WHERE symbol = ?` exactly (duckdb_store.py:182) while bars are keyed by str(conId) (data_access.py:356-365; mmr_cli.py:7304-7306), yet sdk passes the raw ticker without conId resolution (contrast _handle_data_query at mmr_cli.py:7167-7176). So `hist` is always empty: avg_daily_volume stays 0 → ADV cap skipped (position_sizing.py:342); vol_info None → ATR scaler skipped, only 'no volatility data' appended (position_sizing.py:271-272). Both errors independently fatal even if paths coincided. High severity: the touted ATR/ADV safety features are inert on the live auto-sizing path, though propose→approve human review and the surfaced 'no volatility data' note partially mitigate.


### [x] HIGH — approve() treats an RPC timeout after order transmission as failure, marking the proposal terminally FAILED while the order may be live

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1425`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** approve() calls place_expressive_order and catches all exceptions (line 1425), including the TimeoutError that _SyncMethodCall raises after 30s even when the server has already transmitted the order to IB (place_expressive_order does a snapshot + multi-leg staging, plausibly >30s under IB lag). On timeout the proposal is set to FAILED -- a terminal, immutable state per the proposal state machine -- with no order_ids recorded and no reconciliation against the broker's open orders. The caller (LLM loop per CLAUDE.md workflow) sees a failure and will re-propose/re-approve, duplicating the position. Also, the status is set to APPROVED before execution (line 1364); a crash between APPROVED and placement leaves a proposal stuck in APPROVED that approve() refuses to touch (requires PENDING), with no recovery path.

- **Failure scenario:** LLM approves proposal #42 (BUY 500 AAPL bracket). IB Gateway is sluggish; the RPC times out at 30s but the bracket transmits seconds later. Proposal #42 is FAILED with no order_ids; the LLM, following the documented loop, creates and approves proposal #43 for the same thesis. The account ends up with 1000 shares and two brackets -- double the intended exposure.
