- **Suggested fix:** On TimeoutError specifically, do not transition to FAILED; query get_trades/get_orders to reconcile (match by algo tag/contract/quantity) before deciding, or introduce a PENDING_CONFIRMATION status. At minimum record the ambiguity in metadata and surface 'order state unknown -- do not retry blindly'.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. Default MMR timeout is 30s (sdk.py:147); the approve command uses it (mmr_cli.py:10094→2551). RPC raises TimeoutError on no reply (clientserver.py:396). Server-side place_expressive_order awaits each IB ack unbounded (trading_runtime.py:962) across margin whatIf + entry + TP + SL legs, with the SL leg transmit=True (line 1018) routing the bracket to market before the ack the server still awaits; the handler is not cancelled when the client times out, so the order stays live. approve()'s blanket except (sdk.py:1425) catches TimeoutError and sets FAILED — terminal (proposal_store.py:34) — with no order_ids and no broker reconciliation; nothing anywhere matches orderRef='proposal' back to a live order. The stuck-APPROVED sub-claim also holds: approve() requires PENDING (sdk.py:1360). No guard refutes this. The only uncertainty is whether IB latency exceeds 30s while live — plausible and entirely unguarded. High: mislabeled FAILED can drive the documented LLM loop to double real exposure.


### [x] HIGH — Resize re-creates stop-loss and take-profit as independent standalone orders, destroying the bracket's OCA linkage and parentId

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1660`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** Original protective orders are bracket children (parentId > 0), so IB's OCA semantics guarantee the SL is auto-cancelled when the TP fills and vice versa. execute_resize_plan re-creates each protective via place_standalone_order (trading_runtime.py:1157), which builds plain StopOrder/LimitOrder objects with no ocaGroup and no parentId. After a resize, a position with both an SL and a TP has two unlinked full-size closing orders. Additionally, the re-created TP no longer satisfies the plan's own protective-order detection (is_tp at line 1556 requires parentId > 0), so a second resize will neither cancel nor resize it, leaving a stale-quantity SELL LMT live against a smaller position.

- **Failure scenario:** Long 100 XYZ with bracket TP LMT SELL 100 @ 120 / SL STP SELL 100 @ 90. Resize to 50 shares: standalone TP SELL 50 @ 120 and STP SELL 50 @ 90 are placed, unlinked. Price rallies, TP fills (position now 0); the STP SELL 50 remains live. Weeks later price falls through 90 and the GTC stop executes: account is short 50 XYZ that nobody intended.

- **Suggested fix:** Set a shared ocaGroup on the re-created SL/TP pair (place_standalone_order should accept oca_group), or re-create as a proper attached bracket. Also broaden protective detection to catch standalone LMT closers created by a prior resize.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. place_standalone_order (trading_runtime.py:1174-1207) builds plain StopOrder/LimitOrder with no parentId and no ocaGroup. execute_resize_plan (sdk.py:1652-1670) cancels the original bracket children (sdk.py:1602) and re-creates each protective independently via that method, so the SL/TP pair loses its linkage — after a resize a position with both an SL and TP has two unlinked full-size closers; one filling leaves the other live (the naked-stop / over-sell scenario). The original legs were canonical bracket children (trading_runtime.py:990-1022, same shape as ib_async.IB.bracketOrder) which TWS auto-OCAs, so this is a genuine loss of safety. Independently of broker OCA behavior, sdk.py:1556 requires parentId>0 to classify an LMT as a take-profit, so the re-created parentId=0 LMT is invisible to a second resize and stays at a stale quantity against a smaller position — a concrete over-sell path. High severity is appropriate for a capital-safety-first system.


### [x] HIGH — to_market() discards the cancel result and immediately re-places a market order, risking double execution

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:793`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** to_market() reads a stale get_trades snapshot, then calls self.cancel(order_id) and throws away the returned SuccessFail (line 793). It does not verify the cancel succeeded nor wait for a Cancelled status (IB cancellation is asynchronous; server-side cancel_order just issues the request). It then unconditionally places a new market order for the full quantity via place_expressive_order. If the original limit order fills in the window between the get_trades snapshot and the cancel (exactly the near-the-money limits users convert to market), or the cancel is rejected, both orders execute.

- **Failure scenario:** Open BUY LMT 200 AMD @ 164.90 with market at 164.95. User runs to_market(order_id). While the RPC round-trips, the limit fills. The cancel returns 'cannot cancel filled order' (ignored), and the new MKT BUY 200 is placed and fills: 400 shares bought, double the intended position, with no warning to the user.

- **Suggested fix:** Check the cancel SuccessFail and abort on failure; then poll get_trades until the order shows Cancelled (accounting for partial fills, reducing the re-placed quantity by filled amount) before submitting the market order.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. In trader/sdk.py:to_market, quantity=order.totalQuantity (line 779, the full original amount, never reduced by filled shares); cancel(order_id)'s SuccessFail return is discarded (line 793) with no status/poll check; a full-quantity MARKET order is then placed unconditionally (lines 802-810). executioner.py:173-183 shows cancel is async (ib.cancelOrder) and returns None→SuccessFail.fail() when uncancelable, which to_market ignores. Two concrete paths: (1) deterministic over-buy on any partially-filled limit (50/100 filled → cancels 50, places MKT 100 → +50 excess); (2) the race where the limit fully fills before the cancel lands, producing a doubled position. Tests (test_sdk.py:463-537) only cover the happy path and never a failed cancel or partial fill, so nothing guards it. For a live-money system, silent over-positioning is a capital-safety defect; high severity stands despite low frequency.


### [x] HIGH — approve() computes quantity as amount/price with no currency conversion and force-bumps qty to 1

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1394`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** When a proposal has amount but no quantity, approve() computes qty = round(proposal.amount / price) where price comes from an IB ticker snapshot, which is always denominated in the contract's currency. Auto-sized amounts are produced by PositionSizer as amount_usd (base-currency dollars, derived from NetLiquidation). For non-USD instruments -- which the pipeline explicitly supports (propose BHP BUY --exchange ASX --currency AUD per CLAUDE.md) -- this divides USD by an AUD/JPY/HKD price with no FX conversion, systematically mis-sizing the order (~1.5x oversized for AUD at 0.65, ~150x undersized for JPY). Separately, `if qty < 1: qty = 1` (line 1396) silently overrides the sizing engine: any amount smaller than one share's price still buys a full share.

- **Failure scenario:** PositionSizer allocates $10,000 USD to BHP (ASX, trading at A$45). qty = round(10000/45) = 222 shares = A$9,990 which is roughly $6,500 more USD exposure than... inverted: 222 shares cost A$9,990 = ~$6,500 USD when $10,000 was intended if base is AUD, or ~1.5x oversized in the opposite base configuration -- either way the executed notional differs ~50% from the risk-sized amount. Or: a $250 auto-sized proposal on a $3,400 stock rounds to 0, gets bumped to 1, and a $3,400 order (13.6x the sized amount) executes.

- **Suggested fix:** Convert amount into the contract currency using get_account_cash_by_currency exchange rates (or an FX snapshot) before dividing; replace the qty<1 bump with a FAILED transition ('amount below one share').

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. propose() auto-sizes and stores amount = result.amount_usd (sdk.py:1160), a USD/base-currency figure from net_liquidation (position_sizing.py:243, sdk.py:839 NetLiquidation). approve() computes qty = round(proposal.amount / price) (sdk.py:1394) where price is an IB snapshot in the contract currency, with zero FX conversion — so a proposal with exchange=ASX/currency=AUD (documented supported path) divides USD by AUD, mis-sizing. Separately, `if qty < 1: qty = 1` (sdk.py:1395-1396) is reachable for any amount-only proposal (auto-sized proposals have quantity=None; also `--amount 100`) on a stock priced above the amount, forcing a full-share order and overriding the sizer. The reported FX arithmetic is internally muddled but the defect is genuine. High severity for a capital-safety-first live system, tempered only by the narrower triggers (non-USD instruments / above-amount share prices).


### [x] HIGH — approve() marks proposal FAILED on RPC timeout while trader_service continues placing the order — duplicate/orphan live orders

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1403`  ·  _reviewer: architecture_

- **Mechanism:** approve() calls place_expressive_order over ZMQ RPC with the SDK's default 30s timeout, and any exception (including TimeoutError) lands in the except at line 1425-1427 which sets the proposal to FAILED (a terminal, immutable state). But the server-side coroutine is not cancelled by a client timeout: place_expressive_order does whatIfOrderAsync plus up to three _place_and_wait calls, each of which is `await event.wait()` with NO timeout (trading_runtime.py:962). Under IB slowness the server can complete seconds or minutes later and transmit real orders. There is no idempotency key linking the IB order back to the proposal (orderRef is just 'proposal'), and nothing ever reconciles the FAILED proposal against IB open orders/fills.

- **Failure scenario:** IB Gateway hiccups during approve of 'BUY 500 AAPL bracket'. Client times out at 30s → proposal FAILED. 40s later the server-side coroutine finishes and the bracket goes live. The operator/LLM, seeing FAILED, re-proposes and re-approves → two live 500-share positions, double stop/TP exposure; the risk record (proposals) says zero shares were ever bought.

- **Suggested fix:** Give _place_and_wait a hard timeout that cancels staged legs on expiry; make the RPC timeout for order placement longer than the server-side worst case; write the proposal_id into orderRef and add a reconcile step (on FAILED-after-timeout, query IB open orders/executions for that ref before allowing re-approval).

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. RPC default timeout is 30s (sdk.py:147,182) and raises TimeoutError on expiry (clientserver.py:396). approve()'s broad `except Exception` sets the proposal terminal-FAILED (sdk.py:1425-1427). The server coroutine is NOT cancelled by client timeout: each leg does `await event.wait()` with no timeout (trading_runtime.py:962), so the bracket's transmit=True SL leg can go live seconds/minutes later. There is no idempotency link — orderRef is the literal 'proposal' (trading_runtime.py:873) — and no reconcile of a FAILED proposal against IB open orders/executions. The status!=PENDING guard (sdk.py:1360) only blocks re-approving the same proposal; a re-propose is unguarded, so an operator/LLM seeing FAILED can create a second live position with double protective exposure while the audit record shows zero shares. Downgraded to high (not critical): requires a >30s IB ack stall during that approve plus a re-propose to manifest, so low frequency, but the capital-safety impact warrants a fix (server-side hard timeout + cancel, longer placement RPC timeout, proposal_id in orderRef, reconcile before re-approval).


### [x] HIGH — execute_resize_plan cancels protective stops first and never restores them when the delta order fails

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1646`  ·  _reviewer: wrong-thing_

- **Mechanism:** execute_resize_plan's order of operations per position is: (1) cancel all associated protective orders (sdk.py:1601-1612), (2) place the delta market order, (3) re-create protectives. If step 2 fails, line 1646 does `continue  # Skip re-creating protectives if delta order failed` — the position is left live with its stop/trailing-stop/take-profit permanently cancelled, recorded only as a string in results['failures']. Step 2 is likely to fail exactly during a resize: place_order_simple runs the full risk gate (executioner.py:128-150), and RiskLimits.max_open_orders defaults to 15 — a 20-position book with protective orders exceeds that, so the gate rejects the delta AFTER the protectives were cancelled. A CLI crash/Ctrl-C between steps 1 and 3 has the same effect for every remaining position, and there is no persisted plan or recovery pass.

- **Failure scenario:** `resize-positions --max-bound 500000` on a book with 18 open protective orders. For the first position, its STP is cancelled, then the delta market order is rejected by the risk gate ('max open orders exceeded: 18 >= 15'). The loop continues to the next symbol, cancelling its stop too. The user ends the session with multiple positions whose stop-losses were silently removed; an overnight gap-down is unbounded.

- **Suggested fix:** Reverse the order (place delta first, then cancel/re-place protectives), or re-create the original protective orders at original quantities when the delta order fails; run the whole resize with skip_risk_gate semantics or pre-check open-order capacity before cancelling anything.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. sdk.py:1601-1612 cancels protectives first; the delta order at sdk.py:1620 omits skip_risk_gate (defaults False), so executioner.py:128-140 runs the max_open_orders gate (default 15, risk_gate.py:20,47) using len(book.get_orders()). On a large book, iteration 1 still holds other positions' protectives, so the count can exceed 15 and reject the delta AFTER this symbol's stop was cancelled; line 1646 `continue` (and the except at 1648) then skips re-creation, leaving the position unprotected. Even absent the gate, the delta can fail for buying-power/connectivity/validation reasons, and a Ctrl-C between steps 1 and 3 strands protectives for every remaining position. No rollback or recovery pass exists (CLI handler mmr_cli.py:1944 just reports results; no test covers restoration). For a live-money book, silently removing stop-losses is a real capital-safety hazard; high severity is warranted.


### [x] HIGH — Client-side RPC timeout during approve marks the proposal FAILED while trader_service continues executing it

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1426`  ·  _reviewer: wrong-thing_

- **Mechanism:** approve wraps the place_expressive_order RPC in a broad `except Exception` that transitions the proposal to FAILED (sdk.py:1425-1427). RPCClient raises TimeoutError after `timeout` (30s default; clientserver.py:396) but the server-side coroutine is not cancelled — place_expressive_order runs whatIfOrderAsync plus up to three sequential _place_and_wait legs (each an unbounded `await event.wait()`), so a slow Gateway can exceed 30s and still complete afterwards. Result: live orders/position exist, but the proposal is FAILED with no order_ids recorded, and FAILED is terminal so the record can never be corrected.

- **Failure scenario:** Gateway is slow after an overnight reconnect. `approve 42` (bracket) times out client-side at 30s -> proposal 42 marked FAILED. Five seconds later the server finishes placing entry+TP+SL. The LLM loop sees FAILED, re-proposes the same trade, and the second approval doubles the position; the audit trail attributes the live orders to nothing.

- **Suggested fix:** On TimeoutError specifically, do not transition to FAILED — leave APPROVED and reconcile against get_trades/orderRef ('proposal') before allowing a re-propose; or make the server idempotent by passing the proposal_id as orderRef and checking for it first.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. approve() uses MMR() default timeout=30 (mmr_cli.py:10094, sdk.py:147). RPCClient raises TimeoutError at 30s (clientserver.py:396) but ZMQ sends nothing to cancel the server; place_expressive_order awaits whatIfOrderAsync (trading_runtime.py:831) plus up to three legs each with an unbounded `await event.wait()` (trading_runtime.py:962), so a slow Gateway can finish placing orders after the client gives up. The TimeoutError is caught by the broad `except Exception` (sdk.py:1425) and the proposal is set FAILED (sdk.py:1426); FAILED is terminal (`_ALLOWED_TRANSITIONS[FAILED]=set()`, proposal_store.py:34), so a live order is permanently mislabeled with no order_ids. orderRef is the static 'proposal' (trading_runtime.py:854,873), not proposal_id, so no server idempotency blocks a duplicate re-propose. No guard/retry/reconciliation refutes any link. Severity high (capital safety: audit corruption + double-position risk), though gated on >30s Gateway latency so low-frequency.


### [ ] HIGH — Zombie subscriptions: local registry set before publish_contract succeeds and never re-published after trader_service restart

- **Location:** `trader/strategy/strategy_runtime.py:280`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** subscribe() inserts conId into self.strategies BEFORE calling trader_client.rpc().publish_contract(); on all later calls the elif branch skips the publish because the conId is already registered. Two consequences: (1) if the initial publish_contract raises (trader_service bouncing — the reconcile path swallows TimeoutError/ConnectionError at DEBUG, line 482), the local registry says 'subscribed' but trader_service never streams the contract, and reconcile will never retry the publish; (2) when trader_service restarts, its zmq_pubsub_contract_filters dict (trading_runtime.py:711) is empty — no contract is streamed — yet strategy_service's 30s reconcile never re-issues publish_contract because its local dict is intact. All strategies silently receive zero ticks forever.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service is restarted at 10:00 (pycron bounce, IB gateway hiccup). strategy_service stays up, reconcile runs every 30s and 'succeeds'. No strategy receives a tick for the rest of the session; strategies holding positions never emit exit signals; nothing above DEBUG is logged.

- **Suggested fix:** In reconcile, call trader_client.rpc().get_published_contracts() and re-publish any conId in self.strategies that is missing server-side; only add the conId to the local registry after publish_contract returns successfully; log reconcile RPC failures at WARNING, not DEBUG.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end and confirmed. strategy_runtime.py:277-282: the conId is inserted into self.strategies (line 278-279) before publish_contract (line 280); every later call hits the elif (281) and skips publishing. self.strategies is created once (line 123) and never cleared (grep confirms no reset), and run()/reconcile have no trader-restart detection. trader_service's zmq_pubsub_contract_filters is in-memory (trading_runtime.py:143, reset at 258); on restart it's empty and only publish_contract re-registers streaming (738), which reconcile never re-issues. Reconcile swallows Timeout/ConnectionError at DEBUG (481-482), so an initial publish failure is silent and never retried. get_published_contracts (trader_service_api.py:166) exists but is unused. Severity high not critical: it needs a specific trigger (trader_service-only bounce or transient publish failure) and many strategies are propose-only rather than auto_execute, so impact is silent missed/exit signals rather than direct order loss — but it is total and unlogged for the session.


### [x] HIGH — Live path feeds unbounded per-tick pseudo-bars into strategies configured for bar_size — live/backtest parity broken and O(N) growth per tick

- **Location:** `trader/strategy/strategy_runtime.py:243`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** on_ticker_next appends one row per raw IB ticker event (normalize_ticker sets open=high=low=close=last-or-mid) to self.streams[conId] via pd.concat and hands the whole frame to on_prices. There is no aggregation to the strategy's configured bar_size, no dedup/ordering of out-of-order ticks, no seeding from the historical bars fetched into DuckDB by get_historical_data(), and no cap on frame length. So a strategy backtested on 1-min OHLCV bars runs live on tick-frequency rows: indicator windows measured in bars become windows measured in ticks (seconds), producing signals that bear no relation to the backtested behavior. Additionally, pd.concat copies the full frame per tick and strategies like SMICrossOver rerun vbt.MA.run on the full series each tick — O(N^2) CPU and unbounded memory over a session.

- **Failure scenario:** SMICrossOver deployed with bar_size '1 min', FAST=10/SLOW=50 validated by backtest. Live, IB emits several ticker updates per second, so the 10/50 'bar' windows span ~5-25 seconds of ticks; the strategy emits crossover signals on tick noise the backtest never saw. Meanwhile a liquid symbol accumulates hundreds of thousands of rows by afternoon, and each tick costs a full-frame concat plus full-series MA recompute, stalling the event loop.

- **Suggested fix:** Resample ticks into bars of ctx.bar_size (only dispatch on bar close), seed streams from the DuckDB history that get_historical_data already fetched, and cap the retained window to what strategies need.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. Publisher emits raw per-tick IB reqMktData updates (trading_runtime.py:714-715 puts each pendingTicker on 'ticker'; ibreactive.py:199-201 flat_maps pendingTickersEvent with no throttle). on_ticker_next (strategy_runtime.py:239-247) turns each tick into a single OHLC=last row via normalize_ticker (market_data.py:69-84) and pd.concats it unbounded into self.streams[conId], then passes the full frame to on_prices. self.streams is populated ONLY here; get_historical_data writes bars to DuckDB (strategy_runtime.py:597-608), never seeding streams — so no bar aggregation, no history seed, no cap. SMICrossOver.on_prices (smi_crossover.py:95-106) runs vbt.MA.run(close,10/50) over tick rows; its own comment concedes it's "called once per tick," proving windows are counted in ticks not the configured 1-min bars. This is a capital-safety parity break, not mere latency: live signals fire on tick noise unrelated to the backtested/validated behavior, so high severity holds even for a low-frequency system. The O(N^2)/unbounded-memory sub-claim is real but secondary.


### [ ] HIGH — run() is not restart-safe: crash-restart re-binds the RPC port (EADDRINUSE), turning any transient startup failure into permanent service death

- **Location:** `trader/strategy/strategy_runtime.py:655`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** strategy_service.py restarts strategy_runtime.run() on the SAME StrategyRuntime instance after a crash (on_runtime_done -> _start_runtime, up to 5 times). But run() is written as one-shot: it calls zmq_strategy_rpc_server.serve() which creates a fresh ROUTER socket and bind()s the same TCP port while the previous socket from the crashed run is still bound (RPCServer.serve, clientserver.py:434 — nothing closes the old socket) -> zmq EADDRINUSE raises immediately. Also, the startup subscription loop (lines 680-695) calls blocking trader_client.rpc().resolve_symbol()/publish_contract() with no exception handling, so a TimeoutError while trader_service is down is exactly the crash that triggers the restart. Result: first crash -> restart -> instant EADDRINUSE crash x4 -> MAX_RUNTIME_RESTARTS exceeded -> service stops.

- **Failure scenario:** strategy_service starts while trader_service is still connecting to IB. resolve_symbol at line 683 raises TimeoutError after serve() already bound port 42005; run() crashes; the restart 5s later crashes on bind; after 5 rapid attempts the service exits and no strategy runs until a human intervenes.

- **Suggested fix:** Make run() idempotent (close/teardown sockets, subscription and messagebus client before re-setup, or move one-time setup out of run()), and wrap the startup resolve/subscribe loop in the same transient-error handling reconcile uses.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. strategy_service.py:90-92 restarts run() on the same StrategyRuntime instance. run() (strategy_runtime.py:655) calls RPCServer.serve(), which at clientserver.py:434-437 unconditionally creates+binds a fresh ROUTER socket on the same address and never closes the prior one; no teardown exists in on_runtime_done or run(). A second in-process bind() on the same tcp endpoint raises zmq.ZMQError (EADDRINUSE) synchronously, so every restart dies at line 655 -> restarts exhausted -> service stops. First-crash trigger is real: the startup subscribe loop (strategy_runtime.py:680-695) calls the synchronous trader_client.rpc().resolve_symbol (line 683) with no exception handling; it raises TimeoutError (clientserver.py:396) when trader_service RPC is unresponsive. pycron depends_on (pycron.yaml:38) orders process start only, not RPC readiness, and restart_if_found lets trader_service restart later, so this unguarded window is reachable. Severity high: transient startup failure permanently and silently kills the strategy engine, leaving strategy-managed exits unattended.


### [x] HIGH — BookSubject never removes filled/cancelled orders, so the risk gate's max_open_orders counts every order ever seen and falsely blocks all trading mid-session

- **Location:** `trader/trading/book.py:24`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** add_update_trade only prepends: self.orders[orderId] gets a new entry per orderStatus event and entries are never deleted on Filled/Cancelled status (no pop/clear anywhere in the class; self.book is created once in Trader.__init__). Both risk-gate call sites compute open_order_count as len(book.get_orders()) — i.e. the number of DISTINCT orderIds seen since service start, not open orders. With the default RiskLimits.max_open_orders=15 and each bracket consuming 3 orderIds, after 5 bracket proposals (or any mix of 15 filled/cancelled/open orders) every subsequent order is rejected with 'max open orders exceeded' until the service restarts. Secondary effects: cancel_all() (trading_runtime.py:1274) iterates the same dict and issues cancels for long-filled orders, and the per-event list prepending grows without bound.

- **Failure scenario:** A normal trading day: 4 bracket proposals execute in the morning (12 orderIds) plus 3 manual orders. At 2pm a high-conviction proposal is approved and place_expressive_order returns 'Risk gate: max open orders exceeded: 15 >= 15' even though only 4 protective stops are actually open at IB. All trading is blocked for the rest of the session.

- **Suggested fix:** Count open orders from live state: filter book entries by the latest Trade.orderStatus being an active status (or use ib.openTrades()), and prune/mark entries on terminal statuses in add_update_trade.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. book.py:24-32 prepends every Trade (from orderStatusEvent/openOrderEvent/newOrderEvent/cancelOrderEvent, subscribed at trading_runtime.py:363-371) into self.orders keyed by orderId; no pop/clear/del exists anywhere in book.py, so Filled/Cancelled entries never leave. Both gate call sites use len(self.book.get_orders()) (trading_runtime.py:941; executioner.py:139) = count of distinct orderIds ever seen, not live-open. RiskLimits.max_open_orders=15 (risk_gate.py:20) rejects at >= (risk_gate.py:47), and place_expressive_order returns SuccessFail.fail (trading_runtime.py:943-944). ~15 orderIds (5 brackets) permanently disables new-order placement until restart; startup reqAllOpenOrdersAsync pre-seeds the count. No test guards this. Severity high: it fails closed (safer than fail-open, no erroneous trade), but silently and irreversibly blocks all trading — including risk-reducing protective/exit orders — for the rest of a session, and is trivially triggered in one normal day.


### [x] HIGH — RiskGate daily-loss, position-concentration, and signal-rate limits are dead code — every call site passes only open_order_count

- **Location:** `trader/trading/executioner.py:137`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** risk_gate.evaluate() is called from exactly two places (executioner.py:137 and trading_runtime.py:939), and both pass only open_order_count. daily_pnl, portfolio_value and position_value keep their 0.0 defaults, so 'daily_pnl < -max_daily_loss' and the concentration check ('portfolio_value > 0 and position_value > 0') can never trigger. The max_signals_per_hour check counts EventType.SIGNAL rows for strategy_name='manual'/'proposal', but SIGNAL events are only ever appended by strategy_runtime.py for strategy names — so it always counts 0 on the execution path. The only live limit in the gate is max_open_orders. Meanwhile the CLI exposes 'session set max_daily_loss' documented as 'Max allowed daily loss in $ before blocking new orders', giving the operator false assurance that a live-account loss circuit-breaker exists. (PositionSizer has its own daily-loss check, but that only shrinks sizing at propose time; approve/buy/sell paths are unguarded.)

- **Failure scenario:** The account is down $8,000 on the day with max_daily_loss configured at $1,000. The LLM loop approves three more proposals; place_expressive_order calls evaluate() with daily_pnl=0.0, all pass, and orders transmit. The configured daily-loss circuit breaker never fires on any execution path.

- **Suggested fix:** At both call sites, fetch real values (sum of PnLSingle dailyPnL from self.pnl, NetLiquidation, and the whatIf position value already computed for the leverage check) and pass them to evaluate(); or remove the parameters and the CLI knob so the gap is at least visible.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. risk_gate.py:42-44 defaults daily_pnl/portfolio_value/position_value to 0.0. The only two evaluate() callers, executioner.py:137-140 and trading_runtime.py:939-942, pass solely open_order_count, so the daily-loss check (risk_gate.py:54) and concentration check (line 61, gated on portfolio_value>0 and position_value>0) can never trigger. The signal-rate check filters by strategy_name=signal.source_name ('manual'/'proposal'), but EventType.SIGNAL rows are written only by strategy_runtime.py:256 and backtester.py:357 for real strategy names, so count_since returns 0 on the execution path. Only max_open_orders (both paths) and check_leverage (runtime path only) are live. mmr_cli.py:3050 advertises max_daily_loss as blocking new orders — false assurance. High severity: a documented live-account loss circuit breaker that silently never fires is a capital-safety gap, not latency.


### [x] HIGH — helper_create_order turns 'market order with stop-loss' into a bare StopOrder entry — the stop-loss protection is silently consumed as the entry trigger

- **Location:** `trader/trading/executioner.py:249`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** When market_order=True and stop_loss_percentage>0, the branch at line 248 builds a single StopOrder(action, stopPrice=order_price*(1-pct)) as THE order. No market entry and no protective child order are created. For a BUY, the stop price is below the current ask, so IB's buy-stop trigger condition (price rises to stop) is already satisfied — it executes immediately as a market buy — and the position ends up with zero stop-loss protection despite the caller requesting it. For a SELL, the requested immediate market sell instead becomes a dormant sell-stop below the market that may never execute. The same confusion exists in the StopLimitOrder branch. This is reachable via sdk.buy()/sell(stop_loss_percentage=...) over RPC (trader_service_api.place_order_simple).

- **Failure scenario:** A script calls sdk.sell('AMD', quantity=500, market=True, stop_loss_percentage=0.05) intending 'sell now, at market'. Instead a SELL stop at 5% below the bid is placed; AMD drifts up, the order never fills, and the position the caller believes was liquidated is still open and unhedged. Conversely a buy with stop-loss executes but carries no protective stop.

- **Suggested fix:** Build the entry (MarketOrder/LimitOrder) plus an attached protective StopOrder child (parentId + transmit chaining), matching the semantics place_expressive_order implements; or reject stop_loss_percentage on this path outright.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end and confirmed. executioner.py:248-255: when market_order and stop_loss_price>0, the sole order built is a bare StopOrder(action=entry action, stopPrice=below market) — no market entry, no protective child. stop_loss_price (line 244) is always below order_price (=latest_tick.ask, line 231) for both BUY and SELL. trading_runtime.py:1248-1264 places exactly that one order. Reachable via sdk.buy/sell(stop_loss_percentage=) (sdk.py:706-713) and CLI trade buy/sell --stop_loss_percentage (commands.py:1264/1313), whose help promises "place stop loss order." Result: a SELL becomes a dormant resting stop (position not liquidated), a BUY fires immediately with zero protection. Capital-safety impact, hence high. Only mitigation: it's a legacy path flagged "place_order_simple() is not complete" (trader_service_api.py:95), off the main propose/place_expressive_order flow — but still user-reachable with misleading help text.


### [x] HIGH — Event-store append failure after successful order placement converts a live order into a reported failure, inviting duplicate retries

- **Location:** `trader/trading/executioner.py:96`  ·  _reviewer: stores_

- **Mechanism:** In `subscribe_place_order_direct`, `self._log_event(EventType.ORDER_SUBMITTED, ...)` runs inside the `try:` AFTER `await self.trader.client.subscribe_place_order(contract, order)` has already transmitted the order to IB. `_log_event` → `EventStore.append` → `DuckDBConnection.execute_atomic`, which raises (duckdb.IOException after ~45s of starved lock retries, non-lock IOException immediately, disk-full, etc.). The `except Exception` at line 100 then returns `trader_exception_helper(ex)` — a throw observable — even though the order is live. `place_expressive_order._place_and_wait` (trading_runtime.py:946-963) maps that to `trade=None` → `SuccessFail.fail('Failed to place entry order')`, and `sdk.approve()` marks the proposal FAILED. The success observable (fill tracking) is also lost.

- **Failure scenario:** A nightly sweep or another process holds the mmr.duckdb file lock for >45s at the moment a market entry order is approved. The order is transmitted to IB and fills, but append() raises, approve() returns failure and marks the proposal FAILED. The operator/LLM sees FAILED, re-proposes and re-approves → duplicate position on the live account; meanwhile the first order has no protective legs or tracking.

- **Suggested fix:** Wrap `_log_event` in try/except that logs and continues — the audit record must never change the success/failure semantics of an already-transmitted order. Consider logging ORDER_SUBMITTED asynchronously off the placement path.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. executioner.py:95 (subscribe_place_order → ibreactive.py:423 ib.placeOrder) transmits a live order; executioner.py:96 _log_event runs inside the same try. _log_event→event_store.append→duckdb_store execute_atomic can raise (non-lock IOException line 109, exhausted lock retries line 117, disk-full via fn(conn) line 119) with no internal guard. The raise is caught at executioner.py:100 and returned as a throw observable despite the order being live. For a BRACKET proposal the SL leg (trading_runtime.py:1018 transmit=True) transmits the whole bracket, so a _log_event failure makes _place_and_wait return None → line 1024 SuccessFail.fail → sdk.approve (sdk.py:1422) marks the proposal FAILED, inviting a duplicate re-approve while the first order is live and its protective legs are being cancel-raced. The finding's line-984 message attribution is a minor imprecision (that leg is transmit=False), but the mechanism and dangerous FAILED-with-live-order outcome are real. High, not critical: trigger is a rare append failure, but the impact is duplicate/unprotected live-money positions where capital safety dominates.


### [x] HIGH — Risk gate position-concentration and daily-loss limits are silently inert on the manual/option order path

- **Location:** `trader/trading/executioner.py:137`  ·  _reviewer: probe-0:Options live-order path: contract constr_

- **Mechanism:** place_order() invokes self.trader.risk_gate.evaluate(signal=signal, open_order_count=...) but omits portfolio_value, position_value, and daily_pnl, which default to 0.0 in RiskGate.evaluate (risk_gate.py:42-44). The concentration check is guarded by `if portfolio_value > 0 and position_value > 0` (never true here) and the daily-loss check is `daily_pnl < -max_daily_loss` (0 < -X is false), so both are skipped. Only max_open_orders and signal-rate are enforced for direct buy/sell/option orders. Options make this worse because notional = quantity x premium x 100, so even a small contract count is large capital with no size gate.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr options buy AAPL -e 3m -s 250 -r C -q 50 --market` (50 contracts x $8 premium x 100 = ~$40k notional) on a modest account. The risk gate approves because position_value=0 was passed, so the max_position_size_pct (10%) concentration limit never evaluates; an oversized, over-concentrated options position is placed unchecked.

- **Suggested fix:** Pass real portfolio_value/position_value (quantity x price x contract multiplier) and daily_pnl into evaluate() from place_order, or compute them there; treat options multiplier explicitly when deriving position_value.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end and confirmed. `buy_option` (sdk.py:2924) → `place_order_simple` (trading_runtime.py:1233, skip_risk_gate defaults False) → `executioner.place_order` → risk_gate.evaluate(signal, open_order_count) at executioner.py:137. It omits portfolio_value/position_value/daily_pnl, which default to 0.0 (risk_gate.py:42-44). The concentration guard `if portfolio_value > 0 and position_value > 0` (risk_gate.py:61) is never true, and the daily-loss guard `daily_pnl < -max_daily_loss` (risk_gate.py:54) is `0 < -1000` = false. Both are silently skipped; only max_open_orders + signal-rate apply. The manual/option path also lacks the check_leverage gate that place_expressive_order uses (trading_runtime.py:926), so there is zero size/notional control. Severity high: on a live-money system, the 10% concentration cap and daily-loss stop are core capital-safety controls that appear active but are inert for every direct buy/sell/options order.


### [x] HIGH — Correlation clustering is dead code — three fatal call errors are swallowed, so cluster warnings never fire

- **Location:** `trader/trading/portfolio_risk.py:234`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** _compute_correlations() cannot execute past its first statements: (1) `UniverseAccessor(self._duckdb_path)` omits the required second positional arg `universe_library` (universe.py:48) -> TypeError; (2) `accessor.all_definitions()` does not exist on UniverseAccessor (no such method in universe.py) -> AttributeError; (3) `ds.read(con_id, '1 day', count=60)` passes '1 day' as `start` and a nonexistent `count` kwarg (duckdb_store.py read signature is (symbol, start, end, bar_size)) -> TypeError. Additionally it reads the trading DB (sdk.risk_report passes duckdb_path) rather than history_duckdb_path where OHLCV lives. Every failure is swallowed by the blanket `except Exception: return [], 0` at line 302, so `portfolio-risk` always reports zero correlation clusters and data_coverage=0 with no error. tests/test_portfolio_risk.py monkeypatches _compute_correlations, so the breakage is invisible to the suite.

- **Failure scenario:** Portfolio holds 5 highly correlated long semiconductor names totalling 60% of net liq. The LLM loop runs `mmr --json portfolio-risk` before approving another chip trade; correlation_clusters is [] and no 'correlated cluster has X% net exposure' warning appears, so the documented pre-approve risk check passes and the concentrated trade is approved.

- **Suggested fix:** Fix the three call sites (UniverseAccessor(duckdb_path, universe_library), use resolve_symbol or the universe get_all path, ds.read(str(con_id), start=now-90d, bar_size='1 day') against history_duckdb_path), and replace the blanket except with logged/surfaced errors per the fail-loudly principle.

- **Verifier:** All three defects verified. UniverseAccessor.__init__ requires (duckdb_path, universe_library) at universe.py:48, but portfolio_risk.py:234 passes one arg -> TypeError (executes first). all_definitions() does not exist in universe.py. DuckDBDataStore.read signature is (symbol, start, end, bar_size) at duckdb_store.py:175 with no count kwarg, so portfolio_risk.py:247 ds.read(con_id,'1 day',count=60) -> TypeError. The blanket except at portfolio_risk.py:302-303 swallows all, always returning ([],0). tests/test_portfolio_risk.py monkeypatches _compute_correlations (lines 109,130), hiding it. So correlation-cluster warnings never fire. Severity high not critical: separate HHI/gross concentration warnings still compute and would likely catch a 60%/5-name book; only the distinct correlation-cluster gate is dead, but it is a documented pre-approve check the LLM loop relies on.


### [x] HIGH — TradingFilter.load() swallows every exception and silently returns an empty allow-everything filter

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_filter.py:117`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** The bare 'except Exception: return TradingFilter.default()' means any parse error, bad type (e.g. min_price: 'abc' raising in float()), or permission error on ~/.config/mmr/trading_filters.yaml silently yields the default filter, which is completely empty — no denylist, no allowlist, no exchange restrictions. There is no log line at all. Trader startup (trading_runtime.py:274) assigns this to risk_gate.trading_filter, so every subsequent check_instrument() approves everything. This directly violates the 'fail loudly, not silently' design principle for a component whose whole purpose is capital safety.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator hand-edits trading_filters.yaml to add a denylist entry and leaves a stray tab (YAML parse error). trader_service restarts cleanly, no warning is logged, and the LLM loop happily proposes and executes trades in symbols the operator explicitly denylisted, on a live account.

- **Suggested fix:** Fail startup (or at minimum log an ERROR and refuse to trade) when the filter file exists but cannot be parsed; never substitute an empty filter for a present-but-broken config.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. trading_filter.py:117 catches every exception and returns TradingFilter.default() (line 94), an all-empty filter; its is_allowed() (lines 42-77) returns (True,'') because denylist/allowlist are empty, with zero logging. trading_runtime.py:274 assigns this to risk_gate.trading_filter at startup, and executioner.py:111 -> risk_gate.py:92-97 check_instrument then approves every order (non-None but empty filter passes). A malformed present file (YAML syntax error, or min_price:'abc' raising in float() at line 115) silently discards the operator's denylist. No guard, log, or test mitigates this. Directly violates the codebase's "fail loudly, not silently" principle for a capital-safety component. Severity raised to high given a live-money, low-frequency system where a silently-voided denylist can execute explicitly-forbidden trades.


### [x] HIGH — place_expressive_order returns SUCCESS when the protective leg or even the entry fails (all non-BRACKET branches)

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:1082`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** Only the BRACKET branch is transactional. In the TRAILING_STOP branch (lines 1082-1083) and STOP_LOSS branch (lines 1129-1130), if the protective child order fails (subscribe_place_order_direct returns rx.throw, e.g. IB disconnect between legs, account-guard trip, or placeOrder exception), the code does `if trail_trade: trades.append(...)` and falls through to `return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)` — no rollback, no failure. The entry was staged with transmit=False, so it is left as a dangling never-transmitted order at IB while the caller is told the trade succeeded. In the NONE branch (lines 1148-1151), a failed entry (`entry_trade is None`) likewise returns SuccessFail.success with an empty trades list. sdk.approve() (sdk.py:1414) marks the proposal EXECUTED whenever result.is_success(), so the proposal store records EXECUTED with zero or partial order_ids.

- **Failure scenario:** LLM approves proposal #42 (BUY 100 AAPL, trailing-stop exit). Entry stages OK (transmit=False); IB Gateway hiccups before the TRAIL leg, placeOrder raises, trail_trade stays None. Method returns success; proposal is marked EXECUTED. No order ever transmits — the LLM's next portfolio-diff shows no position for a trade it believes executed, and a dead transmit=False entry order lingers at IB. Symmetrically, a rejected market order in the NONE branch returns success with order_ids=[], so a real intended trade silently never happens while the state machine says it did.

- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the BRACKET rollback in TRAILING_STOP and STOP_LOSS: on protective-leg failure, _cancel_trade_safely(entry_trade) and return SuccessFail.fail. In the NONE branch, return SuccessFail.fail when entry_trade is None.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed end-to-end. In trading_runtime.py the BRACKET branch rolls back (cancel entry, return fail: lines 1006-1009, 1027-1031), but TRAILING_STOP (1082 `if trail_trade:`) and STOP_LOSS (1129 `if sl_trade:`) have no else and fall through to `return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)` at 1151, leaving a staged transmit=False entry un-cancelled. The NONE branch (1148-1149) has no `if entry_trade is None` guard at all, so a failed entry returns success with obj=[]. The None state is real: executioner.py:70-101 returns rx.throw on account-guard trip or any subscribe_place_order exception, which fires the observable on_error callback (`on_error=lambda e: task.set()`) leaving trade=None. sdk.py:1412-1419 marks the proposal EXECUTED whenever is_success(), recording empty/partial order_ids. Severity high (not critical): no unintended live order is placed and the transmit=False entry never executes, but state-integrity corruption in an autonomous approve loop causes the LLM to mis-track its book.


### [x] HIGH — Daily-loss and position-concentration risk limits are never enforced — every call site passes only open_order_count

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:939`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** RiskGate.evaluate has four checks: max open orders, daily loss, position concentration, and signal rate. The only two call sites in the codebase (trading_runtime.py:939 and executioner.py:137) call `evaluate(signal=..., open_order_count=...)`, leaving `daily_pnl=0.0` and `portfolio_value=0.0`/`position_value=0.0` at their defaults. `if daily_pnl < -self.limits.max_daily_loss` can never trigger with 0.0, and the concentration branch requires `portfolio_value > 0`. So max_daily_loss ($1000) and max_position_size_pct (10%) are dead code on every real order path — despite CLAUDE.md documenting the risk gate as enforcing 'max position size, daily loss'. The system has live daily-PnL data available (self.pnl cache, ib.accountValues) but never wires it in.

- **Failure scenario:** The LLM trading loop has a bad day: realized daily PnL is -$25,000, 25x past the configured $1,000 daily-loss limit. It approves another proposal. The risk gate evaluates daily_pnl=0.0, approves, and the order is placed. The one capital-safety circuit breaker the operator believes exists never fires, on a live account.

- **Suggested fix:** At both call sites, compute daily_pnl from self.pnl.get_all() / accountValues and pass portfolio_value + estimated position_value, or delete the parameters and the documentation claim so the gap is at least honest (fail-loudly principle).

- **Verifier:** Confirmed. RiskGate.evaluate (risk_gate.py:38-43) defaults daily_pnl=0.0, portfolio_value=0.0, position_value=0.0. The daily-loss check at risk_gate.py:53 (`daily_pnl < -max_daily_loss`) can never fire at 0.0; the concentration check at risk_gate.py:60 is gated on `portfolio_value>0 and position_value>0`. The only two production callers — trading_runtime.py:939 and executioner.py:137 — pass exclusively `signal=` and `open_order_count=`, so both parameters stay at their inert defaults on every real order path. This is despite trading_runtime.py:118 already reading `accountValues()` nearby for the leverage check, so the data is available. tests/test_risk_gate.py:35,43-44 only exercise these branches by passing values directly to evaluate(), never via an order path, giving false confidence. CLAUDE.md documents the gate as enforcing "max position size, daily loss," so the operator believes a circuit breaker exists that never fires. For a low-frequency live-money system, capital-safety dead code is genuinely high severity.


### [x] HIGH — Order 'success' is determined by the local placeOrder echo — IB-side rejections are never observed, so a bracket can transmit with a rejected stop-loss leg and still be marked EXECUTED

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:956`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** _place_and_wait subscribes to the observable from subscribe_place_order_direct and sets its result on the FIRST on_next. In ibreactive.subscribe_place_order (ibreactive.py:423-428), the first emission is rx.of(trade_result) — the Trade object returned synchronously by ib.placeOrder() before IB has acknowledged anything. IB rejections arrive asynchronously as orderStatus 'Cancelled'/'Inactive' or errorEvent, which are emitted as later on_next values (or not at all) and are never inspected. Therefore every leg of place_expressive_order 'succeeds' as long as the local placeOrder call doesn't throw; order status is never checked before returning SuccessFail.success, and sdk.approve() then marks the proposal EXECUTED. The BRACKET rollback logic (entry_trade is None checks) only ever fires for local failures (blank account validation, disconnected socket), never for broker rejections.

- **Failure scenario:** LLM approves a BUY bracket proposal. Entry and TP stage fine; the SL leg transmits the group but IB asynchronously rejects the stop with error 110 (invalid stop price, e.g. price increment violation on an ASX stock). The parent market BUY and TP were already transmitted and the entry fills — the account now holds a live position with NO stop-loss — while place_expressive_order has already returned success and the proposal shows EXECUTED with 3 order_ids. Nothing alerts that the protective leg is dead.

- **Suggested fix:** After placing each leg, wait for a definitive IB ack (orderStatus in Submitted/PreSubmitted/Filled) with a timeout, and treat Cancelled/Inactive or an errorEvent for that orderId as leg failure triggering the existing rollback. At minimum, re-query trade.orderStatus for all legs before returning success and before marking the proposal EXECUTED.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. _place_and_wait (trading_runtime.py:946-963) returns on the first on_next; that first emission is the synchronous placeOrder echo built in subscribe_place_order (ibreactive.py:423-428, rx.of(trade_result) concat live stream) — trade_result is ib.placeOrder()'s immediate fire-and-forget Trade (status PendingSubmit). on_error only fires for LOCAL failures via trader_exception_helper (executioner.py:70-101). Async IB rejections (error 110) arrive as later, uninspected orderStatus/errorEvent emissions. So each leg 'succeeds' and place_expressive_order returns success (line 1151); BRACKET rollback (lines 1006/1027) only fires on trade is None. sdk.approve (sdk.py:1412-1419) then marks the proposal EXECUTED with order_ids, never re-querying orderStatus. The documented 'bracket transactionality' only covers local leg failures, exactly as claimed. Worst case (filled entry + rejected SL = unprotected position reported EXECUTED) hinges on IB filling the parent while rejecting only the SL leg — a broker-behavior dependency — but the code defect (no ack verification before EXECUTED) is unconditional. High rather than critical: requires an uncommon async leg rejection, but yields a silent unhedged live position.


### [x] HIGH — STOP_LOSS and TRAILING_STOP paths return SuccessFail.success when the exit leg fails, leaving the entry staged with transmit=False and the proposal falsely marked EXECUTED

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:1082`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** In place_expressive_order, the TRAILING_STOP branch (line 1082: 'if trail_trade: trades.append(trail_trade)') and the STOP_LOSS branch (line 1129: 'if sl_trade: trades.append(sl_trade)') simply skip appending when the exit leg fails and fall through to 'return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)'. Unlike the BRACKET branch, there is no _cancel_trade_safely rollback and no failure return. The entry was placed with transmit=False, and it is the exit child (transmit=True) that transmits the whole group — so when the exit leg fails, the entry is never transmitted to the market. sdk.approve() sees success and transitions the proposal to EXECUTED (terminal, immutable) with the entry's order_id.

- **Failure scenario:** Proposal 'BUY 100 AAPL limit 210 with STOP_LOSS 195' is approved while the gateway hiccups: the entry stages OK, then subscribe_place_order_direct throws on the SL leg (connection reset). place_expressive_order returns success containing only the staged entry; proposal marked EXECUTED. No order is ever working at the exchange, but the LLM loop and dashboard believe the position was entered with protection — the trade is silently dropped and a dormant untransmitted order lingers at the gateway.

- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the BRACKET branch: if the exit leg trade is None, _cancel_trade_safely(entry_trade) and return SuccessFail.fail so the proposal transitions to FAILED instead of EXECUTED.

- **Verifier:** Control flow confirmed end-to-end. trading_runtime.py:1082-1083 (TRAILING_STOP) and 1129-1130 (STOP_LOSS) only append the exit trade when non-None and otherwise fall through to the shared `return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)` at 1151 — with no rollback of the transmit=False entry, unlike the BRACKET branch (1001-1009, 1024-1031). The exit leg can fail independently: executioner.py:94-101 wraps `subscribe_place_order` exceptions in a throwing observable, and the subscriber's on_error (lines 1080/1127) merely sets the event, leaving trail_trade/sl_trade None. sdk.approve() then hits `if result.is_success()` (sdk.py:1412) and marks the proposal EXECUTED (terminal/immutable) at 1419. No test exercises this path. Severity high, but bounded: entry is transmit=False so nothing reaches the market — the damage is a silently dropped trade, a false immutable EXECUTED state misleading the LLM/dashboard, and a dormant staged order, not live unprotected exposure.


### [ ] HIGH — Live market-data (ticker) subscriptions are never restored after an IB reconnect — strategy tick feed goes silently dead

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:711`  ·  _reviewer: ib-listener_

- **Mechanism:** On disconnect, `disconnected_event` -> `IBAIORx.connect_async()` replaces `self.ib` with a fresh `IB()` (ibreactive.py:333). The snapshot/restore machinery re-attaches eventkit handlers (so the RxPY pipe from `pendingTickersEvent` stays wired), but nothing re-issues `reqMktData` for previously subscribed contracts: `connected_event`/`setup_subscriptions` re-subscribes only positions/portfolio/PnL/book. Worse, `publish_contract` early-returns on its `zmq_pubsub_contract_filters` cache (line 711), which is only reset in `Trader.connect()` at process startup — so even strategy_service's idempotent reconcile (`strategy_runtime.py:280`) and manual `mmr listen`/`watch` re-invocations hit the cache and never re-call `subscribe_contract_direct`. The RxPY plumbing is alive but permanently starved.

- **Failure scenario:** IB Gateway restarts overnight (its scheduled daily restart). trader_service reconnects successfully, portfolio and PnL resume, `status` shows connected. But every ticker previously published on ZMQ :42002 (all strategy bar feeds, `watch`, `listen`) receives zero events from then on: strategies accumulate no new bars and emit no signals, protective/monitoring logic based on live prices is blind, and nothing logs an error. Recovery requires restarting trader_service.

- **Suggested fix:** In `connected_event`, clear `zmq_pubsub_contract_filters`/`zmq_pubsub_contracts` and replay `subscribe_contract_direct` for every previously published conId (keep a persistent set of desired subscriptions and reconcile it against the fresh IB session, like the PnL path does).

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. On disconnect, `disconnected_event` calls `client.connect_async()` which replaces `self.ib` with a fresh `IB()` (ibreactive.py:333) — all server-side `reqMktData` lines are gone. `_restore_event_handlers` (ibreactive.py:131) only re-attaches the `pendingTickersEvent` handler keeping the RxPY pipe wired; it never re-issues `reqMktData`. `connected_event`→`setup_subscriptions` (trading_runtime.py:516,351) re-subscribes only positions/portfolio/PnL/book/orders — never tickers. The only path that calls `reqMktData` for pubsub tickers is `subscribe_contract_direct` (ibreactive.py:455), reached solely via `publish_contract`, which early-returns on the `zmq_pubsub_contract_filters` cache (trading_runtime.py:711). That cache is cleared only at process startup (line 258), never in `connected_event`, so strategy_service's idempotent reconcile (strategy_runtime.py:280) hits the cache and never re-subscribes. Result: after IB Gateway's daily restart, the tick feed is silently dead with no error logged. Severity high not critical: native protective STP/bracket orders rest server-side on IB, so capital protection survives; harm is silent strategy blindness requiring manual restart.


### [x] HIGH — TRAILING_STOP and STOP_LOSS exits return success even when the protective leg fails, leaving a staged transmit=False entry and a proposal falsely marked EXECUTED

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:1081`  ·  _reviewer: architecture_

- **Mechanism:** The BRACKET path correctly rolls back staged legs on failure, but the TRAILING_STOP path (lines 1079-1083) and STOP_LOSS path (lines 1126-1130) do not: the entry is staged with transmit=False, then the protective child is placed with transmit=True; if the child errors (on_error sets the event with trail_trade/sl_trade = None), the code just skips the append and falls through to `return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)` with only the entry trade. The entry is never cancelled and never transmitted. sdk.approve() sees is_success() and marks the proposal EXECUTED with the entry's orderId.

- **Failure scenario:** propose AAPL BUY --trailing-stop-pct 2.0, approve. IB rejects the TRAIL child (e.g. invalid trailingPercent for the instrument). place_expressive_order returns success([entry_trade]); the proposal is marked EXECUTED. No order ever transmits — the operator believes a protected long exists, portfolio shows nothing, and the untransmitted parent lingers at the Gateway. The inverse of the documented 'bracket is all-or-nothing' guarantee for two of the three protected-exit types.

- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the BRACKET rollback: if the TRAIL/STP child returns None, _cancel_trade_safely(entry_trade) and return SuccessFail.fail. Add tests parallel to the existing bracket-rollback tests for both exit types.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. TRAIL (trading_runtime.py:1079-1083) and STOP_LOSS (:1126-1130) place the protective child inline with only `if trail_trade:`/`if sl_trade:` — no else, no rollback — then fall through to `return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)` at :1151. The BRACKET path (:1006,:1027) correctly cancels the entry and returns fail. The None case is real: `ibreactive.py:431` returns rx.throw when placeOrder yields None, and `executioner.py:98` catches placement exceptions into rx.throw, so `on_error` fires leaving the child None. Entry is transmit=False (:1036,:1087); nothing transmits on that branch and the staged parent is never cancelled. `sdk.approve` (sdk.py:1412-1419) then marks the proposal EXECUTED on is_success(). High: violates the documented all-or-nothing guarantee for two exit types, yielding a falsely-EXECUTED proposal with no live protection — a capital-safety/integrity defect, though the on_error branch itself leaves no transmitted exposure.


### [x] HIGH — Risk gate daily-loss and position-concentration limits are dead code — no caller ever passes daily_pnl or portfolio/position value

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:939`  ·  _reviewer: architecture_

- **Mechanism:** RiskGate.evaluate() checks daily_pnl < -max_daily_loss and position_value/portfolio_value > max_position_size_pct, but both production call sites — trading_runtime.place_expressive_order (line 939-942) and executioner.place_order (line 137-140) — call evaluate(signal=..., open_order_count=...) only, so daily_pnl defaults to 0.0 and portfolio/position values to 0. The daily-loss circuit breaker and concentration cap advertised in CLAUDE.md ('RiskGate — pre-trade risk limit enforcement (max position size, daily loss, ...)') can never trigger. Additionally, the signal-rate check counts EventType.SIGNAL rows for signal.source_name, but the manual/proposal paths use source_name 'manual'/'proposal' and nothing ever writes SIGNAL events for those names (only strategy_runtime writes SIGNAL), so the rate limit is also inert for the LLM proposal loop. The only live checks are max_open_orders, the instrument filter, and leverage.

- **Failure scenario:** Account is down $5,000 on the day (limit $1,000). An LLM proposes and approves five more trades in an hour; every one passes the risk gate because daily_pnl is hard-coded 0.0 and no SIGNAL events exist for 'proposal'. The intended loss circuit breaker never fires on a live account.

- **Suggested fix:** Wire real inputs at the call sites: pull dailyPnL from the pnl cache / account values and pass portfolio_value + estimated position_value into evaluate(); either write SIGNAL events on the proposal path or count ORDER_SUBMITTED for the rate limit. Add a regression test asserting the daily-loss branch can actually reject.

- **Verifier:** Both production call sites of RiskGate.evaluate() — trading_runtime.py:939-942 (approve/place path) and executioner.py:137-140 (manual buy/sell) — pass only signal + open_order_count. So daily_pnl defaults to 0.0 (risk_gate.py:42), and the daily-loss branch `daily_pnl < -max_daily_loss` (risk_gate.py:54) is unreachable (0 < -1000 is false). Concentration is guarded by `portfolio_value > 0 and position_value > 0` (line 61), both default 0, so it never runs. The signal-rate check counts EventType.SIGNAL by source_name, but SIGNAL rows are written only for real strategy names (strategy_runtime.py:258), never for 'proposal'/'manual', so it always sees 0. grep confirms only these two evaluate() call sites exist. Partial mitigation: position_sizing.py:320 has its own daily-loss cap, but only on the auto-sized propose path (sdk.py:1093, skipped when explicit qty/amount) and it caps size rather than gating at approve time. The advertised RiskGate circuit breaker/concentration cap are effectively dead code. High severity: a non-firing daily-loss stop on a live account is a capital-safety gap.


### [x] HIGH — STOP_LOSS and TRAILING_STOP exits: protective-leg failure is not rolled back and still returns success

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:1129`  ·  _reviewer: wrong-thing_

- **Mechanism:** place_expressive_order's BRACKET path carefully rolls back staged legs on failure (lines 1001-1031), but the STOP_LOSS path (lines 1126-1130) and TRAILING_STOP path (lines 1079-1083) do the opposite: after staging the entry with transmit=False, if the protective leg's placement fails (`if sl_trade:` / `if trail_trade:` with no else), the code neither cancels the staged entry nor returns failure — it falls through to `return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)` at line 1151 with only the entry in the list. The SDK's approve then marks the proposal EXECUTED (sdk.py:1412-1419). The staged, untransmitted entry order lingers at the Gateway with no protective sibling; nothing in MMR tracks or cancels it.

- **Failure scenario:** `propose NVDA BUY --market --stop-loss 800` approved; the STP leg placement throws (e.g. transient socket error in subscribe_place_order_direct -> on_error fires, sl_trade stays None). Result: proposal recorded EXECUTED with one order_id, LLM loop believes it holds NVDA with a stop. In reality either no position exists (entry never transmitted — silent no-trade) or, if the staged entry later gets transmitted (manually via TWS or a subsequent same-parent transmit), a live position exists with NO stop-loss.

- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the BRACKET logic: on protective-leg failure, _cancel_trade_safely(entry_trade) and return SuccessFail.fail so the proposal transitions to FAILED instead of EXECUTED.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. In trading_runtime.py the BRACKET branch rolls back on protective-leg failure (lines 1006-1009, 1027-1031), but STOP_LOSS (lines 1126-1130) and TRAILING_STOP (lines 1079-1083) use `if sl_trade:`/`if trail_trade:` with no else. Their `on_error=lambda e: sl_task.set()` sets the event WITHOUT setting the trade var, so on placement failure the var stays None, nothing is appended, and control falls through to `return SuccessFail.success(obj=trades)` at line 1151 with only the entry. Since the entry is staged transmit=False and the protective leg carries transmit=True, a failed protective leg yields either a lingering untransmitted entry (no trade) or a naked position. sdk.py:1412-1419 then sees `is_success()`==True and marks the proposal EXECUTED. No compensating guard exists. Severity high: false EXECUTED status plus potential naked/absent position is a capital-safety divergence, though the trigger (placement failure) is low-frequency.


### [x] HIGH — Risk gate daily-loss and concentration limits are dead code — no caller ever passes daily_pnl or portfolio_value

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:939`  ·  _reviewer: wrong-thing_

- **Mechanism:** RiskGate.evaluate (risk_gate.py:38-83) gates on daily_pnl < -max_daily_loss and position concentration, but both defaults are 0.0 and both call sites pass only open_order_count: trading_runtime.py:939-941 (place_expressive_order, i.e. every approved proposal) and executioner.py:137-139 (place_order path for direct buy/sell). So the advertised 'daily loss' and 'max position size' pre-trade limits (RiskLimits.max_daily_loss=1000.0, max_position_size_pct=0.10; CLAUDE.md: 'Risk gate enforces pre-trade risk limits (max position size, daily loss...)') can never block a trade. The only daily-loss brake left is the position sizer's soft check at propose time, which applies only to auto-sized proposals and not to quantity-specified proposals or direct buy/sell.

- **Failure scenario:** Account is down $5,000 on the day (5x the configured $1,000 daily-loss limit). An LLM-generated proposal with explicit --quantity is approved: risk_gate.evaluate receives daily_pnl=0.0, approves, and the trade executes. The documented capital-preservation circuit breaker never fires on any execution path.

- **Suggested fix:** Wire real values at the call sites: compute daily P&L from self.pnl / event store and position/portfolio value from ib.portfolio() before calling evaluate; add a test asserting a trade is rejected when daily loss exceeds the limit.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. RiskGate.evaluate gates on daily_pnl (risk_gate.py:54) and concentration (risk_gate.py:61), both defaulting to 0.0. The only two production callers pass just open_order_count: trading_runtime.py:939-942 (place_expressive_order — every approved proposal) and executioner.py:137-140 (direct buy/sell). A grep confirms daily_pnl=/portfolio_value=/position_value= are supplied ONLY in tests/test_risk_gate.py, never in trader/. So with -5000 daily P&L, an explicit-quantity approved proposal receives daily_pnl=0.0 and passes. The documented daily-loss and max-position-size pre-trade limits are genuinely dead code on all execution paths; the leverage/margin (check_leverage) and signal-rate/open-order limits do work, and the position sizer has a soft daily-loss check only for auto-sized proposals. Severity high, not medium: for a live-money system a non-functioning capital-preservation circuit breaker is a material safety gap, even if latency is irrelevant.


## Material design findings


### [ ] CRITICAL — Crashed trader_service is never restarted; container stays 'up' with trading dead

- **Location:** `start_mmr.sh:1013`  ·  _reviewer: ops_

- **Mechanism:** The shipped Docker path is docker-entrypoint.sh -> exec start_mmr.sh, which launches data/trader/strategy/web as bare background children and enters a monitor loop (lines 997-1020) that only PRINTS a death notice and clears the PID. There is no restart of individual services, and the script exits (allowing docker-compose 'restart: on-failure' to fire) only when data_service AND trader_service AND strategy_service are all dead (line 1013). pycron — the component that owns restart_if_finished supervision per pycron.yaml — is never launched by any shipped code path (grep of start_mmr.sh, docker.sh, docker-entrypoint.sh, Dockerfile shows zero pycron invocations; CLAUDE.md's 'pycron: process manager for all services' and 'start_mmr.sh --no-tmux runs pycron' describe a launcher that no longer exists). Additionally the death report is wrong: 'wait "$pid" 2>/dev/null \|\| true; EXIT_CODE=$?' captures the exit status of '\|\| true', so every death is reported as 'exited with code 0'.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service hits an unhandled exception (e.g. IB Gateway nightly restart race) at 10:00 on a trading day and exits. strategy_service and data_service keep running, so the container never exits and Docker's restart policy never triggers. From then on: strategy signals cannot execute, approve/portfolio/orders RPCs time out, protective-order management (resize, bracket re-creation) is dead, and live positions in account U26774889 sit unmanaged indefinitely until a human notices — on a real-money system.

- **Suggested fix:** Either actually launch pycron (which has restart logic) as the in-container supervisor, or make start_mmr.sh restart a dead service (with capped backoff), or at minimum exit non-zero when trader_service alone dies so 'restart: on-failure' recycles the container. Also move EXIT_CODE capture before '\|\| true'.

- **Materiality:** Verified and the strongest finding. The shipped monitor loop only prints a death notice and clears the PID; it exits (letting Docker's on-failure restart fire) only when data AND trader AND strategy are all dead, so a lone trader_service crash leaves the container 'up' with trading dead indefinitely — signals can't execute, approve/orders/portfolio RPCs time out, protective-order management is dead, live positions sit unmanaged. Grep confirms pycron (the component with restart logic) is never launched by any shipped path. Also confirmed the EXIT_CODE=$? bug: it captures the status of `\|\| true`, so every death reports 'code 0'. For a real-money system this is a capital-safety hole.


### [ ] HIGH — Loop safety rails (max_proposals_per_cycle, auto_approve, daily_pnl_alert_pct, risk_hhi_warning) exist in config/docs but are never enforced in code

- **Location:** `skills/mmr-loop-skill/scripts/loop_engine.py:173`  ·  _reviewer: llm-loop_

- **Mechanism:** DEFAULT_CONFIG advertises hard-sounding limits, and SKILL.md lists 'Safety Boundaries' ('NEVER auto-executes', 'Stops proposing at the limit'), but none are implemented: _state['proposals_this_cycle'] is reset at line 173 and never incremented or checked anywhere; 'auto_approve' is never read by any code path; 'daily_pnl_alert_pct' and 'risk_hhi_warning' are never compared against anything. max_proposals_per_cycle only appears as interpolated prompt text ('max 2 this cycle'), and nothing prevents the LLM from calling MMRHelpers.approve() inside a cycle — the 'proposals, not trades' boundary is purely the absence of an approve instruction in the prompt. For a system driving a live account via a stochastic LLM, every rail is one hallucinated or context-compacted turn away from not existing.

- **Failure scenario:** During a volatile session the momentum scan returns 10 high-score ideas. A context-compacted LLM (the DIGEST phase aggressively compacts every cycle) misremembers the limit and calls propose() ten times, then 'helpfully' calls approve() on each since nothing in code blocks it and auto_approve=False gates nothing. Ten market orders hit the live account in one cycle; the only backstop left is the separate risk gate's per-trade checks.

- **Suggested fix:** Enforce the limits in code: increment proposals_this_cycle inside a propose wrapper and refuse (return an error dict) beyond max_proposals_per_cycle; have the loop expose a gated approve wrapper that hard-refuses unless auto_approve is True AND the proposal is user-confirmed; check daily_pnl against daily_pnl_alert_pct in _loop_hook and inject an alert/stop.

- **Materiality:** Verified by grep: proposals_this_cycle is reset at line 173 and never incremented or checked; auto_approve, daily_pnl_alert_pct, risk_hhi_warning appear only in DEFAULT_CONFIG and never in any code path; max_proposals_per_cycle only interpolates into prompt text. So every advertised 'Safety Boundary' is prompt-suggestion only, enforced by a stochastic, context-compacting LLM. For an autonomous loop driving live account U26774889 this is a real gap — the only hard backstop left is the separate per-trade risk_gate. Materially worth enforcing the rails in code; the trader_service risk gate keeps this from being catastrophic, hence high not critical.


### [ ] HIGH — skip_risk_gate is a caller-supplied RPC flag that simultaneously bypasses the proposal-approval gate, the trading filter, and the risk gate for arbitrary NEW orders

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/trader_service_api.py:84`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** place_order_simple treats skip_risk_gate=True as 'this is a liquidation' and waives the require_proposal_approval gate; the same flag is then forwarded to executioner.place_order where it also skips check_instrument (denylist/allowlist) and risk_gate.evaluate. Nothing server-side verifies the order actually reduces an existing position — the semantics rest entirely on the honesty of the RPC caller. The whole point of require_proposal_approval (per the code comment: 'Defensive gate against LLM loops drifting off-plan') is defeated by a single boolean any client can set, and it removes the denylist too, which liquidation does not require.

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM agent loop drifts off-plan and calls the buy RPC with skip_risk_gate=True (it has seen the flag in close-all code paths / error messages that literally instruct 'Set skip_risk_gate=True'). A brand-new BUY in a denylisted symbol executes on the live account with no proposal, no filter, and no risk gate.

- **Suggested fix:** Split the concerns: a separate 'liquidation' path that server-side verifies the order's action/quantity reduces an existing position (and still applies the denylist), rather than a caller-asserted bypass flag.

- **Materiality:** Verified and this is the strongest finding. A single caller-supplied boolean (skip_risk_gate) simultaneously waives require_proposal_approval (trader_service_api.py:84), check_instrument/denylist and risk_gate.evaluate (executioner.py:110/128), with nothing server-side confirming the order actually reduces a position. The rejection message literally coaches callers to 'Set skip_risk_gate=True'. In an explicitly LLM-driven live-money loop, this defeats the exact defensive gate its own comment says it exists for, and needlessly drops the denylist too (liquidation doesn't need that). Highest capital-safety impact in the batch; the split-out liquidation path that server-side verifies position-reduction is the right fix.


### [ ] HIGH — Proposals never expire and `approve --all` executes arbitrarily stale proposals with no freshness check or confirmation

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:2538`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** The proposal state machine defines EXPIRED, but `grep EXPIRED` shows nothing in the codebase ever sets it — PENDING proposals live forever. `_handle_approve(--all)` loops over every PENDING proposal and executes each via mmr.approve() with no confirmation prompt (unlike `close`/`close-all`, which require y/N). sdk.approve() (sdk.py:1352) does not check `created_at` age, does not re-validate the price snapshot, and for amount-based proposals recomputes quantity from the CURRENT price while executing bracket/stop prices frozen at proposal time.

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM session proposes `BUY AMD --bracket 180 150` when AMD trades at 165; the session ends without approving. Two weeks later AMD trades at 145. `mmr approve --all` (or approving the stale id) buys at market ~145 with a stop-loss at 150 that is ABOVE the market — the SL leg triggers immediately, or IB rejects the bracket leaving the entry unprotected. Every other stale PENDING proposal in the store executes in the same pass with no prompt.

- **Suggested fix:** Auto-transition PENDING proposals older than a configurable TTL (e.g. 1 trading day) to EXPIRED at query/approve time; have approve() compare current price to the stored snapshot and refuse (or require --force) beyond a drift threshold; add a y/N confirmation to `approve --all`.

- **Materiality:** Confirmed and materially dangerous for live money. EXPIRED is defined but never set anywhere, so PENDING proposals live forever. sdk.approve (sdk.py:1352+) does no created_at age check and no snapshot re-validation; for amount-based proposals it recomputes quantity from the CURRENT snapshot price while executing bracket/stop prices frozen at proposal time — exactly the stale-bracket inversion in the scenario (buy at 145 with a stop at 150 above market). _handle_approve(--all) (mmr_cli.py:2531) loops every PENDING proposal through _approve_one with no y/N prompt, unlike close-all. This is a direct capital-safety hole: add a TTL auto-expire, a price-drift refusal, and a confirmation on --all.


### [ ] HIGH — close-all-positions cancels ALL protective orders first, then continues past close failures, leaving naked positions

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:2813`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_close_all runs mmr.cancel_all() (which cancels every open order account-wide, including stops/trailing stops on positions and unrelated pending entries), then loops closing each position with skip_risk_gate=True. If cancel_all fails it merely prints a yellow warning and proceeds; if any individual close_position fails (RPC timeout, contract resolution miss, IB reject), it prints a red line and moves on. There is no rollback or re-protection: a position whose close failed now has no stop-loss, and no automated follow-up re-creates the cancelled protectives (contrast with execute_resize_plan, which re-creates them).
