### [ ] MEDIUM — Pairs strategy identifies which leg a price series belongs to by comparing series lengths — misattributes legs whenever tick rates differ

- **Location:** `strategies/pairs_zscore.py:48`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** on_prices receives a per-conid frame with no identity, so the strategy guesses the conid by 'which stored series is shorter than the incoming one' (lines 48-56) with a value-equality fallback (line 60). This is fuzzy matching on market data — exactly what CLAUDE.md's precision-over-convenience principle forbids. Whenever leg B ticks faster than leg A, a new B frame (len 7) exceeds A's stored length (5), so the loop assigns B's closes to conids[0]: the spread becomes log(B/B)≈0 and subsequent z-scores are computed on corrupted series. Separately, aligning the two legs by trailing index position (iloc[-n:], line 79) pairs prices from different wall-clock times because live tick counts are not synchronized across instruments — so even correctly-attributed series produce a wrong spread.

- **Failure scenario:** Live pair AAPL/ILLIQUID_STOCK: AAPL emits 10 ticks for every 1 of the other leg. Within seconds both stored series contain AAPL closes; the z-score collapses toward 0, then an eventual genuine tick for the illiquid leg produces a spurious \|z\|>2 spike and the strategy emits a BUY on a spread that never existed.

- **Suggested fix:** Pass conid identity into the strategy (e.g. add conId to the normalized frame or dispatch signature) and align legs by timestamp (merge_asof/resample) rather than trailing row index; fail loudly if identity is ambiguous.

- **Verifier:** Both premises verified. strategy_runtime.py:240-247 dispatches per-conId streams via strategy.on_prices(self.streams[conId]) with no conId passed (normalize_ticker yields only OHLCV), so the strategy must guess identity. pairs_zscore.py:49-56 guesses by length growth: iterating conids [A,B], the check `len(close) > len(_prices[A])` fires for any frame longer than A's stored length. Trace (A slow, B fast): once B accumulates >=2 bars, a B-frame overwrites _prices[A], making spread log(B/B)≈0, collapsing z; a later genuine A tick spikes \|z\|>2 and emits a spurious BUY — matching the reported scenario. self.conids is populated from context (strategy.py:96-102), so the path is reachable. Trailing-index alignment (line 79) separately mismatches timestamps. This is precisely the fuzzy market-data matching CLAUDE.md forbids. Kept at medium: the strategy is not wired into any strategy_runtime.yaml, so it only misbehaves if explicitly deployed, and it emits signals rather than directly placing orders.


### [x] MEDIUM — Empty-string env vars override valid YAML config in Container.resolve (IB_ACCOUNT='' bricks trader_service)

- **Location:** `trader/container.py:180`  ·  _reviewer: ops_

- **Mechanism:** Container.resolve uses 'os.getenv(param.name.upper()) is not None' — an empty string counts as set and wins over the config dict. docker-compose.yml unconditionally sets 'IB_ACCOUNT: ${IB_ACCOUNT:-}' and docker-entrypoint.sh writes 'export IB_ACCOUNT=""' into .mmr_env, so when IB_ACCOUNT is absent from .env every service sees IB_ACCOUNT=''. MMRConfig.from_yaml uses the opposite convention ('if not os.getenv("IB_ACCOUNT")' treats '' as unset) and correctly auto-resolves ib.account from ib_live_account/ib_paper_account, and container.py line 107 syncs that good value into configuration['ib_account'] — but resolve() then discards it because the empty env var takes precedence, and Trader.__init__ (trading_runtime.py:66) receives ib_account=''. The connect-time safety guard (trading_runtime.py:177) then refuses to start. Same latent hazard applies to every constructor param whose uppercased name collides with a set-but-empty env var.

- **Failure scenario:** User deletes IB_ACCOUNT from .env, following trader.yaml's documented 'Set ib_paper_account / ib_live_account in trader.yaml' path. In Docker, trader_service raises 'SAFETY: no ib_account configured' at every start despite a correctly configured trader.yaml, and (per the supervision finding) is never restarted — trading is down with a misleading diagnostic pointing at config that is actually fine.

- **Suggested fix:** Treat empty-string env vars as unset in Container.resolve (match MMRConfig's 'if not os.getenv' convention), or drop the ':-' defaults from docker-compose so unset host vars stay unset in the container.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. container.py:180 uses `os.getenv('IB_ACCOUNT') is not None`, so an empty-string env var counts as set and overrides the good config value that container.py:107 just synced from mmr_config.ib.account. config.py:187 uses the opposite convention (`if not os.getenv('IB_ACCOUNT')`) so it correctly auto-resolves ib.account from ib_paper_account/ib_live_account when the env is "". docker-entrypoint.sh:24 unconditionally exports IB_ACCOUNT="${IB_ACCOUNT:-}" (also docker-compose.yml:70) and sources it before launching services, so every service sees IB_ACCOUNT="" whenever it's absent from .env. Result: Trader.__init__ gets ib_account='' and trading_runtime.py:177 raises AccountNotPinnedError despite valid trader.yaml. Severity medium not higher: this is fail-safe (refuses to start, never mis-routes an order to the wrong/default account), so capital is protected; impact is availability plus a misleading diagnostic, and the error text itself names IB_ACCOUNT as a workaround.


### [x] MEDIUM — DateRange default with dt.datetime.now() is frozen at import time, causing write_resolve_overlap to silently delete bars written after process start in long-lived processes

- **Location:** `trader/data/data_access.py:526`  ·  _reviewer: stores_

- **Mechanism:** `TickData.read` (line 526) and `Data.read` (line 375) declare `date_range: DateRange = DateRange(dt.datetime(1970,1,1), dt.datetime.now())` — the `now()` is evaluated once at module import. `write_resolve_overlap` (line 507) calls `self.read(contract)` with this default, so in a long-lived process (the interactive mmr REPL kept open for days, or the market_data.subscribe_security backfill path in trader_service) the merge reads only bars dated before process start. Bars dated after import time are excluded from the merge, but DuckDBDataStore.write() then DELETEs the full [min,max] span of the merged frame for that bar_size — deleting those excluded rows without re-inserting them.

- **Failure scenario:** An mmr REPL is opened Monday and left running. The daily data-refresh cron writes Tue/Wed daily bars from separate processes. On Friday the user runs `history massive --prev_days 1` in the REPL: the merge reads bars only up to Monday, the merged frame spans [old_min..Friday], and write() deletes Tue/Wed bars in that span without re-inserting them — silent loss of two days of daily bars, later 'fixed' only by chance re-downloads. Any strategy/backtest reading in between sees a gap or trades on incomplete history.

- **Suggested fix:** Make the default `date_range=None` and compute `DateRange(dt.datetime(1970,1,1), dt.datetime.now())` inside the function body at call time.

- **Verifier:** The core claim is correct Python semantics: the default `DateRange(dt.datetime(1970,1,1), dt.datetime.now())` at data_access.py:526 is evaluated once at import, freezing `end` to process-start. `write_resolve_overlap` (line 507) reads with that frozen default; because a DateRange is truthy, `get_data` (line 553) uses it verbatim, capping the read at import time. The merged frame therefore omits bars written by other processes after start, and duckdb_store.py:261-284 DELETEs the full [min,max] span (per bar_size) then re-inserts only the merged frame — silently dropping the omitted intermediate bars. The REPL loop (mmr_cli.py:9946) supplies the long-lived process, and a narrow-window `history` download supplies the incomplete data_frame. Confirmed end-to-end. Severity is medium, not high: it corrupts historical bars (strategies/backtests read stale gaps) rather than mispricing a live order, and requires a days-open REPL plus concurrent cron writes plus a narrow refetch — a real but conditional combination. The market_data.py:230 backfill path is mostly self-covering.


### [x] MEDIUM — TickData.missing() cannot detect interior gaps — resample('D') includes empty bins, so holes between first and last stored bar are permanent

- **Location:** `trader/data/data_access.py:621`  ·  _reviewer: history-workers_

- **Mechanism:** missing() builds the set of covered dates via `df.resample('D').first().index.date`. Pandas resample produces a bin for every calendar day between the frame's min and max timestamps, including empty bins (verified: a frame with bars on Jun 1, 2 and 8 yields dates Jun 1-8). Every session between the first and last stored bar therefore appears covered regardless of whether any data exists on it. Since missing() drives all incremental refresh (data_service.pull_massive/pull_twelvedata/pull_ib and mmr_cli's data download/refresh freshness guard), any interior hole — a swallowed TwelveData chunk failure, a partially failed multi-range download, manually deleted rows — is never re-fetched. Only gaps strictly before the first or after the last stored bar are detected.

- **Failure scenario:** TwelveData 429s on the chunk covering days 10-15 of a 30-day 1-min download (twelvedata_history logs and skips it); the partial frame is written and the job reports completed. Every subsequent `mmr data refresh` calls missing(), which reports zero missing ranges because resample bridges the hole. A backtest over the window silently trains and fills across a 5-day void; the composite score and confidence stats are computed on a truncated trade set with no warning.

- **Suggested fix:** Drop empty bins before extracting dates, e.g. `df.resample('D').first().dropna(how='all').index.date`, or compare per-session row counts against the calendar.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed. data_access.py:621 builds covered dates via `df.resample('D').first().index.date` with no dropna. Runtime check proves resample emits a bin (date) for EVERY calendar day between min and max, including empty interior bins (bars on Jun 1,2,8 yield Jun 1-8). The gap loop (632-643) only emits ranges for sessions `not in dates`, so interior holes are permanently invisible. missing() feeds all incremental refresh (data_service.py:263/339/413, mmr_cli.py:7385, market_data.py:214, strategy_runtime.py:550), so a swallowed chunk failure or deleted rows is never re-fetched; only pre-first/post-last gaps are caught. Severity medium not high: it silently corrupts the OHLCV foundation for backtests and defeats incremental refresh, but does not directly mis-execute a live order — harm is indirect (backtest confidence/deploy decisions computed on holey data) and requires an interior hole to actually form.


### [x] MEDIUM — Upsert DELETE + INSERT is not wrapped in a transaction — a crash between them permanently destroys the deleted range

- **Location:** `trader/data/duckdb_store.py:265`  ·  _reviewer: data-access_

- **Mechanism:** DuckDBDataStore.write() implements upsert as DELETE-then-INSERT inside execute_atomic(). execute_atomic only shares a connection under a lock; it never issues BEGIN/COMMIT, and the DuckDB Python API autocommits each statement (verified empirically: closing the connection after the DELETE and before the INSERT leaves the table emptied and durable). If the process dies between the two statements (SIGKILL, OOM — the container runs with hard memory limits, or Ctrl-C during a refresh), the deleted rows are gone and nothing is reinserted. Because write_resolve_overlap merges the FULL existing history into the frame it writes back, the DELETE range routinely spans the symbol's entire history for that bar_size — so the blast radius is 'every bar this symbol has', not just the refreshed window. The same non-transactional pattern also affects INSERT failures (e.g. a type-cast error aborts after the DELETE already committed).

- **Failure scenario:** User Ctrl-C's (or the OOM killer hits) `mmr data refresh --all` at the instant a symbol's write_resolve_overlap is between DELETE and INSERT. Years of AAPL daily history vanish from mmr_history.duckdb with no error logged. Subsequent backtests/strategy warm-ups run on an empty or truncated dataset; missing() then triggers a giant refetch, or worse, strategies start with too-short warm-up windows.

- **Suggested fix:** Wrap _write in an explicit transaction: conn.execute('BEGIN TRANSACTION') ... conn.execute('COMMIT') with rollback on exception (or conn.begin()/commit()), and do the same for other multi-statement execute_atomic bodies.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. execute_atomic (duckdb_store.py:70-121) has no BEGIN/COMMIT (grep confirms none anywhere in the file); DuckDB autocommits each statement. _write (lines 265-286) commits the DELETE, then separately runs INSERT, so a death between them leaves the DELETE durable and nothing reinserted. write_resolve_overlap (data_access.py:507-522) reads the full existing history and rewrites it, making min_date/max_date (261-262) span the symbol's entire history for that bar_size — confirming the "wipes everything" blast radius. Ctrl-C during `mmr data refresh` (KeyboardInterrupt between the two execute calls) or OOM/SIGKILL is a real trigger. Severity lowered to medium: this is a re-downloadable OHLCV cache (missing() refetches), not order/position/capital state, so no direct capital loss; the crash window is narrow. Still a genuine non-transactional-upsert bug worth the suggested BEGIN/COMMIT fix.


### [ ] MEDIUM — Resolver cache is never invalidated and its hit path bypasses exchange/sec_type filters due to an operator-precedence bug

- **Location:** `trader/data/universe.py:145`  ·  _reviewer: stores_

- **Mechanism:** Two defects in `resolve_universe`'s `_resolver_cache` hit path. (1) Precedence: `if check_exchange(exchange, definition) and not universe or universe == u.name:` parses as `(A and B) or C`, so when a universe name is supplied and matches the cached entry, the exchange check is skipped entirely; and `check_sec_type` is never consulted on the cache path at all, so a sec_type filter is silently ignored on cache hits. (2) Staleness: the cache is populated on every successful resolve but never cleared by `update()`, `insert()`, or `delete()`, so a long-running trader_service keeps serving a SecurityDefinition that has been removed or corrected in the DB until restart. Per CLAUDE.md, a conId that is no longer locally registered must fail loudly, not resolve from a stale cache.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator finds a symbol registered with the wrong exchange/primaryExchange (e.g. NYSE ADR instead of ASX listing), runs `universe remove` + `universe add` to fix it. trader_service's resolve_symbol RPC — used by the CLI buy/propose path to build the order contract — keeps returning the cached old definition, and the next order routes to the wrong exchange/currency. Deleted conIds likewise keep resolving instead of erroring.

- **Suggested fix:** Parenthesize as `A and (not universe or universe == u.name)`, add the sec_type check to the cache path, and clear `_resolver_cache` in update()/insert()/delete() (or drop the cache — scans over a few hundred definitions are cheap at this scale).

- **Verifier:** Both defects verified in code. Precedence: universe.py:145 `check_exchange(...) and not universe or universe == u.name` parses as `(A and not universe) or (universe==u.name)` (Python: `and` > `or`), so a matching universe name bypasses the exchange filter, and check_sec_type is never called on the cache path. Staleness: `_resolver_cache` is populated (lines 162/172/181) but grep confirms no invalidation in update()/insert()/delete() (lines 211-220). trading_runtime.py:217 keeps a persistent accessor for trader_service's lifetime; non-cache reads hit DuckDB live (get()→library.read), so the never-cleared cache masks cross-process universe corrections that would otherwise be visible. resolve_symbol RPC feeds _to_contract (sdk.py:584) for order routing, giving an end-to-end wrong-contract path. Severity medium, not high: the precedence trigger needs int conId + matching universe + mismatching exchange (and sec_type isn't even passed at trading_runtime.py:648-652), and staleness requires a same-conId fix during uptime after that conId was cached.


### [ ] MEDIUM — IB daily bars are timestamped at UTC midnight then converted to exchange tz, shifting every daily bar to the previous calendar day

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ib_history_worker.py:287`  ·  _reviewer: history-workers_

- **Mechanism:** For '1 day' bars with formatDate=2, ib_async returns the bar date as a datetime.date. The code detects this (`type(df_result.index[0]) is date`) and sets utc=True, making pd.to_datetime place the bar at 00:00 UTC of the session date; the following tz_convert(tz_info) (default 'US/Eastern' — data_service never passes the security's timezone) moves it to 19:00/20:00 of the PREVIOUS day. TickData reads always convert to America/New_York, so every IB-sourced daily bar is attributed to the prior calendar date by anything that groups by day: missing() compares these shifted dates against exchange-calendar sessions (the newest session always looks missing, forcing a re-download every run — which, via the asyncio.run reuse bug, is what triggers the NaN poisoning on every ASX cron run), and backtest windows / freshness checks are off by one day. This also makes IB daily rows inconsistent with TwelveData/Massive daily rows for the same symbol, which are stored at exchange-tz midnight.

- **Failure scenario:** ASX daily refresh stores BHP's Friday session bar at Thursday 19:00 America/New_York. `mmr data query BHP --days N` and backtests attribute Friday's close to Thursday; missing() reports Friday absent on every run and re-downloads it daily even when fully covered.

- **Suggested fix:** For date-typed daily bars, localize to the exchange timezone at session midnight (tz_localize(tz_info)) instead of utc=True + tz_convert, and pass the security's timeZoneId from data_service instead of defaulting to US/Eastern.

- **Verifier:** Mechanism verified in code. ib_async 2.1.0 `parseIBDatetime` returns `dt.date` for daily "YYYYmmdd" bars, so `type(df_result.index[0]) is date` is True (ib_history_worker.py:283-284), setting utc=True. `pd.to_datetime(..., utc=True)` places the session at 00:00 UTC, then `tz_convert(tz_info)` (line 291) with the US/Eastern default moves it to the prior calendar evening — I reproduced: session 2026-06-26 → 2026-06-25 20:00 Eastern, and after `resample('D').first().index.date` → 2026-06-25. data_service.py:201-208 never passes tz_info (uses default), so even ASX bars use US/Eastern. The read path re-converts to America/New_York (data_access.py:353) and missing() resamples by day (data_access.py:621), so the newest session always appears absent → re-download every run, and IB daily rows land one calendar day off Massive/TwelveData rows for the same symbol. Real defect. Severity medium, not high: the shift is uniform so an isolated backtest's OHLC sequence/P&L is intact; harm is data-integrity (cross-source day misalignment, freshness/missing off-by-one, redundant re-downloads) rather than direct mis-execution of a live order.


### [ ] MEDIUM — MultithreadedTopicPubSub.start() and MessageBusServer.start() hang forever if the background thread dies on bind failure

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:954`  ·  _reviewer: messaging_

- **Mechanism:** MultithreadedTopicPubSub.start() spawns _publisher_loop in a thread and then blocks on self.wait_handle.wait() with no timeout. wait_handle is only set inside main() after the bind succeeds; if zmq_publisher.bind() raises (port already in use — e.g. a stale process from an unclean restart still holds 42002), _publisher_loop re-raises inside the thread and dies without ever setting the event, so start() blocks forever. MessageBusServer.start() (line 688) has the identical pattern — and it is an `async def` calling the blocking threading.Event.wait(), so it freezes the whole trader_service event loop, not just one call. Both are invoked from Trader.connect() (trading_runtime.py:252-255), so a bind conflict turns startup into a silent hang instead of a loud error.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service crashes uncleanly and pycron restarts it while the old process still holds port 42002. The new process passes IB account verification, then MultithreadedTopicPubSub._publisher_loop dies on 'Address already in use'; start() waits forever on the event. The service never binds its RPC port, all CLI/strategy_service calls time out, and there is no error in the logs pointing at the port conflict.

- **Suggested fix:** Have the thread set the event in a finally block (or store the exception on the handle) and make start() use wait(timeout=...) and re-raise the captured bind error.

- **Verifier:** The hang is real. In MultithreadedTopicPubSub._publisher_loop, the PUB bind at clientserver.py:924 is inside a try that re-raises (925-927), and wait_handle.set() only runs at line 932 after a successful bind; start() (line 954) waits with no timeout, so a bind failure kills the thread and hangs forever. MessageBusServer.__combined_loop binds at line 636 before wait_handle.set() at 640 with no guard; the exception exits run_until_complete (674) and the thread dies, so start() (688) blocks on a blocking threading.Event.wait() inside an async def, stalling the event loop. Both are reached from Trader.connect() (trading_runtime.py:252,255). A live process holding 42002/42006 gives EADDRINUSE. One correction: it is NOT silent — line 926 does logging.exception(e) naming the bind error. Severity re-rated to medium: it fails closed (no orders placed, IB-side stops still resting), so it is an availability/operability outage needing a manual kill, not a capital-loss path.


### [x] MEDIUM — place_order_simple silently converts any action string not containing 'BUY' into a SELL order

- **Location:** `trader/messaging/trader_service_api.py:97`  ·  _reviewer: messaging_

- **Mechanism:** `act = Action.BUY if 'BUY' in action else Action.SELL` uses a case-sensitive substring test with SELL as the catch-all default. A caller sending 'buy', 'Buy', a typo, or any unexpected token gets a SELL order with no error — the opposite side of the intended trade. This violates the fail-loudly principle in an API explicitly exposed to LLM-driven callers over RPC, where non-canonical strings are a realistic input. (Contrast with place_expressive_order, which at least passes the raw string to IB where an invalid action is rejected.)

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM or script calls place_order_simple with action='Buy' (title case) for 100 shares of AMD. 'BUY' is not a substring of 'Buy', so the gate maps it to Action.SELL and the service opens a 100-share short instead of a long, on the live account.

- **Suggested fix:** Normalize and validate: `action = action.upper()`; raise ValueError (returned as SuccessFail.fail) unless action is exactly 'BUY' or 'SELL'.

- **Verifier:** Code matches the finding. trader/messaging/trader_service_api.py:97 does `act = Action.BUY if 'BUY' in action else Action.SELL` — case-sensitive substring with SELL default; Action (objects.py:10) has no normalization, and trader.place_order_simple (trading_runtime.py:1233) gets an already-decided enum, so no downstream guard. The RPC and the public SDK method sdk.py:706 both accept `action: str` with no uppercasing/validation and forward it directly, and this RPC is documented as LLM/script-facing. A caller passing 'Buy'/'buy'/typo intending a long silently opens a short. Caveat: every in-repo caller (commands.py:1225, sdk.py:1488 close, resize) passes canonical uppercase strings, so no existing internal path triggers it — it requires a non-canonical external caller. Latent but real; wrong-side live order justifies medium given capital-safety weighting.


### [ ] MEDIUM — `strategies backtest` silently ignores the deployed strategy's params and drops trade persistence

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:4129`  ·  _reviewer: cli-2_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_strategy_backtest builds a synthetic argparse.Namespace containing only strategy/class_name/conids/universe/days/capital/bar_size, then calls _handle_backtest. It never copies found.get('params') from strategy_runtime.yaml into the namespace, so the backtest runs with the strategy class's default tunables instead of the params the deployed strategy actually trades with (strategy_runtime.py passes params=strategy_config.get('params', {}) to the live instance). Additionally, the namespace lacks 'save_trades', so _handle_backtest's getattr(args, 'save_trades', False) at line 6903 evaluates False — the run is persisted with empty trades_json/equity_curve_json, disabling the entire statistical-confidence block, contrary to the documented 'persisted by default' behaviour on the real backtest command (argparse default save_trades=True at line 1357).

- **Failure scenario:** User deploys a sweep winner with `strategies deploy orb_gld --params '{"RANGE_MINUTES": 45}'` (default is 15), then validates it with `mmr strategies backtest orb_gld`. The backtest silently runs RANGE_MINUTES=15, reports metrics for a strategy that is not the one trading live, and persists a run row with no trades blob so `backtests show`/`confidence` can't compute PSR/t-test. The user keeps (or kills) a live strategy based on results for a different configuration.

- **Suggested fix:** Copy found.get('params', {}) into bt_args (e.g. as the JSON 'params' field), and set save_trades=True / include the other backtest defaults explicitly so the synthetic namespace matches the real parser's defaults.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. `_handle_strategy_backtest` (mmr_cli.py:4129-4137) builds a Namespace omitting `params`/`param`/`save_trades`. `_handle_backtest` reads `getattr(args,'params',None)`/`getattr(args,'param',[])` (6816-6818), so no overrides apply and the run uses class defaults — but the deployed strategy's params ARE written to YAML (`params:` field, 3901-3914) and consumed live via `strategy_config.get('params',{})` (strategy_runtime.py:428). Separately, `getattr(args,'save_trades',False)` at 6903 yields False (empty trades_json/equity_curve_json) while `no_save` absent means the run is still persisted (6889), contradicting the real parser default `save_trades=True` (1357). The `default True` at 6617 is in the unrelated `_handle_backtest_sweep`. Severity medium: it corrupts the human keep/kill decision on a live strategy and disables PSR/t-test confidence, but does not itself place wrong orders.


### [x] MEDIUM — data download --source ib hangs forever on the second fetch: cached IB connection is bound to a closed event loop

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:7432`  ·  _reviewer: cli-3_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_data_download creates a single IBHistoryWorker (line 7298) and then calls asyncio.run(worker.get_contract_history(...)) once per (symbol, missing-range) inside the download loop (line 7432). The first asyncio.run creates loop A; get_contract_history sees self.connected=False and calls connect_async(), binding the ib_async socket transport/protocol to loop A. asyncio.run then closes loop A, but IBHistoryWorker.connected stays True and ib_client.isConnected() still returns True. The next asyncio.run creates loop B; get_contract_history skips reconnect and calls reqHistoricalDataAsync, whose wrapper.startReq creates an asyncio.Future() bound to loop B (verified in ib_async 2.1.0 wrapper.py:370). Incoming socket data can only be dispatched by loop A's selector, which is closed and never runs again, so the future never resolves and the await blocks indefinitely (ib_async has no default request timeout). This is the exact code path used by the cron-driven `data refresh` for non-US universes (source auto-detects to 'ib' for ASX).

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr data download BHP CBA --source ib` (or the nightly `data refresh` job for an ASX universe with 2+ stale symbols): BHP downloads fine in loop A; CBA's asyncio.run enters loop B, reqHistoricalDataAsync awaits a future that can never be completed, and the CLI/cron process hangs forever. ASX data silently stops refreshing, the IB client-id slot stays occupied, and subsequent scheduled refreshes pile up behind the hung process — leading to stale international data feeding scans/backtests/ATR sizing.

- **Suggested fix:** Do all ranges/symbols inside one asyncio.run (e.g. an async helper that connects once and iterates), or reset worker.connected and recreate/reconnect the IB client per asyncio.run call, or use worker.connect()/synchronous API with ib_async's own loop instead of nested asyncio.run calls.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. mmr_cli.py:7298 builds one IBHistoryWorker; 7432 calls asyncio.run(worker.get_contract_history) per (symbol,range), each a fresh loop. ib_history_worker.py:179 skips reconnect while self.connected stays True, and 189 passes because ib_async isConnected reflects connState/_apiReady (client.py:141, ib.py:412), never reset when asyncio.run closes loop A. The transport is bound to loop A (util.getLoop → get_running_loop). On the 2nd asyncio.run (loop B), wrapper.py:375 creates asyncio.Future() on loop B; the socket reader lives only on closed loop A, so the future never resolves and the await hangs (no ib_async timeout). Small request writes succeed via raw sock.send, so it hangs rather than erroring. _handle_data_refresh (7724) feeds all universe symbols to one _handle_data_download, so a 2+ symbol ASX (source auto→ib) job hangs on symbol 2. Real bug, but impact is a hung process + stale international data, not wrong trades or capital loss; US/twelvedata path unaffected — medium, not high.


### [x] MEDIUM — data refresh marks every job success=True even when all downloads fail (fail-loudly violation on the cron path)

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:7725`  ·  _reviewer: cli-3_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_data_refresh appends {'job': ..., 'success': True} whenever the inner _handle_data_download call returns without raising. But _handle_data_download never raises on failure: it early-returns (print_status + return) when the API key or duckdb_path is missing, and it swallows every per-symbol/per-range download exception into a printed `failed` counter (lines 7450-7461) that the refresh wrapper never sees — the wrapper even forces _json_mode=False, discarding the download's own {'success': failed==0} JSON summary. The final batch output is {'success': true, 'ok': N, 'failed': 0} regardless of how many symbols actually failed.

- **Failure scenario:** TwelveData API key expires (or the provider rate-limits every call). The nightly pycron `data refresh --all` run downloads 0 rows for every symbol in every job, yet emits {"success": true, "ok": 2, "failed": 0}. Nothing alerts; local OHLCV silently goes stale until someone happens to run `data status` or a sweep freshness guard trips days later — meanwhile backtests, idea scans and ATR-based position sizing consume increasingly stale data.

- **Suggested fix:** Have _handle_data_download return its (completed, skipped, failed) counts (or raise on failed>0 / config errors) and propagate them into each job's result so `success` reflects reality; make the top-level JSON `success` false when any job had failures.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. `_handle_data_download` (trader/mmr_cli.py:7213) returns None in all paths and never raises on failure: config errors early-return bare (7238/7243/7250/7254), and per-symbol download exceptions are caught at 7450-7461 and folded into a printed `failed` counter. The refresh wrapper (7717-7733) marks a job `success:True` whenever the call returns without raising (7725), and its only failure path is the `except` at 7731. It also forces `_json_mode=False` (7722), so the download's own `{'success': failed==0}` block (7480-7488) is suppressed and, being printed not returned, is invisible to the wrapper. Thus a fully-failed nightly `data refresh --all` (expired/rate-limited key) emits `{'success': true, 'ok': N, 'failed': 0}` (7738-7742) — a genuine fail-loudly violation. Medium, not high: no direct wrong-trade; secondary guards (`data status`, sweep `_freshness_check`) eventually catch staleness that feeds ATR sizing/backtests.


### [ ] MEDIUM — data migrate-symbols can create duplicate OHLCV bars — blind UPDATE re-keys string rows onto an existing conId key with no dedup

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:7568`  ·  _reviewer: cli-3_

- **Mechanism:** The migration runs `UPDATE tick_data SET symbol = <conid> WHERE symbol = <ticker>`. tick_data has no primary key or uniqueness constraint (duckdb_store.py:147 — plain CREATE TABLE with only a non-unique index), and DuckDBDataStore.read() returns rows verbatim ordered by date with no deduplication. If the same instrument was downloaded both before registration (string-keyed rows, e.g. 'JPM') and after registration (conId-keyed rows, e.g. '624888') over overlapping dates — a natural sequence given `data download` auto-registers resolutions in the 'downloads' universe — the UPDATE merges the string rows into the conId key, producing two rows per (date, bar_size). Per the project's own principle, wrong data is worse than no data: duplicated bars double volumes, distort ATR/rolling indicators, and make backtests process each bar twice.

- **Failure scenario:** User runs `data download JPM` while trader_service is down (rows stored under 'JPM'), later downloads JPM again after it resolves (rows stored under conId '624888' for the same year), then runs `mmr data migrate-symbols`. Every overlapping trading day now has two identical daily bars under conId 624888; a subsequent backtest on JPM sees ~504 bars/year, computes wrong indicator values and inflated trade counts, and position sizing computes ATR from corrupted series.

- **Suggested fix:** Before re-keying, delete string-keyed rows whose (date, bar_size) already exist under the conId (or use an INSERT ... SELECT with anti-join then DELETE), and/or add a uniqueness constraint on (symbol, date, bar_size) to tick_data.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. tick_data has no uniqueness constraint (duckdb_store.py:145-169, only a non-unique index). read() returns rows verbatim with no DISTINCT (duckdb_store.py:196-202). The two-key precondition really occurs: _handle_data_download stores under storage_key = conid if conid else symbol (mmr_cli.py:7447) — ticker-string keys when trader_service is down, conId keys when it's up, over overlapping dates. The migrate path (mmr_cli.py:7568-7573) issues a blind UPDATE tick_data SET symbol=? WHERE symbol=? with no delete/anti-join, unlike the normal write() upsert that deletes-then-inserts by symbol+date+bar_size (duckdb_store.py:265-288). So re-keyed string rows coexist with existing conId rows, yielding duplicate (date,bar_size) bars that corrupt backtests, ATR/rolling indicators, and ATR-based position sizing. Medium, not high: it corrupts stored history feeding sizing/backtests rather than directly placing a wrong order, and needs a specific download sequence plus the maintenance command.


### [x] MEDIUM — close_position does not clamp quantity to the position size — an over-sized close reverses the position into an unintended short/long

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1462`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** close_qty = abs(quantity) if quantity is not None else abs(pos_size); action is derived from the position sign. Nothing checks quantity <= abs(pos_size), and the CLI handler (_handle_close, mmr_cli.py:2774) passes args.quantity straight through with only a y/N confirm that displays the raw number. A 'close' command semantically means reduce-to-flat, but an over-quantity submits a market order for more shares than held, flipping the book through zero into a new short (or long for shorts). The risk gate does not catch this (concentration check is dead per the other finding), and there is no whatIf/position check on this path.

- **Failure scenario:** Position: long 100 AAPL. User (or LLM tool call) runs 'close 3 --quantity 1000' having misread the row. A market SELL 1000 is placed: the 100-share long closes and a naked 900-share short opens on the live account, with no protective orders.

- **Suggested fix:** Clamp close_qty to abs(pos_size) (or fail loudly when quantity > position size) in both sdk.close_position and the CLI handler.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end and confirmed. sdk.py:1462 does close_qty = abs(quantity) with no clamp to abs(pos_size); action comes only from position sign (1463). CLI _handle_close forwards args.quantity unmodified (mmr_cli.py:2774,2781), and --quantity is a first-class flag (514). Downstream there is no position-aware guard: place_order_simple builds a plain market order (trading_runtime.py:1233); the risk gate's concentration check is inert because evaluate() is called with default portfolio_value/position_value=0.0 (executioner.py:137-140) and the branch requires both >0 (risk_gate.py:61); sanity_check_order is a stub returning True (order_validator.py:35). So an oversize close submits a market order exceeding holdings, flipping long→short (or short→long) with no protective orders — for any broker allowing the reversal. Severity medium, not higher: it requires a deliberately oversize --quantity (default None safely closes the full position), and the interactive path has a y/N confirm showing the share count; the sdk/LLM path has no such gate.


### [x] MEDIUM — USD-denominated sized amount divided by local-currency price when converting to quantity — no FX conversion anywhere

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1394`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** The sizer computes amount_usd against USD limits (min/max_position_usd, max_position_pct of a USD NetLiquidation). At approve time, `qty = round(proposal.amount / price)` uses the IB snapshot price, which is quoted in the instrument's listing currency (AUD for `propose BHP --exchange ASX --currency AUD`, a documented flow). The same unit mixing exists inside PositionSizer.compute (position_sizing.py:344,405): the ADV cap `max_shares_by_adv * effective_price` and quantity `sized / qty_price` treat local-currency prices as USD. No FX rate is applied anywhere in the propose->approve pipeline (fx conversion helpers exist in sdk.py:3579 but are unused here).

- **Failure scenario:** propose BHP BUY --confidence 0.7 --exchange ASX --currency AUD auto-sizes $5,000 USD; approve computes qty = round(5000 / 45) = 111 shares costing A$5,000 ≈ US$3,300 — 34% under the intended size, and every USD cap was checked against the wrong notional. For an account whose base currency is weaker than the instrument currency (or a pence-quoted LSE listing) the same math over-buys, breaching max_position_usd/max_position_pct.

- **Suggested fix:** Convert the snapshot price to the account base currency (IB provides $LEDGER ExchangeRate values, already read in get_account_cash_by_currency) before dividing, or size non-base-currency proposals in local currency explicitly and record the FX rate in metadata.

- **Verifier:** The finding holds. At approve, sdk.py:1394 does `qty = round(proposal.amount / price)` where `proposal.amount` is `result.amount_usd` (sdk.py:1160-1161), derived from `net_liquidation * base_position_pct` clamped to USD limits (position_sizing.py:243-293), while `price` is the raw IB snapshot price in the contract's listing currency (get_snapshot at sdk.py:1376-1389). No FX conversion appears anywhere in the propose→approve path; `get_account_cash_by_currency` (sdk.py:2067) is unused here. The `--exchange ASX --currency AUD` flow is documented and passes through (propose signature sdk.py:1079, contract built at 1367-1370). For BHP: US$5,000 / A$45 = 111 shares ≈ US$3,300 (~34% under). The ADV cap (position_sizing.py:344) also mixes local price into a USD budget. Severity medium, not critical: the default US/USD path is correct, and international proposals typically *under*-size (soft miss); only pence-quoted or weaker-base cases over-buy and can breach max_position_usd/pct — a real but bounded capital-safety exposure confined to non-USD proposals.


### [x] MEDIUM — When the sizer blocks a trade (returns $0), the block reason and warnings are silently discarded and an unsized proposal is still created

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1160`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** In propose(), sizing_result metadata (including warnings like 'Daily loss $2,100 exceeds limit' or 'At position limit 20/20') is only attached when `result.amount_usd > 0`. When the sizer deliberately zeroes the size for a risk reason, the proposal is created anyway with quantity=None/amount=None and no sizing metadata; the entire sizing block is additionally wrapped in `except Exception: pass` (line 1169-1170), so config/portfolio-state failures also degrade to an unsized proposal with no explanation. The caller/LLM later gets a generic 'No valid quantity or amount specified' at approve time, with the actual risk-block reason lost.

- **Failure scenario:** Daily loss limit is breached; LLM runs `mmr --json propose AAPL BUY --confidence 0.8`. A proposal is created, returns a proposal_id with no sizing_result and no warning. The LLM (or user) retries with an explicit `--amount 5000`, which bypasses the sizer entirely — the daily-loss circuit breaker is defeated without anyone seeing it fired.

- **Suggested fix:** Always attach sizing_result (including the zero-size case with capped_by/warnings) to metadata, and consider refusing to create the proposal (or marking it REJECTED with reason) when the sizer returns 0 for a risk-limit reason.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end and confirmed. When the sizer zeroes size for a risk reason (position_sizing.py:312-326 sets amount_usd=0, capped_by='daily_loss_limit'/'max_positions', with warnings), sdk.py:1160 gates metadata attachment on `result.amount_usd > 0`, so the reason/warnings are dropped; the proposal is still created (sdk.py:1172) unsized, and sdk.py:1169-1170 also swallows config/portfolio failures. At approve time this yields the generic `'No valid quantity or amount specified'` (sdk.py:1400) and marks FAILED—actual reason lost. The escalation is real and worse than stated: a retry with `--amount` skips the sizer (sdk.py:1093 guard), and the execution-path risk gate never enforces daily loss—executioner.py:137-140 calls `evaluate()` without passing `daily_pnl`, so it defaults to 0.0 and the check at risk_gate.py:54 (`0.0 < -1000`) is always False. So the sizer's zero is the only daily-loss brake, and its rationale is silently discarded. Bumping to medium: capital-safety defense-in-depth defect, though it fires only in the relatively rare loss-limit/position-limit state.


### [ ] MEDIUM — buy/sell silently ignore explicit --sectype/--exchange/--currency when a same-symbol contract is cached from portfolio()

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:700`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** _place_order first checks `self._contract_map.get(symbol)` (populated by every portfolio() call, keyed by localSymbol-or-symbol) and only falls back to _resolve_contract — which is the only path that honours the sec_type/exchange/currency arguments passed from the CLI's `buy`/`sell` flags (mmr_cli.py:1891-1915). In a REPL session where the symbol is already held, the cached contract wins and the user's explicit routing hints are discarded without any warning. This violates the project's 'precision over convenience' principle (CLAUDE.md: 'If a symbol resolves to the wrong exchange, that's a bug').

- **Failure scenario:** In the REPL, the user runs `portfolio` (caching BHP as the held ASX/AUD listing), then `buy BHP --exchange NYSE --currency USD --market --quantity 100` intending the US ADR. The cached ASX contract is used, and 100 shares are bought on ASX in AUD — wrong exchange, wrong currency, wrong instrument, with no error or notice.

- **Suggested fix:** Only use the cached contract when no explicit sec_type/exchange/currency hints were supplied (or when they match the cached contract's fields); otherwise always call _resolve_contract with the hints.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. sdk.py:700-703 uses the cached contract first and only falls back to _resolve_contract (the only hint-honoring path, 329-353) on a cache miss. portfolio() caches every holding by localSymbol-or-symbol (sdk.py:495 + _extract_contract:458). The REPL runs a single persistent mmr instance (mmr_cli.py:10042 dispatch(mmr, args)), so the cache persists from `portfolio` into a later `buy`/`sell`. buy/sell forward sec_type/exchange/currency (mmr_cli.py:1892-1915) but they are discarded when the cache hits. No guard clears the cache or reconciles hints; no test covers _place_order's cache branch. Concrete failure: hold ASX BHP, run `portfolio`, then `buy BHP --exchange NYSE --currency USD` fills on ASX/AUD with no warning. Severity medium: trigger is narrow (same-ticker cross-listing in one session) but consequence is a wrong-instrument live-money order, violating the stated precision principle.


### [x] MEDIUM — approve() marks the proposal FAILED on RPC timeout even though the order may have been placed, inviting a duplicate trade

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1425`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** sdk.approve() wraps contract resolution, snapshot, and place_expressive_order in one `except Exception` that sets the proposal to FAILED. A ZMQ RPC timeout (clientserver raises TimeoutError client-side) is indistinguishable from 'order was never sent' — the server may have received the request and placed the order after the client gave up. FAILED is terminal in the state machine, and the CLI (_approve_one, mmr_cli.py:2550) reports it as a plain failure with no hint that broker state must be reconciled before retrying.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service is briefly slow (IB pacing); `mmr approve 42` times out client-side and prints 'Approve #42 failed: TimeoutError...'. The order was actually placed and fills. The operator (or LLM loop, following the failure message) creates and approves a replacement proposal → a second identical market order fills, doubling the position.

- **Suggested fix:** Distinguish timeout/connection errors from definitive rejections: on ambiguous failures, leave the proposal APPROVED with an 'unknown execution state — reconcile with `mmr orders`' message instead of FAILED, and/or have approve() cross-check open orders/executions for the algo tag before allowing a re-submission.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end and could not refute. clientserver.py:396 raises TimeoutError on RPC timeout; sdk.py:1402-1410 runs place_expressive_order under consume(); the broad except at sdk.py:1425-1427 catches ANY exception (including TimeoutError/ConnectionError) and unconditionally marks the proposal FAILED with a generic message. There is no timeout/rejection discrimination and no open-order/algo-tag cross-check. proposal_store.py:34 makes FAILED terminal, so recovery means a fresh proposal; mmr_cli.py:2560 prints a plain "Approve #N failed" with no reconcile hint. The only runtime-dependent link is whether the server actually placed the order during the timeout window (inherent RPC ambiguity), but the code-level unsafety is fully present. Severity medium, not high: the 30s RPC timeout on an order-staging call is uncommon, and the LLM loop's portfolio-diff/snapshot would typically surface the surprise position — but for live money a silent duplicate fill is a real capital-safety gap worth fixing.


### [ ] MEDIUM — compute_resize_plan silently swallows get_trades failure, so execution resizes positions while leaving old full-size protective orders live

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1527`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** The protective-order discovery in compute_resize_plan wraps get_trades in try/except Exception: pass (lines 1521-1527). If that RPC fails (timeout, transient trader_service issue), every adjustment gets associated_orders = [] and no error is surfaced anywhere -- the plan looks identical to 'no protective orders exist'. execute_resize_plan then places delta market orders without cancelling or resizing the real protective orders, which remain live at pre-resize quantities. This directly violates the fail-loudly principle in a path that places real orders.

- **Failure scenario:** resize-positions --max-bound 400000 runs while trader_service is briefly slow; get_trades times out. The plan shows no 'Associated orders to adjust', the user confirms, and positions are cut 50%. The untouched GTC STP SELL 100 on a now-50-share position later triggers, selling 100 shares and flipping the book short 50.

- **Suggested fix:** Let the get_trades exception propagate (or abort plan computation with an explicit error) -- a resize plan must not be built without a confirmed view of open orders.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. sdk.py:1522-1527 swallows a get_trades() exception with `except Exception: pass`, leaving trades_raw={}. Then sdk.py:1536-1574 assigns associated_orders=[] to every adjustment (inner loop gated on `if trades_raw:`). In the CLI, mmr_cli.py:2886 computes has_orders=False, so no protective-orders section is shown — indistinguishable from "no protectives exist." After confirmation, execute_resize_plan (sdk.py:1594-1649) skips the cancel step (empty associated list) but still places the delta market order, leaving real protective orders live at pre-resize quantity. No guard exists elsewhere; this is the only protective-order discovery site and the CLI does no independent open-orders check. Requires portfolio() (1501) to succeed while get_trades() transiently fails — plausible since they are separate RPCs. Genuine "fail loudly" violation on an order-placing path. Severity medium: real capital-safety hazard (oversized stop can over-sell and flip the book short) but conditional on a transient RPC failure during a manual resize with existing protectives.


### [ ] MEDIUM — Resize totals and bounds sum marketValue across positions without FX normalization

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:68`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** compute_resize_deltas (and compute_resize_plan at line 1506) computes total_value = sum(abs(p['marketValue'])) directly from PortfolioSummary rows. Those values flow unconverted from ib_async PortfolioItem.marketValue (trading_runtime.py:1399), which IB reports per-instrument in the contract's currency; there is no FX conversion anywhere in the path. For a mixed-currency book (US + ASX positions, which this system explicitly trades), the sum adds USD and AUD as raw numbers, so the comparison against max_bound/min_bound (a base-currency dollar figure) and the resulting scale_factor are both wrong. portfolio_snapshot's exposure_pct (line 943) has the same mixed-unit division against base-currency NetLiquidation.

- **Failure scenario:** Book: $300k of US stocks + A$300k of ASX stocks, AUDUSD 0.65 (true total ~$495k). resize-positions --max-bound 500000 computes total 600,000, decides the portfolio is over-bound, and sells down ~17% of every position -- real trades triggered purely by a unit error; conversely a genuinely over-bound book can be judged compliant.

- **Suggested fix:** Convert each position's marketValue to base currency (rates are available via get_account_cash_by_currency's exchange_rate map) before summing, or hard-fail resize when more than one currency is present.

- **Verifier:** Could not refute. Traced end-to-end: portfolio() (sdk.py:463-487) copies IB's PortfolioItem.marketValue verbatim (trading_runtime.py:1399); no currency column is even carried. compute_resize_deltas (sdk.py:68) and compute_resize_plan (sdk.py:1506) sum abs(marketValue) with zero FX conversion, then compare against a base-currency max/min_bound and derive scale_factor -> target_qty -> real market orders. An exchange_rate map exists (sdk.py:2062) but is never used in this path; grep confirms no conversion anywhere. The only link resting on broker behavior is that IB's updatePortfolio marketValue is in the contract's local currency (it has no currency arg and marketPrice is the local instrument price) — well-established IB behavior. CLAUDE.md and the live-account memory confirm the system trades mixed US+ASX/SEHK books, so the mixed-currency trigger is real; no single-currency guard exists. Severity medium: it fires only on a genuinely mixed-currency book and resize-positions is a deliberate manual command with a --dry-run preview showing the (inflated) total, so a user can catch it before capital moves.


### [ ] MEDIUM — Symbol-keyed contract cache overrides explicit exchange/currency hints and collapses dual listings

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:700`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** _place_order prefers self._contract_map.get(symbol) over resolving with the caller's explicit sec_type/exchange/currency hints, and _contract_map is keyed by bare symbol and overwritten per portfolio row (line 495). Two consequences: (1) buy('BHP', exchange='NYSE', currency='USD') while holding ASX BHP silently routes to the cached ASX/AUD contract, ignoring the caller's hints -- the 'close enough lookup' CLAUDE.md forbids; (2) if both listings of a dual-listed symbol are held, close_position('BHP') takes pos_size from the first matching portfolio row (line 1457) but the contract from whichever row was iterated last, so the quantity of one listing can be sold on the other listing's contract.

- **Failure scenario:** Hold 1,000 BHP on ASX and short 200 BHP on NYSE. portfolio() caches the NYSE contract last. close_position('BHP') matches the ASX row (pos 1000, action SELL) but sends SELL 1000 on the NYSE conId -- increasing the NYSE short to 1,200 while the ASX position is untouched.

- **Suggested fix:** Key _contract_map by conId (or (symbol, exchange, currency)); only use the cache when the caller supplied no hints; make close_position operate on conId, requiring disambiguation when a symbol maps to multiple positions.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. _contract_map is keyed by bare symbol (sdk.py:495, last-write-wins) and persists across REPL commands (mmr_cli.py:2744 relies on that persistence). Claim 1: sdk.py:700 prefers the cached contract over the caller's exchange/currency hints, so buy('BHP', exchange='NYSE') routes to a cached ASX contract. Claim 2: close_position takes pos_size from the first sorted portfolio row (sdk.py:1457) but the contract from the last-cached row (sdk.py:1467); the CLI-passed con_id (mmr_cli.py:2772) is dead because line 1470 only consults it on a cache miss, which never occurs after portfolio(). For a symbol held on two exchanges under the same IB ticker, one listing's quantity is sent on the other's conId. Both violate CLAUDE.md "precision over convenience." Not refutable. Raised to medium: wrong-instrument live orders are a capital-safety defect, gated behind the rare dual-listing condition.


### [x] MEDIUM — Approve converts USD amount to quantity using local-currency price — no FX conversion for international proposals

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1394`  ·  _reviewer: wrong-thing_

- **Mechanism:** For an amount-based proposal, approve computes `qty = round(proposal.amount / price)` (sdk.py:1394) where `price` is the raw IB snapshot last/ask/bid in the contract's own currency (AUD for ASX, JPY for TSE, HKD for SEHK). But `amount` is USD: the auto-sizer's result field is literally `amount_usd` (position_sizing.py, computed from the USD NetLiquidation), and CLI docs describe --amount as dollar value. There is no FX conversion anywhere on the propose->approve path (the propose-time leverage estimate at sdk.py:1223-1229 makes the same USD/local-currency mix). The resulting position is wrong by the full FX factor, and the `if qty < 1: qty = 1` floor at sdk.py:1395-1396 can force a trade even when the mis-converted qty rounds to zero.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr propose 7203 BUY --market --exchange TSE --currency JPY --confidence 0.7` auto-sizes to amount_usd=10000. At approve, Toyota snapshot last=3000 (JPY) -> qty=round(10000/3000)=3 shares = ¥9,000 ≈ $60 — a $10,000 intent becomes a $60 position (167x undersized). For ASX at 0.65 AUDUSD the position is ~35% smaller than sized; for a proposal where the user meant AUD, it is oversized instead. Sizing, group budgets, and leverage estimates are all silently wrong.

- **Suggested fix:** Resolve the contract currency at approve time and convert amount via an FX rate (IDEALPRO midpoint snapshot) before dividing; fail loudly if the rate can't be fetched. Also tag proposal.amount with an explicit currency field.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. `amount` is USD: auto-sizer returns `amount_usd` from NetLiquidation, which IB reports in account base currency USD (position_sizing.py:243-246; sdk.py:2149). At approve, the contract is resolved with `proposal.currency` (AUD/JPY/HKD) (sdk.py:1367-1370), so `get_snapshot` yields a local-currency price, and `qty = round(proposal.amount / price)` (sdk.py:1394) divides USD by a local price with no FX step (grep confirms no convert/IDEALPRO on this path). The `qty<1→1` floor (1395-1396) can force an unintended trade. Position is wrong by the full FX factor: JPY/HKD undersize (safe direction), GBP/EUR oversize (capital-risk direction). Real bug. Severity re-assessed to medium: US/USD is the default and dominant flow (currency defaults to USD, no error there); the defect only bites international amount-based proposals, and the common large-price markets (JPY/HKD) undersize conservatively, though EUR/GBP can oversize.


### [x] MEDIUM — to_market re-places the full original quantity, ignoring partial fills on the cancelled limit order

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:779`  ·  _reviewer: wrong-thing_

- **Mechanism:** to_market reads `quantity = float(order.totalQuantity)` (sdk.py:779) from the resting limit order, cancels it, and re-places that quantity as a market order via place_expressive_order. totalQuantity is the original order size; the already-filled portion is in trade.orderStatus.filled/remaining (which the same file uses correctly in orders() at line 635-636). Any partial fill before conversion is double-bought/sold. The re-created STOP_LOSS child is likewise sized to the full original quantity.

- **Failure scenario:** Limit BUY 1000 AMD @ $180 fills 400 shares, then the price runs away. User runs `to-market <orderId>`: parent cancelled, MARKET BUY 1000 placed -> final position 1400 shares, 40% oversized, with a protective stop sized 1000 against a 1400 position.

- **Suggested fix:** Use `trade.orderStatus.remaining` (with a guard for zero remaining) as the re-placed quantity.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed. sdk.py:779 sets `quantity = float(order.totalQuantity)` (original size), never reading `trade.orderStatus.remaining`, though the same file uses `remaining`/`filled` correctly in orders() (sdk.py:635-636). to_market cancels the parent (IB cancels only the unfilled remainder; filled shares persist as a position) and re-places the full totalQuantity as MARKET (sdk.py:802-810), also sizing the STOP_LOSS child to the full quantity (798). No guard exists; tests (test_sdk.py:462-537) only cover fully-unfilled orders and assert quantity==100.0, none exercise a partial fill. Concrete path: LMT BUY 1000 fills 400 → cancel drops 600 → MARKET BUY 1000 → 1400-share position with a 1000-share stop. Severity medium: genuine capital over-exposure and mis-sized protective stop, but only on the partial-fill-then-convert path.


### [x] MEDIUM — propose --group silently no-ops when the group does not exist, disabling budget tracking

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1194`  ·  _reviewer: probe-2:position_groups store and group-budget e_

- **Mechanism:** In propose(), group registration calls gs.add_member(group, symbol) but ignores its return value and wraps the whole block in `except Exception: pass` (lines 1191-1196). PositionGroupStore.add_member (position_groups.py:163-168) returns False without inserting if the named group row does not exist — it never auto-creates the group. So when a user proposes into a group that was never created via `group create`, the proposal record still carries group='mining' but no membership row is written and no group exists. portfolio_risk.analyze() (portfolio_risk.py:146-178) iterates group_store.list_groups(), which won't include the nonexistent group, so that position is never counted toward any budget and no over-budget warning can ever fire. This contradicts the documented 'auto-registers the symbol into the named group' behaviour and the fail-loudly principle.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator runs `mmr propose BHP BUY --market --confidence 0.7 --group mining` before ever running `group create mining`. The proposal is created and approved; BHP fills. `mmr portfolio-risk` shows no 'mining' group and never flags the 20% mining budget being breached, so the operator keeps adding mining names believing the budget guardrail is active when nothing is tracked.

- **Suggested fix:** Have propose() create the group on demand (or check existence and surface a clear error) instead of silently swallowing add_member's False/exception; at minimum log a warning when add_member returns False.

- **Verifier:** Code path is real. sdk.py:1194 calls gs.add_member(group, symbol) and swallows the result in except Exception: pass (1191-1196). position_groups.py:167-168 returns False without inserting when the group row is absent (confirmed by test_position_groups.py:90-92). portfolio_risk.py:148 iterates only list_groups(), so an unwritten membership is never budget-counted. propose never auto-creates the group (only group create at mmr_cli.py:2597 does), contradicting CLAUDE.md's "auto-registers the symbol into the named group." I downgrade to medium: budgets are warning-only soft limits, and the over-budget check is gated on max_allocation_pct > 0 (portfolio_risk.py:156), which requires an explicit group create --budget — and once the group exists, add_member succeeds. The real residual harm is the silent ordering gap (pre-create proposals drop membership) plus the swallowed False violating fail-loudly; no direct order-placement risk.


### [x] MEDIUM — Sortino ratio uses std of the negative-return subsample instead of downside deviation, allowing unbounded inflation

- **Location:** `trader/simulation/backtester.py:634`  ·  _reviewer: backtester_

- **Mechanism:** Sortino is computed as `returns.mean() / negative.std()` where `negative = returns[returns < 0]`. This is wrong on two counts: (1) canonical Sortino divides by downside deviation about the target (sqrt(mean(min(r,0)^2)) over ALL n returns), not the sample std of only the losing bars; (2) `negative.std()` is centered on the mean of the losses, so it measures dispersion AMONG losses, not their magnitude. A strategy whose losses are large but tightly clustered gets a near-zero denominator and an astronomically inflated Sortino; if all losses are exactly equal, `negative.std() == 0` and Sortino is reported as 0.0. Sortino is the first and most heavily weighted term in `_bt_composite_score` (mmr_cli.py:4880), which is the DEFAULT sort for `backtests list` and the sweep leaderboard.

- **Failure scenario:** A 1-min strategy averages +0.01% per bar but every loss is ~-2.0% ± 0.01% (steamroller profile). True downside deviation ≈ 2%, true Sortino ≈ 0.05·sqrt(bpy); computed `negative.std()` ≈ 0.0001 so Sortino ≈ 100·sqrt(bpy) — inflated ~20,000x. The run floats to the top of `backtests list` and the nightly sweep digest's strong-candidates table, steering the user/LLM toward deploying a blow-up-prone strategy.

- **Suggested fix:** Compute downside deviation as `np.sqrt((returns.clip(upper=0) ** 2).mean())` over all returns and divide `returns.mean()` by that before annualizing.

- **Verifier:** Math defect is real and reachable. backtester.py:631-634 computes Sortino as returns.mean()/negative.std() where negative=returns[returns<0] — pandas sample std of only losing bars (dispersion AMONG losses), not downside deviation about zero. Any fixed-stop strategy yields near-identical loss magnitudes → negative.std()≈0 → Sortino inflated arbitrarily (the >0 guard at :632 only catches exactly-equal losses, reported as 0.0). Impact traces end-to-end via UNCLIPPED consumers: the sweep morning-digest ranking _rough_score = sortino+min(pf,3)-10*dd (mmr_cli.py:6027-6036) and backtests --sort-by sortino (mmr_cli.py:5204) both float inflated runs to the top. The finding overstates the DEFAULT sort path — _bt_composite_score clips sortino/3.0 to [-2,2] (mmr_cli.py:4890), bounding it there. Severity is medium not high: it is a ranking/display metric with no order-placement effect, the docstrings and CLAUDE.md repeatedly state composite/ranking is "Not a decision metric — use the statistical-confidence block for deploy/reject," and the strong-candidates filter additionally gates on sharpe>2.0 and pf>1.5.


### [x] MEDIUM — Trade-level P&L omits buy-side commission, overstating expectancy_bps, profit_factor and win_rate

- **Location:** `trader/simulation/backtester.py:607`  ·  _reviewer: backtester_

- **Mechanism:** Round-trip P&L is computed as `(trade.price - entry_price) * trade.quantity - trade.commission`, where `trade.commission` is the SELL-side commission only; `avg_entry` is built from raw buy fill prices with no buy-side commission added. Win classification (line 612) ignores commissions entirely (`trade.price > entry_price`). So the headline expectancy_bps — which the code's own comment says 'is what actually has to survive slippage/commissions' — plus profit_factor and win_rate are systematically optimistic by the buy-side commission. Note the statistical layer (`backtest_stats.round_trip_pnls`, lines 112-116) correctly deducts BOTH sides, so the headline metrics and the confidence-block P&Ls disagree for the same run.

- **Failure scenario:** Scalping a $5 stock with default commission_per_share=0.005 (10 bps per side): a strategy with true net expectancy of ~0 bps reports +10 bps expectancy and a >1 profit factor, passing the 'survives costs' screen; trades where price barely exceeds entry but net P&L is negative are counted as wins, inflating win_rate.

- **Suggested fix:** Include buy-side commission in avg_entry (weighted average of price + commission/share) and classify wins on net pnl > 0, matching round_trip_pnls in backtest_stats.py.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. backtester.py:599 builds avg_entry from raw buy fill price with no buy-side commission; :607 computes pnl subtracting only trade.commission (sell-side, per :418); :612 classifies wins on trade.price > entry_price, ignoring commissions. These feed win_rate (:622), profit_factor (:645), and expectancy_bps (:658-659) — whose comment (:654) claims it must "survive slippage/commissions." Meanwhile backtest_stats.py:112-116 correctly deducts both buy (lot[2]) and sell commission, so the headline and confidence-block P&Ls disagree for the same run. commission_per_share defaults to 0.005 (:35), so on a low-priced/high-turnover strategy the buy-side omission systematically overstates the metrics. Real and reproducible. Medium: bias is one side's per-share commission (bps-scale), significant only for high-turnover strategies; the documented deploy gate is the correct confidence block, not these headline numbers.


### [ ] MEDIUM — Strategy enabled-state is not persisted and WAITING_HISTORICAL_DATA never transitions — strategies silently stop (or run without their data precondition) after restart

- **Location:** `trader/strategy/strategy_runtime.py:217`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** Two state-machine holes. (1) install() sets INSTALLED and only the enable_strategy RPC moves a strategy to RUNNING; nothing persists this, so after any process restart every strategy reloads as INSTALLED and __get_enabled_strategies skips it — a strategy that was live yesterday is silently dark today. (2) __get_enabled_strategies dispatches strategies in WAITING_HISTORICAL_DATA, but no code ever re-evaluates that state after get_historical_data() completes: SMICrossOver.enable() parks itself in WAITING when bars are missing and stays there forever (its own on_prices guard means it never signals), while a base-class strategy in WAITING would be dispatched and can signal on whatever partial tick data exists, defeating the readiness gate.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator enables smi_crossover which is managing an open position via exit signals. The container is rebuilt overnight (docker.sh -s + restart). strategy_service reloads the YAML, the strategy comes back as INSTALLED, is never dispatched, and the position's exit condition passes unnoticed; `strategies` output shows it loaded, masking the problem.

- **Suggested fix:** Persist enabled state (e.g. an `enabled` field in strategy_runtime.yaml or the object store) and re-apply it on load; in the reconcile loop, re-run the readiness check for WAITING_HISTORICAL_DATA strategies and either promote them to RUNNING or exclude WAITING from dispatch.

- **Verifier:** Both state-machine holes are real. RUNNING is reachable only via the enable_strategy RPC → implementation.enable() (strategy_runtime.py:195-197); install() sets INSTALLED (strategy.py:154-157); run() (647-748) never auto-enables; no `enabled` field exists in strategy_runtime.yaml and no persistence exists (grep confirmed). __get_enabled_strategies (line 217) dispatches only RUNNING/WAITING, so after restart all strategies reload INSTALLED and are silently un-dispatched while `get_strategies()` still lists them — matching the "silent dark" claim. Part 2: SMICrossOver.enable() parks in WAITING (smi_crossover.py:53-55) and nothing re-runs enable() after get_historical_data(); _reconcile_sync only re-subscribes; on_prices returns None unless RUNNING (line 99), so it stays dark forever. Medium, not high: reaching RUNNING requires a prior operator RPC, and the capital-loss (missed live exit) escalation depends on signal auto-execution wiring not clearly present; the certain harm is missed dispatch masked by the loaded listing.


### [x] MEDIUM — Intraday strategies are silent no-ops live: runtime dispatches on_prices, they only implement on_bar

- **Location:** `trader/strategy/strategy_runtime.py:247`  ·  _reviewer: probe-3:Intraday session, timezone, and RTH boun_

- **Mechanism:** The live runtime calls `strategy.on_prices(self.streams[conId])` exclusively. All five intraday strategies (vwap_reversion, opening_range_breakout, opening_drive_fade, late_day_momentum, vwap_reclaim) implement only `precompute` + `on_bar` and do not override `on_prices`; the base `Strategy.on_prices` (strategy.py:181) returns None. So once deployed to the strategy_service they generate zero signals. Compounding this, the EOD-flat / max_hold_bars exit synthesis that these strategies depend on for risk control lives only in the backtester loop (exit_conditions), not in the live runtime — so even if a position were opened by other means, close_by_time would never fire live. This violates the fail-loudly principle: a trader runs `strategies deploy` + `reload`, sees the strategy 'RUNNING', and it does nothing, with no error.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator backtests opening_range_breakout, likes the numbers, deploys it live with `mmr strategies deploy opening_range_breakout --conids ...`. The service subscribes and marks it RUNNING, ticks flow, but on_prices returns None every bar, so no trades ever occur — the operator believes an intraday strategy is active when it is inert, and any manually held position tagged to it never gets the EOD-flat protection the backtest assumed.

- **Suggested fix:** Either add an on_prices shim in these strategies (compute precompute state + call on_bar on the accumulated window) or have the base on_prices default-dispatch through precompute/on_bar; and port the time-based exit synthesis into the live runtime so close_by_time/max_hold_bars are enforced in production.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed end-to-end. strategy_runtime.py:247 dispatches only strategy.on_prices(); grep shows no on_bar/precompute call anywhere in the runtime. Base Strategy.on_prices returns None (strategy.py:167-181), and the base docstring explicitly admits "For live trading the runtime still uses on_prices — on_bar is backtest-only today" (strategy.py:203-205). All five intraday strategies (opening_range_breakout, vwap_reversion, opening_drive_fade, late_day_momentum, vwap_reclaim; also gap_reversion) implement only precompute+on_bar, never on_prices. Deployed live they emit zero signals silently, and the EOD-flat/max_hold exits live only in the backtester. Severity medium, not higher: this fails closed — a no-op opens no positions and loses no capital directly. The harm is the fail-loudly violation (operator sees RUNNING, gets nothing) plus loss of EOD protection on a manually-held tagged position; there is no wrong-trade/capital-loss path.


### [ ] MEDIUM — Location-code parsing resolves symbols on the wrong exchange (SMART fallback / TSE-vs-TSEJ / 'MAJOR')

- **Location:** `trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:1229`  ·  _reviewer: idea-scanner_

- **Mechanism:** IBIdeaScanner._resolve_symbols derives the IB exchange by blindly taking parts[2] of the location code (line 1226-1229). Three failure modes: (1) two-part codes like STK.CA or STK.EU (both listed as supported in CLAUDE.md) yield exchange_hint='' so the partial Contract is built with exchange='SMART' and no currency, and reqContractDetails returns multi-listing matches from which defs[0] is picked arbitrarily — typically the US listing, not the local one; (2) STK.JP.TSE yields 'TSE', which in IB's exchange namespace is Toronto (Tokyo is 'TSEJ' — the exact confusion CLAUDE.md's precision principle calls out); (3) STK.US.MAJOR yields 'MAJOR', not a valid IB exchange. The resulting wrong-exchange contract's conId is also stored in conid_map and used for news lookups. This directly violates the 'never fall back to fuzzy/close-enough lookups' design principle.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr ideas momentum --location STK.CA --tickers SHOP` resolves SHOP via SMART with no currency constraint; defs[0] is the NYSE/USD listing. The scan is labeled a Canada scan but shows US prices/currency, and any LLM proposal built from it targets the wrong listing. `--location STK.JP.TSE --tickers 7203` builds Contract(exchange='TSE') and queries Toronto for a Tokyo ticker.

- **Suggested fix:** Maintain an explicit location-code → IB exchange map (validated, fail loudly on unknown codes), always set currency on the partial Contract, and raise if reqContractDetails returns multiple ambiguous matches instead of taking defs[0].

- **Verifier:** Code defect confirmed. idea_scanner.py:1227-1229 takes parts[2] blindly: two-part codes (STK.CA/STK.EU, both documented) yield exchange_hint='' → Contract built with exchange='SMART' and no currency (1236-1240), then defs[0] picked unconditionally (1248). tests/test_idea_scanner.py:1689 asserts exactly this SMART fallback for STK.CA. resolve_contract (trading_runtime.py:628) passes the partial straight to reqContractDetailsAsync with no exchange/currency post-filter. STK.JP.TSE yields 'TSE' (Toronto, not Tokyo/TSEJ — the confusion CLAUDE.md's precision principle flags); STK.US.MAJOR yields invalid 'MAJOR'. This violates 'resolve exactly or fail.' The exact 'US listing returned' outcome depends on IB's defs ordering (runtime), but the defect is fully in code. Downgraded to medium: this is the ideas discovery/display path (conId feeds snapshots/news at 1050-1095), not order execution — propose/approve resolve independently via local-DB resolve_symbol, so no direct wrong-order link.


### [ ] MEDIUM — Partial history-fetch failures silently produce zeroed change/gap/rel_vol and missing indicators; guard only fires when ALL fetches fail

- **Location:** `trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:1138`  ·  _reviewer: idea-scanner_

- **Mechanism:** The comment at lines 1104-1105 says 'If >50% of fetches fail, raise', but the code at line 1138 raises only when len(history_failures) == history_limit (100% failure). Any symbol whose history fetch failed — or any symbol beyond the contracts[:top_n*2] fetch cap (line 1111) — has no entry in history_map, so _build_candidates (line 1307-1315) computes change_pct=0.0, gap_pct=0.0, rel_vol=0.0 and step 7 leaves rsi/sma/ema absent. On the explicit-tickers path min/max_change filters are relaxed (lines 1041-1044), so these candidates pass filters and are returned showing 'change_pct: 0.00' as if it were real data; on the scanner path they are silently filtered out by min_change_pct, shrinking the pool with only a service-side WARNING log.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr ideas mean-reversion --location STK.AU.ASX --tickers BHP CBA CSL WBC NAB` with IB pacing causing 4 of 5 history fetches to time out: four rows come back with change_pct=0.00, rel_vol=0.00 and no RSI/SMA, scored as if flat and quiet. An LLM consuming --json output treats 0.00% change as fact and reasons from it when proposing trades.

- **Suggested fix:** Implement the documented >50% threshold, and mark rows with missing history as None/NaN (not 0.0) or drop them with an explicit per-symbol warning in the returned output.

- **Verifier:** Traced fully. The guard at idea_scanner.py:1138 fires only on 100% failure (`len(history_failures) == history_limit`), contradicting the >50% intent documented at 1104-1105. On partial failure, failed symbols have no history_map entry; `_build_candidates` (1304-1325) sets prev_close=0 → change_pct=0.0, gap_pct=0.0, rel_vol=0.0, and step-7 indicators (1159-1172) are skipped. On the explicit-tickers path, min/max_change_pct are relaxed to None (1041-1044); min_relative_volume defaults to 0.0 (38) and 0.0 < 0.0 is False (324), while price/volume come from the real snapshot — so zeroed rows survive apply_filters and are returned as `change_pct: 0.00` with a service-side-only WARNING (1130). Confirmed real fail-loudly violation. Severity medium, not high: this is idea-generation input to an LLM, one step removed from execution (propose→approve→risk-gate intervene), missing RSI yields neutral mean-reversion scores that rank low, and it requires IB pacing failures — data-integrity degradation, not direct capital loss.


### [x] MEDIUM — Zero-volume instruments bypass the min_volume liquidity filter (and unknown spread bypasses max_spread_pct)

- **Location:** `trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:318`  ·  _reviewer: idea-scanner_

- **Mechanism:** apply_filters checks `if c['volume'] > 0 and c['volume'] < filters.min_volume: continue` — a candidate with volume == 0 (halted stock, missing/NaN IB snapshot volume coerced to 0 at line 1343, or missing TD field) passes a min_volume=500,000 preset filter outright. Similarly line 326's spread check `c.get('spread_pct', 0) > filters.max_spread_pct > 0` passes when bid/ask were unavailable and spread_pct defaulted to 0.0. Both cases treat 'no liquidity data' as 'perfectly liquid', the opposite of the conservative default a liquidity gate should have.

- **Failure scenario:** On the IB path a thinly traded ASX name returns NaN volume in its snapshot (common with delayed data); volume becomes 0, it passes the 500K min-volume filter, scores well on gap/change computed from history, and surfaces as a top idea. The LLM proposes a position in an instrument too illiquid to exit cleanly.
