- **Suggested fix:** Treat volume<=0 as failing min_volume when min_volume>0 (or mark liquidity as unknown and exclude/flag), and likewise reject or flag candidates with unknown spread when max_spread_pct is active.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. idea_scanner.py:318 `if c['volume'] > 0 and c['volume'] < filters.min_volume: continue` — volume==0 fails the first conjunct, so it is NOT skipped and passes even a 500K preset. Volume becomes 0 legitimately: line 1298 `snap.get('volume') or 0`, then line 1343 `int(volume) if volume and volume == volume else 0` coerces NaN (common in delayed IB snapshots) to 0. The candidate also clears the other gates: rel_vol defaults 0.0 (line 1323) and min_relative_volume defaults 0.0 (line 38, no preset overrides), so `0.0 < 0.0` is False; change_pct/gap_pct come from history bars (lines 1314-1320), so it still scores and surfaces. Spread mirror at line 326 with default spread_pct=0.0 (line 1333) likewise passes. No guard elsewhere; test_min_volume_filter (line 275) uses 50_000, never 0, so no test contradicts. Medium: it feeds illiquid names into the LLM idea flow, but propose/approve review and the risk gate sit between this and live orders.


### [x] MEDIUM — No order quantity/price validation anywhere: OrderValidator is a stub and equity-amount sizing divides by IB's no-data bid sentinel, producing negative or NaN quantities

- **Location:** `trader/trading/executioner.py:216`  ·  _reviewer: execution_

- **Mechanism:** helper_create_order computes quantity = equity_amount / (latest_tick.bid * multiplier) with no check that bid is a valid positive price. ib_async Tickers report -1.0 or NaN for bid when there is no market data (market closed, no subscription). bid=-1 yields a large NEGATIVE quantity (round(-10000) passes straight through); bid=NaN yields NaN quantity; bid=0 raises ZeroDivisionError. The order is then submitted to IB with totalQuantity negative/NaN. The only backstop, OrderValidator.sanity_check_order (order_validator.py:35), unconditionally returns True, so the ExecutorCondition.SANITY_CHECK path in place_order is decorative — nothing in the system validates quantity>0, non-fractional where required, order_price>0 (a limit order with no limit_price and market_order=False gets lmtPrice=0.0), or bracket price relationships. This violates the project's stated 'precision over convenience' principle: the wrong order reaches IB and only the broker's rejection saves you.

- **Failure scenario:** After hours, 'buy AMD --amount 10000 --market' via place_order_simple: get_snapshot returns bid=-1.0, quantity becomes -10000, a MarketOrder(action='BUY', totalQuantity=-10000) is transmitted to IB. Best case IB rejects with a confusing error; the SANITY_CHECK gate that exists precisely for this passes it unconditionally.

- **Suggested fix:** Implement sanity_check_order: reject quantity <= 0 / NaN, require a valid positive tick price before amount-based sizing (fail loudly naming the sentinel), and validate lmtPrice/stopPrice > 0 and stop/TP on the correct side of the market.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end and confirmed. place_order_simple (trading_runtime.py:1246) calls get_snapshot, whose own code comments document that IB returns bid/ask = -1 sentinel or NaN off-hours / without a subscription (ibreactive.py:725,741,788), and returns that ticker to the caller. helper_create_order then computes quantity = equity_amount/(latest_tick.bid*multiplier) with no validity guard (executioner.py:216); bid=-1 -> quantity=-10000, the `<1 and >0` guard (line 218) is skipped, round(-10000) passes through into MarketOrder totalQuantity. The only backstop, sanity_check_order, unconditionally returns True (order_validator.py:35), so the SANITY_CHECK path (executioner.py:152-162) is decorative. The risk gate never receives the quantity (evaluate is called with only signal+open_order_count, executioner.py:137-140; risk_gate.py:38-83), so it can't catch it. The lmtPrice=0.0 limit-order path (executioner.py:272-279) is also real. Severity is medium, not critical: the products are malformed (negative/NaN qty, zero limit price) that IB rejects rather than wrong-direction executed trades, so it's a fail-loudly/precision violation rather than a silent-loss path — but capital-safety-relevant and worth fixing.


### [x] MEDIUM — Correlation computed on raw price levels, not returns — spurious clusters once the feature is fixed

- **Location:** `trader/trading/portfolio_risk.py:260`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** `df.corr()` is applied to a DataFrame of raw daily closes. Correlation of non-stationary price levels is dominated by common trend: any two stocks that both drifted up over the 60-day window show corr near 1 regardless of whether their returns co-move. CLAUDE.md describes this feature as 'return correlation clusters'. This is currently masked because _compute_correlations never executes (see the dead-code finding), but the moment those call errors are fixed, the >0.7 threshold will cluster essentially all trending positions together and the avg_corr numbers reported to the LLM will be meaningless.

- **Failure scenario:** After the call-site bugs are repaired: a portfolio of 10 unrelated uptrending stocks (bull tape) all show pairwise price-level corr > 0.9 -> one giant 'correlated cluster' with 70% net exposure -> a warning fires on a genuinely diversified book, while true return-correlation structure (e.g. two miners moving together in returns but one range-bound) is not distinguished.

- **Suggested fix:** Compute correlation on percentage returns: `df.pct_change().dropna().corr()`, and require a minimum overlap of return observations.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed. portfolio_risk.py:256-260 builds a DataFrame of raw daily closes and calls df.corr() — Pearson correlation on non-stationary price levels, never pct_change(); CLAUDE.md specifies "return correlation clusters," so intended semantics are returns. The finding's "masked by dead code" premise is actually wrong in the bug's favor: the call site (:186-188) passes all four args matching the signature, with weights/signed_weights built at :100/106, so _compute_correlations executes live in analyze(). Co-trending longs can spuriously agglomerate (:266-298) into one cluster whose net_weight_pct>0.30 fires a false "correlated cluster" warning to the LLM (:195-203). Tests (test_portfolio_risk.py:102-133) mock the helper entirely, so the level-correlation math is untested. The claim slightly overstates "corr near 1 regardless" (level Pearson is noisy), but the substance holds. Medium is fair: it corrupts a risk signal feeding propose/approve, not capital placement directly.


### [x] MEDIUM — PositionSizingConfig.load silently falls back to built-in defaults on any parse error

- **Location:** `trader/trading/position_sizing.py:120`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** `except Exception: return PositionSizingConfig()` means a malformed position_sizing.yaml (bad indent, a non-numeric value causing float() to raise, transient IO error) silently reverts every hard limit to the shipped defaults: max_position_usd back to $25,000, daily_loss_limit_usd back to $2,000, max_total_exposure_pct back to 0.80, etc. This directly violates the fail-loudly principle for the file that defines capital-safety limits, and the caller (sdk.propose / session_status) gets no indication the user's configured limits were discarded.

- **Failure scenario:** User tightens max_position_usd to 2,000 and daily_loss_limit_usd to 500 in ~/.config/mmr/position_sizing.yaml but introduces a YAML syntax error while editing. Every subsequent auto-sized proposal is sized against the default $25,000 cap and the $2,000 loss limit — 12.5x and 4x looser than intended — with zero warnings.

- **Suggested fix:** Let parse errors propagate (or raise a named ConfigError); at minimum log an error and set a flag surfaced in SizingResult.warnings / session_summary.

- **Verifier:** Traced concretely. position_sizing.py:120-121 is a bare `except Exception: return PositionSizingConfig()`. A malformed YAML makes `yaml.safe_load` (line 100) raise YAMLError, and a non-numeric value makes `float(...)` (lines 102-118) raise ValueError — both caught, both silently returning the dataclass defaults: max_position_usd=25_000 (103), daily_loss_limit_usd=2_000 (110), max_total_exposure_pct=0.80 (105). Callers do not detect this: sdk.py:872 (`session_status`) and sdk.py:1099 (propose) call `PositionSizingConfig.load()` and pass the result straight into `PositionSizer`, with no validation, no warning, and no surfaced flag in SizingResult/session_summary. So a user's tightened caps are discarded silently — exactly the fail-loudly violation claimed, on the file defining capital-safety limits. No guard refutes it. Severity is medium (arguably high given live-money stakes and dangerous direction — always looser), but the trigger requires a specific user YAML edit error, not a spontaneous condition.


### [x] MEDIUM — Daily loss limit under-counts losses when per-position PnL is NaN (PnL subscription gaps are silently skipped)

- **Location:** `trader/trading/position_sizing.py:320`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** state.daily_pnl is built in sdk._get_portfolio_state (sdk.py:851) as `portfolio_df['dailyPNL'].sum()`. Each position's dailyPNL comes from trading_runtime._get_portfolio_summary_sync's find_pnl_or_nan (trading_runtime.py:1364-1368), which returns NaN whenever the (account, conId) PnL subscription hasn't populated the cache — a race the codebase itself documents as common after trader_service restart. pandas Series.sum() skips NaN by default, so positions with missing PnL contribute $0 loss; if all are NaN the sum is 0.0. The daily-loss circuit breaker at line 320 then compares a partial (or zero) loss against daily_loss_limit_usd and keeps sizing new trades.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service restarts mid-session; PnL subscriptions for 8 of 10 positions haven't re-established. Real daily loss is -$3,500 (limit $2,000) but the two subscribed positions show -$400. The sizer sees daily_pnl=-400, the loss limit never trips, and the LLM loop keeps proposing and approving new positions during a drawdown that should have halted trading.

- **Suggested fix:** Treat NaN dailyPNL as unknown: count NaN positions and surface a warning (like the existing rpc_errors mechanism), or refuse to apply the loss-limit check as 'passed' when coverage is incomplete.

- **Verifier:** Traced end to end. find_pnl_or_nan (trading_runtime.py:1364-1368) returns float('nan') when the (account,conId) PnL subscription cache is unpopulated (the documented post-restart race). That NaN carries into PortfolioSummary.dailyPNL (1405) and the DataFrame dailyPNL column (sdk.py:490). _get_portfolio_state does portfolio_df['dailyPNL'].sum() (sdk.py:851); pandas Series.sum() defaults skipna=True, so NaN positions add $0 and an all-NaN portfolio sums to 0.0. The breaker at position_sizing.py:320 then compares a partial/zero loss and never halts. No guard covers this: state.rpc_errors (sdk.py:844,854,865) only catches RPC exceptions, not NaN cells; the portfolio() call succeeds. (Note portfolio_snapshot at sdk.py:921 uses `or 0`, but the sizing path does not.) Severity medium: it only disables a soft proposal-halt during a transient gap that repopulates on reconcile, but a failed daily-loss stop during a drawdown is a real capital-safety gap.


### [x] MEDIUM — Risk gate 'open order' count uses BookSubject, which never removes filled/cancelled orders — trading freezes after 15 lifetime orders

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:941`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** place_expressive_order (line 941) and executioner.place_order (executioner.py:139) pass `open_order_count=len(self.book.get_orders())` to risk_gate.evaluate, which rejects when count >= RiskLimits.max_open_orders (hardcoded 15, RiskGate is constructed with bare RiskLimits() at connect). BookSubject.add_update_trade (book.py:24-37) only ever adds orderId keys — nothing anywhere prunes filled, cancelled, or historical orders (verified: no pop/clear/del on book.orders in the codebase). reqAllOpenOrdersAsync at startup plus every newOrder/orderStatus/openOrder event grows the dict monotonically for the life of the trader_service process. cancel_all() (line 1274) has the same flaw: it iterates every order ever seen and issues cancelOrder for long-dead orders.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service runs for a week. Five bracket proposals execute and fully close (15 orderIds seen, all dead). The 16th proposal — including an attempt to exit a losing position via propose/approve — is rejected with 'max open orders exceeded: 15 >= 15' even though zero orders are open. All proposal-driven trading, including protective exits, is blocked until the service is restarted.

- **Suggested fix:** Count genuinely open orders: filter book trades by ib_async active order statuses, or use self.client.ib.openTrades()/reqAllOpenOrders. Also prune terminal orders from BookSubject on orderStatus Filled/Cancelled, and make RiskLimits configurable.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. BookSubject.add_update_trade (book.py:24-37) only inserts orderId keys and nothing anywhere prunes filled/cancelled orders (codebase grep clean). The book subscribes to orderStatusEvent/newOrderEvent/openOrderEvent (trading_runtime.py:363-370), so get_orders() grows monotonically. Both risk checks pass open_order_count=len(book.get_orders()) (trading_runtime.py:941, executioner.py:139), and risk_gate.py:47 rejects at >= max_open_orders (default 15, risk_gate.py:20; gate built bare at trading_runtime.py:270). After ~5 executed brackets (15 dead orderIds), all new proposals are rejected until restart. Confirmed. Severity downgraded to medium for a low-frequency live system: it fails closed (no wrong trades), broker-resting bracket protective legs stay live so open positions keep their stops, and set_risk_limits (trader_service_api.py:339) lets an operator raise the cap at runtime without restart — partially refuting the finding's 'hardcoded/not configurable/restart-only' framing. Real availability defect, not a direct capital-loss path.


### [ ] MEDIUM — Ticker publications (publish_contract) are never re-established after an IB reconnect — strategy market data dies silently

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:711`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** connect_async() (ibreactive.py:333) replaces self.ib with a fresh IB() instance; all reqMktData subscriptions are per-connection and die with the old socket. Trader.connected_event re-runs setup_subscriptions (book, positions, portfolio, PnL) but never re-issues market-data requests. Worse, publish_contract short-circuits at line 711: `if contract.conId in self.zmq_pubsub_contract_filters: return self.zmq_pubsub_contracts[contract.conId]` — and zmq_pubsub_contract_filters is only reset in the sync connect() path (first boot, line 258), never in connected_event/reconnect. strategy_runtime only calls publish_contract for NEW conIds during reconcile (strategy_runtime.py:466 'idempotent — only new conIds trigger publish_contract'), so nothing on either side ever re-requests the data.

- **Failure scenario:** IB Gateway does its standard nightly auto-restart. trader_service reconnects fine, status shows ib_connected=true, portfolio/PnL work. But every ticker feed backing the ZMQ pubsub (strategy bars, CLI listen/watch) is gone: publish_contract returns the cached dead observable and no reqMktData is ever re-sent. Live strategies receive zero bars from that point on and silently stop generating signals — no error anywhere, indefinitely, until a human restarts trader_service.

- **Suggested fix:** In connected_event, snapshot zmq_pubsub_contract_filters keys, clear the filters/contracts dicts, and re-call publish_contract for each previously published conId (contracts are recoverable from the portfolio universe or by caching the Contract objects).

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. On reconnect, disconnected_event→connect_async() replaces self.ib with a fresh IB() (ibreactive.py:333), so all prior reqMktData subscriptions die with the old socket. connected_event() (trading_runtime.py:516-535) disposes/re-subscribes only book/positions/portfolio/PnL via setup_subscriptions; it never touches zmq_pubsub_contract_filters/contracts and never re-calls publish_contract. The filters dict is reset only in the sync connect() path (line 258), never on reconnect. publish_contract short-circuits at line 711 (`if contract.conId in self.zmq_pubsub_contract_filters: return cached observable`). strategy_runtime.subscribe() only calls publish_contract when `conId not in self.strategies` (strategy_runtime.py:277-280), so its 30s reconcile never re-requests either. Net: no reqMktData is ever re-issued; ticker pubsub dies silently. Real bug. Severity medium, not high: for a capital-safety-first low-frequency system this degrades toward NOT trading (fail-safe direction) — resting STP/TRAIL protective orders live at IB and survive; the direct capital risk is loss of availability/strategy-managed exits, not erroneous money movement, though status misleadingly shows connected.


### [ ] MEDIUM — connected_event runs twice per reconnect (eventkit emit + explicit call), causing racy duplicate subscriptions and 3x book event processing

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:579`  ·  _reviewer: ib-listener_

- **Mechanism:** `ib_async.IB.connectAsync` emits `connectedEvent` at its end (verified in ib_async 2.1.0), and `connected_event` is attached before `connectAsync` runs (restored by `_restore_event_handlers`), so eventkit schedules `connected_event()` as a task. The reconnect loop then calls `await self.connected_event()` again at line 579. Two concurrent `setup_subscriptions` runs interleave: each disposes `self.disposables` and clears `pnl_subscriptions` before re-subscribing, so one run can dispose/clear the other's freshly created subscriptions or leave both sets alive (duplicate portfolio/PnL observers). Deterministically, both runs call `book.subscribe_to_eventkit_event(...)`, which does a bare `e += self.on_eventkit_update` with no `in`-check (reactivex.py:150), on top of the one connection re-attached by handler restore — so after a reconnect the book handler is connected 3x to `orderStatusEvent` et al. (eventkit invokes duplicates 'just as many times').

- **Failure scenario:** After the first Gateway reconnect, every order status/fill event is pushed through BookSubject three times: `book.trades`/`book.orders` lists get triplicate prepended entries, `get_trade_log()`/`mmr trades` shows each fill 3 times, and triplicate UpdateEvents go out on ZMQ; duplicated `reqAllOpenOrdersAsync` replays interleave with live status events.

- **Suggested fix:** Pick one trigger: either rely solely on the `connectedEvent` handler and drop the explicit `await self.connected_event()` (or vice versa, detaching the handler), guard `connected_event` with an asyncio.Lock/generation counter, and make `subscribe_to_eventkit_event` skip events the handler is already connected to (`if self.on_eventkit_update not in e`).

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. Installed ib_async 2.1.0 `connectAsync` ends with `self.connectedEvent.emit()` (ib.py), and `connected_event` is re-attached to the fresh IB before that via `_restore_event_handlers` (ibreactive.py:334). eventkit's `Slots.__call__` schedules the coroutine with `asyncio.ensure_future`, so it runs once as a task; trading_runtime.py:579 then `await self.connected_event()` runs it again. `connected_event` (516-535) has no lock, so two concurrent `setup_subscriptions` interleave. `subscribe_to_eventkit_event` uses bare `e += self.on_eventkit_update` with no dedup (reactivex.py:157), so on top of the restore-reattach the book handler ends 3x on `orderStatusEvent`; `book.on_next` prepends (book.py:31-32) → triplicate trade-log/order entries and triplicate ZMQ UpdateEvents. Severity medium not high: the `_pnl_subscriptions_lock` first-claim guard (397-400) and idempotent `__update_portfolio` prevent portfolio/PnL corruption, and no order-placement path is affected — the concrete damage is audit-trail/book duplication plus racy disposable leaks, only after a Gateway reconnect.


## Low bugs


### [x] LOW — backtest_sweep parallel path crashes with AttributeError when any child job times out; backtest_batch reports timeouts as status='ok'

- **Location:** `skills/mmr-skill/scripts/mmr_helpers.py:2351`  ·  _reviewer: llm-loop_

- **Mechanism:** _run_cli_json returns {'data': None, 'error': ..., 'timed_out': True} on timeout and {'data': '<stdout string>', 'error': 'Failed to parse JSON'} on parse failure — it never raises. backtest_batch._one therefore never hits its 'except asyncio.TimeoutError' branch and labels these results status='ok'. backtest_sweep's parallel path then evaluates entry.get('result', {}).get('data', {}).get('summary', {}): since the 'data' key exists with value None (or a str), .get('data', {}) returns None/str and the chained .get raises AttributeError ('NoneType'/'str' object has no attribute 'get'), which is uncaught — the entire sweep coroutine dies after all jobs already ran.

- **Failure scenario:** A 30-combo parameter sweep with concurrency=6 and per_job_timeout=600 runs for 40 minutes; one slow 1-min-bar combo exceeds 600s and comes back as {'data': None, 'timed_out': True} with status 'ok'. The leaderboard loop hits None.get('summary') and backtest_sweep raises AttributeError — 29 successful results are discarded from the return value (persisted rows survive, but the caller gets a traceback instead of a leaderboard) and the LLM re-runs the whole sweep.

- **Suggested fix:** In _one, inspect parsed for 'timed_out'/'error' and return status='timeout'/'error' accordingly; in the sweep leaderboard loop, guard with isinstance(data, dict) before drilling into 'summary'.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end in skills/mmr-skill/scripts/mmr_helpers.py. _invoke (L24-30) subprocess.run raises TimeoutExpired; _run_cli_json_sync (L49-50) catches it and RETURNS {"data": None, "timed_out": True} (parse failure L55-56 returns {"data": <str>, "error": ...}). MMRHelpers.backtest returns this via _run_cli_json_str (L2282) as a JSON string — no exception. backtest_batch._one (L2433-2449) json.loads it and returns status="ok"; the `except asyncio.TimeoutError` (L2450) is unreachable, so timeouts are mislabeled "ok" (contradicting the docstring). backtest_sweep's parallel leaderboard loop (L2348-2352) then does entry["result"].get("data", {}).get("summary", {}); with data=None (timeout) or data=str (parse fail) this raises AttributeError, uncaught (no try/except around the L2346 loop), killing the sweep coroutine and discarding all successful results. Refutation failed. Severity downgraded to low: research/backtest path only, no capital at risk, persisted rows survive; harm is a lost leaderboard + re-run latency.


### [x] LOW — MMRHelpers.cli() splits the command with str.split(), silently mangling quoted arguments

- **Location:** `skills/mmr-skill/scripts/mmr_helpers.py:3630`  ·  _reviewer: llm-loop_

- **Mechanism:** The documented escape hatch does command.split(), so any shell-style quoting the LLM naturally writes — cli('reject 42 --reason "changed thesis"') or cli('propose AMD BUY --reasoning "gap up on earnings"') — is tokenized into '"changed' and 'thesis"', producing wrong argparse values or stray positional-argument errors. Because the CLI may accept the first mangled token as a valid value (e.g. --reason '"changed'), the corruption can be silent rather than a parse failure.

- **Failure scenario:** The LLM has no dedicated helper for a niche command and runs MMRHelpers.cli('universe add asx_watch BHP --exchange ASX --currency AUD') — fine — but later runs cli('reject 7 --reason "stale price, re-evaluate"'); argparse receives extra positionals, errors out (or stores a garbage reason), and depending on the target command the LLM retries with progressively mangled quoting instead of accomplishing the action.

- **Suggested fix:** Use shlex.split(command) instead of command.split(), and note in the docstring that shell quoting is supported.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. mmr_helpers.py:3630 does `args = command.split()`, then `_run_cli(*args)` → `_run_cli_sync` (line 34) invokes the CLI with a list argv (no shell re-parsing). So `cli('reject 7 --reason "stale price"')` tokenizes to `['reject','7','--reason','"stale','price"']`: `--reason` captures the literal `"stale` and `price"` becomes a stray positional that argparse rejects. shlex is never imported (grep confirms). The mechanism is real and unhandled. But two facts cap severity at low: (1) the docstring at line 3622 already documents "The command string is split by spaces," making it a known limitation, and (2) every capital-affecting command has a dedicated typed helper — `propose` (line 2874) and `reject` (line 3009) take real Python args, so the money path already escapes correctly; `cli()` is a genuine niche escape hatch. Mangled quoting almost always yields a loud argparse error, not a silent wrong-sized trade. Fix (shlex.split) is trivial and correct, but not a capital-safety defect.


### [ ] LOW — web_dashboard omitted from PID-clear case and cleanup trap: orphan process + infinite 2s failure spam

- **Location:** `start_mmr.sh:1007`  ·  _reviewer: ops_

- **Mechanism:** Two omissions around WEB_PID: (1) the monitor loop's case statement (lines 1007-1011) clears DATA_PID/TRADER_PID/STRATEGY_PID after a death but has no web_dashboard arm, so once web.app dies, 'kill -0' fails on every 2-second iteration and the loop prints 'web_dashboard (PID n) exited with code 0' forever — unbounded container-stdout growth (compose has no logging size limits configured, so the json-file log grows without bound). (2) the cleanup trap (lines 615-649) SIGINTs/SIGKILLs only $STRATEGY_PID $TRADER_PID $DATA_PID, never $WEB_PID, so in hybrid (host) mode Ctrl-C leaves web.app orphaned holding port 7424; the next ./start_mmr.sh launches a new web.app that fails to bind, dies immediately, and triggers defect (1)'s infinite spam.

- **Failure scenario:** Host developer runs ./start_mmr.sh, Ctrl-Cs it, and starts it again. The old dashboard still owns :7424, the new one crashes on bind, and the console/log fills with a failure line every 2 seconds for the life of the session; in Docker the same spam fills the docker log file on disk.

- **Suggested fix:** Add web_dashboard to the case statement (clear WEB_PID) and include $WEB_PID in the cleanup trap's kill lists.

- **Verifier:** Core defect confirmed end-to-end. Monitor loop checks $WEB_PID (start_mmr.sh:998) and prints "web_dashboard ... exited" on death (line 1005), but the PID-clearing case (lines 1007-1011) omits a web_dashboard arm, so WEB_PID is never blanked; kill -0 fails every 2s (line 1019) and the failure line repeats forever while any real service lives (exit guard at line 1013 also ignores WEB_PID). Unbounded log growth is real. The cleanup trap omission is also real (lines 619/628/640 never signal $WEB_PID), matters in the SIGTERM/docker-stop path where wait (646) then blocks on unsignaled web. However the finding's specific interactive-Ctrl-C orphan scenario is overstated: without job control the background web.app shares the script's process group and receives the terminal SIGINT directly, so it exits on its own. Severity downgraded to low: this is ops/log-hygiene (slow disk fill only after web.app dies), not a trade-correctness or capital risk.


### [x] LOW — Session VWAP resets on UTC calendar day, not the ET trading day

- **Location:** `strategies/vwap_reversion.py:56`  ·  _reviewer: probe-3:Intraday session, timezone, and RTH boun_

- **Mechanism:** `day = prices.index.normalize()` buckets the session by UTC midnight (both ternary branches are identical and neither converts to ET). In production the index is tz-aware UTC, so `normalize()` yields UTC-midnight day keys = 19:00/20:00 ET the prior evening. The docstring claims 'Session VWAP resets at the start of each trading day', but the reset actually happens at ~7-8pm ET. VwapReversion also applies no RTH filter, so its cumulative price*volume/volume VWAP spans the prior day's after-hours, the overnight gap, and pre-market — and any after-hours bars past 19:00 ET (00:00 UTC) spill into the next UTC day. The four sibling intraday strategies all correctly do `idx.tz_convert('America/New_York')` and group by `et.date`; this one is the outlier.

- **Failure scenario:** On US 1-min data stored as UTC, the VWAP for a bar at 10:00 ET is computed from a 'day' that began at 20:00 ET the previous evening and includes overnight/pre-market prints, so the z-score `(close - vwap)/std` is materially off from a true session VWAP. BUY/SELL signals (and the crossed_up exit) fire at different, wrong bars than the documented session-reset logic intends, producing a backtest that does not reflect the stated strategy.

- **Suggested fix:** Match the other strategies: `et = prices.index.tz_convert('America/New_York'); day = pd.Series(et.date, index=prices.index)` and group by that (optionally restrict to RTH).

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. vwap_reversion.py:56 ternary is a genuine no-op (both branches `prices.index.normalize()`), so no ET conversion. duckdb_store.py:213-214 stores/reads OHLCV as UTC-tz-aware; backtester.py:300 feeds that frame to precompute, so `index.tz` is UTC and normalize() yields UTC-midnight keys (~19:00-20:00 ET prior evening). Extended-hours bars are present (massive_history.py:35 Polygon minute aggs default to 4:00-20:00 ET; ib_history_worker.py:248 useRTH=False), and there is no RTH filter, so the cumulative VWAP pools pre-market/RTH/after-hours and the reset lands mid-after-hours, not at session start. Sibling vwap_reclaim.py:44-48 correctly tz_converts to America/New_York and groups by et.date with an RTH mask; this file is the lone outlier. Real bug. Severity is low for a capital-safety-focused system: it degrades one intraday strategy's signal/backtest fidelity but is not a direct loss-of-capital path.


### [x] LOW — trader_exception passes constructor arguments in the wrong order — every TraderException has message=True and scrambled fields

- **Location:** `trader/common/exceptions.py:21`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** trader_exception calls `exception_type(data is not None, client, trader.startup_time, last_connect_time, message, inner, get_callstack(10))` but TraderException.__init__ declares `(message, storage_connected, ib_connected, startup_time, last_connect_time, inner, call_stack)`. Positionally: message becomes the bool `data is not None`, ib_connected becomes a datetime, and the actual message string lands in last_connect_time. __str__ additionally swaps the storage_connected/ib_connected labels (line 55-57). Every exception raised through this helper — order-placement failures, account-pinning rejections in subscribe_place_order_direct, publish_contract errors — carries `.message == True` and misfiled diagnostics, and these are what propagate to RPC clients as exc_args.

- **Failure scenario:** subscribe_place_order_direct refuses an order because order.account mismatches the configured account. The CLI/LLM receives a TraderException whose message field is the literal bool True and whose 'last_connect_time' line contains 'place_order()'; the real refusal reason is buried in the inner exception. An operator (or the LLM loop) triaging a live rejected order gets scrambled diagnostics — a direct fail-loudly violation on the money path.

- **Suggested fix:** Call the constructor with keyword arguments (message=message, storage_connected=..., ...) and fix the label swap in __str__; add a unit test asserting field round-trip.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed by direct code reading. exceptions.py:21-29 passes positional args (data is not None, client, startup_time, last_connect_time, message, inner, callstack) into TraderException.__init__ (line 35-44) whose signature is (message, storage_connected, ib_connected, startup_time, last_connect_time, inner, call_stack). So .message = bool True, and the real message string lands in last_connect_time; __str__ (line 55-57) also swaps storage/ib labels. Traced to money-path callers: account-pinning refusals (executioner.py:72,83-92) and risk-gate/trading-filter rejections (executioner.py:120-149). No tests cover it. Severity is LOWER than medium: the guards still correctly refuse the order — only the exception's diagnostic fields are scrambled, and the real reason remains recoverable via .inner or the mislabeled str() line. This is observability degradation, not a capital-safety failure; no wrong trade results.


### [x] LOW — bool config fields coerced via int() — bool branch unreachable, env override crashes startup

- **Location:** `trader/config.py:164`  ·  _reviewer: ops_

- **Mechanism:** In MMRConfig.from_yaml, nested-field coercion checks 'isinstance(current_val, int)' before 'isinstance(current_val, bool)'. Since bool is a subclass of int, bool-typed fields (massive.delayed, default False) always take the int branch and the elif-bool branch is dead code. YAML-sourced Python bools survive (int(True)==1), but an env-var override is a string: MASSIVE_DELAYED=false → int('false') → ValueError, uncaught, raised during Container.__init__ — so every service and every CLI invocation dies at startup. (Had the bool branch been reachable it would also be wrong: bool('false') is True.)

- **Failure scenario:** Operator exports MASSIVE_DELAYED=true (or false) to toggle the delayed feed, exactly as the 'env vars override config values (uppercased)' doc suggests. trader_service, strategy_service, data_service and the CLI all crash with 'ValueError: invalid literal for int()' before any logging is configured; under Docker the container crash-loops via restart: on-failure.

- **Suggested fix:** Check 'isinstance(current_val, bool)' first and parse with a truthy-string set (like Container._coerce_env_value does: raw.lower() in ('1','true','yes','on')).

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. config.py:59 makes massive.delayed a bool (default False). In from_yaml (config.py:164-167) `isinstance(current_val, int)` is checked before the bool branch; bool subclasses int, so delayed always takes the int branch and the elif-bool branch is unreachable. config.py:147/150 feed a raw env string into `value` when MASSIVE_DELAYED is set, so `int("false")` raises ValueError. This runs inside container.py:103 (MMRConfig.from_yaml) during Container.__init__, which every service and the CLI build at startup, so the uncaught error aborts them. YAML bools survive (int(False)==0); only the documented env-override with non-numeric strings crashes. Real bug. Severity low for a capital-safety-weighted system: it fails loudly at startup, can't produce wrong trades or capital loss, and triggers only when an operator explicitly sets a word-valued MASSIVE_DELAYED (not a default); numeric 1/0 still works.


### [ ] LOW — date_summary() and list_symbols() ignore bar_size, so `mmr data summary` fabricates per-bar-size coverage

- **Location:** `trader/data/data_access.py:468`  ·  _reviewer: data-access_

- **Mechanism:** DuckDBDataStore.min_date/max_date accept a bar_size parameter, but TickData.date_summary() never passes it (nor does summary() or get_data()'s no-range path), so the returned min/max span ALL bar sizes for the symbol. TickData also inherits Data.list_symbols(), which returns every symbol in the shared tick_data table regardless of bar size. `mmr data summary` (mmr_cli.py:7093-7133) iterates per bar_size, calls tickdata.list_symbols() and tickdata.date_summary(), and prints a coverage row per (symbol, bar_size) — but both the symbol list and the start/end dates are cross-bar-size aggregates. Relatedly, summary() (line 496) computes min/max unfiltered but then read()s with the bar_size filter, so `.iloc[0]` raises IndexError when the symbol has no rows at this bar size.

- **Failure scenario:** AAPL has daily bars through today but 1-min bars ending a month ago. `mmr data summary` shows the '1 min' row for AAPL with end = today. The operator (or the LLM loop reading --json output) concludes intraday data is fresh and deploys/keeps a 1-min strategy whose warm-up silently uses month-old data. Wrong data presented as fresh — directly against the 'wrong data is worse than no data' principle.

- **Suggested fix:** Pass bar_size=self.library_name into library.min_date/max_date in date_summary/summary/get_data, and add a bar_size-filtered list_symbols to DuckDBDataStore for TickData to use.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. date_summary (data_access.py:468-469) calls min_date/max_date without bar_size; with bar_size=None those queries span all bar sizes (duckdb_store.py:304-344). TickData.list_symbols (data_access.py:391 -> duckdb_store.py:296-302) returns DISTINCT symbol unfiltered by bar_size. mmr_cli.py:7093-7133 loops per bar_size and prints a coverage row using both, so a symbol with only daily bars appears under a "1 min" row with daily start/end dates — fabricated coverage, confirming the bug. However get_data/read DO filter by bar_size (data_access.py:566), so backtests and live warm-up read correct rows; the defect is confined to the read-only `data summary` inventory (and cli/commands.py:552, polygon_batch.py:73), with no path into any trade computation. summary()'s IndexError is real but that method is uncalled in production. Because a dedicated freshness command (`mmr data status`) exists and nothing consumes this summary to pick data, harm is a misleading table, not a wrong trade — hence low, not medium.


### [x] LOW — Universe.find_symbol treats numeric ticker strings as conIds, breaking or misresolving numeric symbols (e.g. HK tickers 0700/0005)

- **Location:** `trader/data/universe.py:35`  ·  _reviewer: stores_

- **Mechanism:** `find_symbol` does `if type(symbol) is str and symbol.isnumeric(): match conId == int(symbol)` with an `elif` for symbol-name matching, so a numeric ticker string can NEVER match by symbol name. The CLI explicitly supports Hong Kong tickers like '0700' and '0005' (CLAUDE.md examples), and `find_symbol` is used by data_service.py:81 and batch/ib_history_queuer.py:107 to resolve download targets. '0700' becomes a lookup for conId 700; if some instrument with conId 700 exists in any universe, the download resolves to that entirely unrelated instrument — the exact 'integer conId must not blur into string ticker' class of bug the Design Principles call out (in the reverse direction).

- **Failure scenario:** User adds HK ticker 0700 (Tencent) to a universe and requests a history download via data_service; `find_symbol('0700')` searches for conId 700 instead of symbol '0700', either failing to resolve (download silently skipped for that symbol) or, if a stale conId 700 exists, downloading and storing data for the wrong instrument under the wrong key — which later feeds backtests/strategies for Tencent.

- **Suggested fix:** In find_symbol, try an exact symbol-string match first and only fall back to conId interpretation when no symbol matches (mirroring resolve_universe, which checks both), or require callers to pass int for conId lookups.

- **Verifier:** The bug is real and traceable. universe.py:35-40: `if type(symbol) is str and symbol.isnumeric()` matches on `conId == int(symbol)` with an `elif` for name — a numeric ticker string (HK stocks store symbol as "700"/"0700") can never match by symbol name. Reachable via data_service.py:81 (symbols+universe download → find_symbol returns None → "not found" warning, download silently skipped) and mmr_cli.py:9448 (`universe remove 0700` reports not found). Notably resolve_universe (lines 164-182) does check both conId and name, so the symbols-only path is fine; only find_symbol is broken. However, the finding's severe sub-claim — "downloads the wrong instrument under conId 700" — is essentially unreachable: real IB conIds are 6-9 digits, so no `definition.conId == 700` collision occurs. The concrete impact is a silent skip/miss (data-availability/usability), not wrong trades or misfiled data. LOW severity is correct for a capital-safety-weighted system.


### [ ] LOW — IB daily bars keyed at UTC midnight vs Massive/TwelveData daily bars at Eastern midnight — same session gets two different timestamps

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ib_history_worker.py:287`  ·  _reviewer: data-access_

- **Mechanism:** For daily bars ib_async returns datetime.date index values; the worker does pd.to_datetime(index, utc=True) (lines 282-287), stamping session D at 00:00 UTC. massive_history.py:54 and twelvedata_history.py:194 stamp the same session at 00:00 US/Eastern (= 05:00 UTC). Two effects: (1) when a symbol's daily data is refreshed from more than one source (source auto-detects per universe; a conid in two universes/jobs, or a manual --source override), write_resolve_overlap's index-dedup sees two distinct timestamps for the same session and keeps BOTH — duplicate daily bars per session in the store. (2) When IB-sourced daily bars are read back, TickData tz-converts to America/New_York, so session D displays as D-1 19:00/20:00; missing()'s `.index.date` then attributes every IB daily bar to the previous calendar day, making the latest session appear permanently missing (refetch churn every run) and making date-keyed comparisons against exchange_calendars sessions systematically off by one.

- **Failure scenario:** AAPL is in both the 'downloads' universe (twelvedata daily refresh) and later fetched via IB for a strategy warm-up. The store ends up with two bars per session at 00:00Z and 05:00Z; the backtester and live warm-up window see 2x daily bars (one possibly NaN/partial), doubling apparent bar counts and corrupting rolling indicators — silently.

- **Suggested fix:** Normalize daily-bar timestamps to a single convention at write time (e.g. exchange-local midnight, tz-aware) in TickData.write / DuckDBDataStore.write, or fix the IB worker to localize date-typed daily indexes to the exchange tz instead of UTC.

- **Verifier:** Mechanism verified. IB daily bars key at 00:00 UTC (ib_history_worker.py:283-287; date index + utc=True); Massive/TwelveData key at 05:00 UTC (massive_history.py:54, twelvedata_history.py:194). duckdb_store.py:149/214/235 persists both as distinct TIMESTAMPTZ instants, so write_resolve_overlap's index dedup (data_access.py:513) keeps both. On read, _fix_df_timezone converts to America/New_York (data_access.py:335,352), so IB's 00:00Z bar lands at D-1 19:00 and missing()'s resample('D').index.date (data_access.py:621) attributes it to D-1 — off by one vs exchange_calendar sessions. data_service.py:413-428/213 writes IB daily unnormalized through this path. Confirmed. Downgrading severity: the always-firing symptom (IB-daily incremental refetch churn) is pure latency, irrelevant to capital. The duplicate-bar corruption that could poison a backtest requires the same conid+bar_size sourced from both IB and Massive/TwelveData, which the default per-universe source auto-detect never does — only a manual --source/history ib override triggers it. Latent, config-conditional, not a live-order path.


### [ ] LOW — Null-row markers are localized to the machine's local timezone and injected at daily frequency into intraday frames

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ib_history_worker.py:329`  ·  _reviewer: history-workers_

- **Mechanism:** The injected no-data marker rows take a naive midnight date, tz_localize it to the host's local timezone, then tz_convert to tz_info. In the Docker container (UTC) with tz_info='US/Eastern', a marker for June 1 lands at May 31 20:00 ET — the wrong session date — so the marker 'covers' the wrong day in missing(). Separately, missing_dates is computed as a daily-frequency pd.date_range (carrying the first bar's time-of-day) differenced against the intraday index, so for 1-min downloads a NaN row is injected on nearly every day that has real data but no bar at that exact minute; these spurious NaN rows are persisted into tick_data alongside real bars.

- **Failure scenario:** Container (UTC) downloads 1-min US data: each day gains a stray NaN bar at a shifted timestamp, and genuine no-trade-day markers are attributed to the prior date — a day that actually has no data is recorded as covered while the marker's own day already had bars, leaving the true gap invisible to (a fixed) missing().

- **Suggested fix:** Localize marker rows with tz_localize(gettz(tz_info)) directly, restrict injection to daily bar sizes (or exchange-calendar sessions), and never inject markers into intraday frames based on a daily date_range.

- **Verifier:** The two code defects are real and deterministic. ib_history_worker.py:223 defines local_tz as the host tz (UTC in the container); lines 329-330 localize marker rows to local_tz then convert to tz_info, unlike the real-bar path (lines 287-291) which never touches local_tz. In a UTC container with tz_info='US/Eastern', a naive-midnight marker shifts to the prior day 20:00 ET, so missing()'s resample('D').first() (data_access.py:621) attributes it to the wrong session. Line 312's pd.date_range uses default DAILY freq against an intraday index whose earliest_date carries the first bar's minute-of-day, injecting spurious NaN rows into 1-min frames. However, capital impact is negligible: the mislocalized marker leaves the true no-data day uncovered, so missing() re-fetches it (wasted work, not silent gap); spurious 1-min NaN rows land on days already covered by real bars and are dropped by the backtester; and US data uses twelvedata, not this IB path. Genuine data-hygiene bug, correctly rated low.


### [ ] LOW — IB no-data null rows are localized with the host machine timezone, not the requested tz

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ib_history_worker.py:329`  ·  _reviewer: probe-3:Intraday session, timezone, and RTH boun_

- **Mechanism:** Null placeholder rows for missing/no-trade days are built from `earliest_date..current_date` (already in tz_info, e.g. US/Eastern), stripped to naive wall-clock (`replace(tzinfo=None)`), then `tz_localize(local_tz)` where `local_tz` is the host's local timezone captured at line 223, and finally `tz_convert(tz_info)`. Real data rows are placed in tz_info directly. On a UTC host (the Docker deployment), an ET wall-clock like 2024-01-02 00:00 is localized as 00:00 UTC and converted to 2024-01-01 19:00 ET — the previous calendar day. The same download therefore produces different null-row timestamps depending on the host timezone.

- **Failure scenario:** Running `mmr data ib --bar_size '1 day'` inside the UTC container writes daily no-data markers stamped 19:00 ET of the prior trading day; running the identical command on a US/Eastern laptop stamps them at 00:00 ET of the correct day. Coverage/freshness accounting (`data status`) and any consumer that keys on the placeholder day disagree between hosts, and daily null markers can be attributed to the wrong session.

- **Suggested fix:** Localize null rows to tz_info directly (or build them tz-aware in tz_info) instead of round-tripping through the host's local timezone.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed by reproduction. In ib_history_worker.py, missing_dates (line 312) are built from a tz_info-aware date_range; each is stripped to naive tz_info wall-clock (line 314) then re-localized as the host's local_tz (line 329, captured line 223) and tz_convert'd to tz_info (line 330). Real data rows (line 291) skip local_tz entirely. On a UTC host, ET wall-clock 2024-01-02 00:00 becomes 2024-01-01 19:00 ET (prior day); on an ET host today it becomes 23:00 due to fixed-offset DST mismatch — so null-row timestamps are host- and season-dependent. Real bug. Severity low: only NaN placeholder rows for no-data days are affected; backtester drops NaNs and daily upserts DELETE by date range, so real prices/orders are unaffected. Impact is coverage/freshness bookkeeping (data status) disagreeing across hosts, not capital risk.


### [ ] LOW — Every snapshot request permanently leaks two Rx subscriptions on the hot ticker path

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ibreactive.py:520`  ·  _reviewer: ib-listener_

- **Mechanism:** `__subscribe_contract` creates a relay Subject `xs` and subscribes it to the `contracts_subject` filter pipe, but the returned disposable of `contract_filter.subscribe(xs)` (line 520) is discarded — disposing the caller's subscription to `xs` (as `__get_single_mrkt_data` does at line 815) never unhooks `xs` from `contracts_subject`. It also stores `self.error_disposables[reqId] = err.subscribe(...)` (line 541) which is only disposed at full `shutdown()`. Since `unsubscribe_contract` raises 'not implemented' (line 556), there is no cleanup path at all. Every `get_snapshot`/`get_snapshots_batch` call therefore adds one permanent subscriber to the `pendingTickersEvent -> flat_map` fan-out plus one permanent error_subject subscriber and dict entry.

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM loop or cron runs `ideas momentum --location STK.AU.ASX` (53 tickers) hourly: ~106 subscriptions leak per scan, thousands after a few days. Every live tick for every published contract is then filtered through thousands of dead `xs` subjects on the main asyncio loop, steadily inflating CPU per tick and delaying ticker publication to strategies; memory (error_disposables, closures holding Contracts) grows without bound until restart.

- **Suggested fix:** Return/compose the upstream disposable so disposing the outer subscription also disposes `contract_filter.subscribe(xs)`, and remove/dispose `error_disposables[reqId]` when the snapshot completes or times out.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. ibreactive.py:520 `contract_filter.subscribe(xs)` discards its disposable; `contract_filter` derives from `contracts_subject` = `_contracts_source.pipe(flat_map)`, and `_contracts_source` is a hot `EventSubject` fed by `pendingTickersEvent` (reactivex.py:137/195). Each subscribe adds a permanent observer. The snapshot path `__get_single_mrkt_data` (line 772) calls `__subscribe_contract` directly, bypassing `contracts_cache`, so every `get_snapshot` makes a fresh uncached `xs`. Disposal at lines 801/815 only detaches `observer` from `xs`, never `xs` from the source; `error_disposables[reqId]` (541) clears only at `shutdown()` (390); `unsubscribe_contract` raises `not implemented` (556). So each snapshot leaks one hot-source subscriber (filter predicate runs per future tick) plus one error subscriber and dict entry. Real, but purely a CPU/memory-growth issue with no capital-safety impact and mitigated by restarts — low, not medium.


### [ ] LOW — Any IB message carrying the market-data reqId — including informational warnings — is escalated to stream-fatal on_error, failing snapshots that have usable data

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ibreactive.py:541`  ·  _reviewer: ib-listener_

- **Mechanism:** `__subscribe_contract` routes every `error_subject` event with a matching reqId into `xs.on_error(...)` with no severity discrimination. IB sends informational, non-fatal messages against a market-data reqId — e.g. 10167 ('Requested market data is not subscribed. Displaying delayed market data') and 10090 ('part of requested market data is not subscribed') — while data continues to flow. In `__get_single_mrkt_data`, `on_error` sets `thrown_exception`, and line 817 raises it even when a fully populated ticker was already captured (`populated_ticker` is discarded). A Subject that receives on_error is also permanently dead, so the (cached) `subscribe_contract` path would return a poisoned observable with no cache invalidation.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr snapshot BHP --delayed` on an account without a live ASX subscription: IB emits 10167 immediately after `reqMktData`, `on_error` fires before/despite delayed ticks arriving, and the snapshot raises instead of returning the delayed ticker; in `get_snapshots_batch` the symbol is silently omitted from ideas-scan results.

- **Suggested fix:** Maintain a set of informational/warning codes (10167, 10090, 2100-range) that are logged and optionally attached to the ticker but do not terminate the stream; only true failures (200, 354, 10197, 162) should on_error.

- **Verifier:** Code path is real and end-to-end traceable. `__handle_error` (ibreactive.py:222) excludes only 2104/2106/2107/2158; all other codes, incl. informational 10167/10090, go to `error_subject.on_next` (line 237). `__subscribe_contract` routes any reqId-matching event to `xs.on_error` (lines 524-526, 534-541), the reqId capture (line 497) matches getReqId's assignment. In `__get_single_mrkt_data`, on_error sets `thrown_exception` (759-761) and line 817-819 raises it unconditionally, discarding `populated_ticker` (820); the Subject is then terminal so no later delayed tick recovers it. Only external dependency is IB emitting 10167 against the mkt-data reqId while delayed data flows — standard TWS behavior I can't execute here. Severity correctly LOW: snapshots feed research/ideas-scans, so impact is a raised snapshot or a symbol dropped from a scan — a coverage/latency loss, never a wrong trade or capital-safety event.


### [ ] LOW — get_shortable_shares starts a streaming reqMktData that is never cancelled — IB market-data lines leak until the ~100-line cap

- **Location:** `trader/listeners/ibreactive.py:822`  ·  _reviewer: ib-listener_

- **Mechanism:** `get_shortable_shares` calls `__get_single_mrkt_data` with `snapshot=False` and `tick_list=[Shortable]`, which issues a streaming `reqMktData`. The success path of `__get_single_mrkt_data` (lines 814-820) disposes only the Rx observer; `cancelMktData` is called only on the timeout path (line 803). With `unsubscribe_contract` unimplemented, each distinct contract queried for shortable shares permanently consumes one of IB's limited simultaneous market-data lines (default ~100) for the life of the process, on top of the lines already used by `publish_contract` for portfolio/strategy tickers.

- **Failure scenario:** A session with ~50 published portfolio/strategy tickers plus shortable-shares checks across a scan universe crosses IB's line limit; IB returns error 101 ('Max number of tickers reached') and new `publish_contract` calls for freshly added positions silently deliver no data.

- **Suggested fix:** Call `self.ib.cancelMktData(contract)` on the success path whenever the request was streaming (`snapshot=False`) and the contract was not already subscribed by the publish path.

- **Verifier:** The core defect is real and traceable: get_shortable_shares uses snapshot=False (ibreactive.py:830) via __get_single_mrkt_data, which subscribes through __subscribe_contract → self.ib.reqMktData(snapshot=False) (lines 772, 499-502). The success path (lines 814-815, 820) only does Rx subscription.dispose(); cancelMktData runs solely on the timeout path (line 803), and unsubscribe_contract raises not-implemented (line 556). So each distinct contract streams a market-data line for the process lifetime. But the finding's failure scenario is overstated: the only caller is the manual single-symbol CLI command `info shortable` (commands.py:927), not any scan/loop, and IB reuses the line for repeated same-contract queries — so reaching the ~100-line cap needs 100+ distinct symbols manually queried in one session. No capital-safety impact; worst case is silent no-data. Genuine but negligible-severity leak.


### [x] LOW — Sharpe-CI annualization: BarSize(record.bar_size) always throws and is silently swallowed, so bars_per_year is always 252 — wrong for any non-daily decimation and masking a scale mismatch with the decimated curve

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:4975`  ·  _reviewer: backtester_

- **Mechanism:** `_compute_bt_stats` does `BarSize(record.bar_size)` where `record.bar_size` is a string like '1 min' (persisted via `str(bar_size)`), but BarSize is an IntEnum whose values are ints — the by-value lookup raises ValueError on every call. The bare `except Exception: bars_per_year = 252.0` swallows it (fail-loudly violation), so the documented intent ('mirrors Backtester._bars_per_year so the Sharpe bootstrap CI is on the same scale as the stored sharpe_ratio') is dead code. It is only correct by coincidence in the default config, where `_decimate_equity_curve_json` resamples the persisted curve to daily and sqrt(252) matches. With the documented `equity_decimation: none` (or integer-N) mode, the persisted curve of a 1-min run yields per-minute returns annualized by sqrt(252) instead of sqrt(98280): the CI is understated ~19.7x and will not bracket the headline sharpe_ratio, violating the invariant documented at mmr_cli.py:4634-4638. Conversely, anyone 'fixing' the parse to `BarSize.parse_str` without making it decimation-aware would overstate the CI ~19.7x in the default config.

- **Failure scenario:** User sets `equity_decimation: none` in trader.yaml (documented option) and runs a 1-min backtest with true annualized Sharpe ~2.0. `backtests confidence` reports sharpe_ratio CI of roughly [0.05, 0.15] — the LLM/user rejects a genuinely good strategy, or distrusts the entire confidence block because the CI is 20x away from the point estimate.

- **Suggested fix:** Use `BarSize.parse_str(record.bar_size)`, remove the blanket except, and derive the annualization factor from the persisted curve's actual timestamp spacing (e.g. median delta) rather than the run's bar_size, so it stays correct under every decimation mode.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed end-to-end. record.bar_size is a string like '1 min' (backtest_store.py:36 field bar_size: str; persisted via str(bar_size) at mmr_cli.py:6634/6937). BarSize is an IntEnum with int values 0-20 (objects.py:44-65), so BarSize(record.bar_size) at mmr_cli.py:4975 does a by-value lookup on a string and always raises ValueError, swallowed by the bare except at 4977-4978, pinning bars_per_year=252.0 unconditionally. Under the default equity_decimation:daily (trader.yaml:89), the curve is resampled to per-day points (mmr_cli.py:336) so sqrt(252) is right only by coincidence. Under the documented equity_decimation:none / integer-N modes (mmr_cli.py:339-353), a 1-min run keeps per-minute spacing, so per-minute returns (mmr_cli.py:4967) get annualized with sqrt(252) instead of sqrt(~98280) — Sharpe CI mis-scaled ~19.7x, breaking the bracketing invariant at 4633-4638. Severity low: this is a backtest confidence-display/decision-support metric, not an execution or capital path, and it only misfires under an explicitly non-default config with sub-daily bars.


### [x] LOW — reject --all ignores the per-proposal return value and reports success even when the reject failed

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:2570`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** In _handle_reject's --all branch, `mmr.reject(p.id, reason=...)` returns False when the proposal is no longer PENDING (e.g. concurrently approved by another session or the web dashboard) or not found, but the return value is discarded and 'Proposal #N rejected' is printed unconditionally. The single-id branch checks the result; the bulk branch does not — a fail-loudly violation on a state-mutating command.

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM loop approves proposal #7 at the same moment an operator runs `mmr reject --all`. reject(7) returns False (state is APPROVED/EXECUTED), yet the CLI prints 'Proposal #7 rejected'. The operator believes the trade was stopped while the order is live in the market.

- **Suggested fix:** Check the boolean: print a red 'reject failed (status changed?)' line for any proposal where mmr.reject() returns False, mirroring the single-id path.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. `mmr.reject` (sdk.py:1342-1350) returns False when the proposal is missing or `status != 'PENDING'`. In `_handle_reject`'s `--all` branch (mmr_cli.py:2565-2571), the code queries PENDING proposals, then loops calling `mmr.reject(p.id, ...)` and discards the return, printing `Proposal #N rejected` unconditionally. The single-id branch (2578-2582) correctly checks the boolean and prints a failure line otherwise — so the inconsistency is real, not misread. The race is credible in this architecture: the web dashboard (port 7424) and LLM approve loop can transition a proposal PENDING→APPROVED/EXECUTED between the query and the reject call, yielding False that is silently swallowed. This violates the codebase's stated "fail loudly" principle for a state-mutating command. Severity stays low: the window is narrow (TOCTOU only) and reject doesn't itself move money, but for capital-safety it does risk an operator falsely believing a live order was stopped, so it sits at the low/medium boundary.


### [x] LOW — group --budget unit heuristic misinterprets values <= 1 (1 becomes 100%, 0.5 becomes 50%)

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:2595`  ·  _reviewer: cli-1_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_group create/set uses `budget = args.budget / 100.0 if args.budget > 1 else args.budget`. The help text says '20 = 20%', so a user (or LLM, which elsewhere uses 0-1 fractions for --confidence and risk `--max-position-size-pct`) passing `--budget 1` meaning 1% gets max_allocation_pct=1.0 (100%), and `--budget 0.5` meaning 0.5% gets 50%. The inconsistent unit conventions across commands make this heuristic likely to be hit.

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM, pattern-matching the fraction convention used by `risk --max-position-size-pct 0.10`, runs `group create speculative --budget 0.05` intending 5%... which works, but later `group set speculative --budget 1` intending a 1% clamp silently sets the budget to 100%, so the portfolio-risk analyzer never flags the group as over budget and concentration warnings that the LLM loop relies on are suppressed.

- **Suggested fix:** Drop the heuristic: accept percent only (validate 0 < budget <= 100, divide by 100), and reject ambiguous values with an explicit error, consistent with the fail-loudly principle.

- **Verifier:** Code trace is real and complete. mmr_cli.py:2595/2652: `budget = args.budget/100.0 if args.budget > 1 else args.budget` — any value <=1 skips the /100, so `--budget 1` (meaning 1%) stores 1.0 (100%) and `--budget 0.5` stores 0.5 (50%). Stored verbatim in position_groups.py:145. portfolio_risk.py:155-156 computes over_budget as `group_pct > max_allocation_pct` where group_pct is a fraction (value/net_liq, max ~1.0); with budget=1.0 the group can never be flagged, suppressing the warning at :167 and summary at :348-351. No guard exists anywhere. Severity low: group budgets are explicitly soft advisory limits (warnings, not rejections), the help text says "20 = 20%" so the ambiguous <=1 input is atypical, and no capital is directly mis-committed — only an advisory concentration warning is silenced.


### [x] LOW — _compute_bt_stats: BarSize(record.bar_size) always raises, pinning Sharpe-CI annualization to 252 regardless of bar size

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:4975`  ·  _reviewer: cli-2_

- **Mechanism:** BarSize is an IntEnum whose values are 0..20; record.bar_size is a string like '1 min' (written via str(bar_size)). `BarSize(record.bar_size)` therefore raises ValueError for every stored row (verified: BarSize('1 min') / BarSize('1 day') both raise), and the broad `except Exception` silently falls back to bars_per_year=252.0. The correct call is BarSize.parse_str(...). The code comment claims it 'mirrors Backtester._bars_per_year so the Sharpe bootstrap CI is on the same scale as the stored sharpe_ratio', but that never happens. With the default equity_decimation='daily' the 252 fallback is accidentally correct (the persisted curve is daily), but with equity_decimation='none'/N (a documented trader.yaml knob, and all rows persisted before decimation existed) the bar returns are per-bar (1-min), the headline sharpe was annualized with sqrt(~98,280), and the CI is annualized with sqrt(252) — ~19.7x too small. Note also: a naive 'fix' to parse_str would break the default daily-decimated path, because the factor must match the decimation actually applied to the stored curve, not the run's bar_size.

- **Failure scenario:** With `equity_decimation: none`, a 1-min 365-day run stores sharpe_ratio=2.1. `mmr backtests confidence <id>` reports sharpe_ratio_ci_lo/hi_annualized around [0.05, 0.15] — a CI that doesn't remotely bracket the point estimate. The LLM decision loop (or a human) either rejects a genuinely strong strategy or, having learned the CI is 'broken', starts ignoring the confidence block entirely, defeating the deploy/reject gate.

- **Suggested fix:** Use BarSize.parse_str(record.bar_size), and derive bars_per_year from the granularity of the persisted equity curve (e.g. infer from timestamp spacing, or store the decimation mode on the record) rather than the run's bar_size.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed. BarSize is an IntEnum (objects.py:44-65); record.bar_size is a VARCHAR string (backtest_store.py:36,554). Executed proof: BarSize('1 min')/BarSize('1 day') both raise ValueError, so mmr_cli.py:4975 always throws and the except at 4977 pins bars_per_year=252.0; the "mirrors Backtester._bars_per_year" comment never runs. Headline sharpe uses _bars_per_year(config.bar_size)=98,280 for 1-min (backtester.py:568), while the CI annualizes with sqrt(252) (backtest_stats.py:319,329) — ~19.7x mismatch under equity_decimation none/N on intraday curves. Severity lowered to low: it is an advisory confidence metric (no execution impact); the default daily decimation path is correct, and any daily-bar run — the norm for a low-frequency book — hits _bars_per_year(Days1)=252 so the fallback is coincidentally right. Only intraday runs with non-default decimation are affected.


### [ ] LOW — Sweep pipeline has no exception safety: one unexpected job exception (or a parent crash) leaves the sweep stuck in status='running' forever

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:6001`  ·  _reviewer: cli-2_

- **Mechanism:** _execute_jobs_parallel returns `await asyncio.gather(*(_one(j) for j in jobs))` without return_exceptions=True, and _one only catches asyncio.TimeoutError and json.JSONDecodeError. Any other exception — OSError from create_subprocess_exec (EMFILE/ENOMEM is realistic with concurrency up to 16 spawning pandas-heavy children), or UnicodeDecodeError from the strict stdout.decode()/stderr.decode() calls — cancels all sibling tasks and propagates out of _run_sweeps_async. Because finalize_sweep (line 5889) and _write_sweep_digest are not in a try/finally, the sweeps row created up-front with status='running' is never transitioned: no digest, results of already-completed jobs uncounted, in-flight subprocesses orphaned. backtest_store.py has no recovery/reconciliation for stale 'running' rows (verified by grep), so the same permanent-'running' state results from any parent crash (OOM, reboot) — a stated crash-recovery concern for a cron-driven nightly pipeline. `sweep watch` (line 6495) loops until status != 'running', so it spins forever on such a sweep, and `sweep list` misreports it as active indefinitely.

- **Failure scenario:** Nightly cron runs `mmr sweep run nightly.yaml` with 1080 jobs; 400 jobs in, the machine hits fd/memory pressure and one create_subprocess_exec raises OSError. asyncio.run raises, the process exits, the 400 persisted child rows are never summarized, sweeps row #12 stays 'running' forever, no morning digest is written, and the next morning `mmr sweep watch 12` hangs indefinitely.

- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the per-job body in a broad try/except returning {'status': 'error', ...} (or pass return_exceptions=True and map exceptions to error results), decode subprocess output with errors='replace', and move finalize_sweep into a try/finally. Add a startup/list-time sweep reconciliation that marks 'running' sweeps with no live parent as 'failed'.

- **Verifier:** The bug is real and traceable. mmr_cli.py:6001 gathers without return_exceptions=True; _one (5936-5999) only catches TimeoutError/JSONDecodeError, so an OSError from create_subprocess_exec (5956, realistic under ENOMEM/EMFILE on a 1080-job pandas-heavy nightly run) or a strict UnicodeDecodeError (5974/5981/5989/5998) propagates. finalize_sweep (5889) is not in try/finally in _run_sweeps_async, so the row stays status='running' forever; backtest_store.py has no stale-running reconciliation, so any parent crash (OOM/reboot) yields the same. sweep watch loops on status=='running' (6495) and never self-terminates. However, severity is LOW for this system: the sweep pipeline is a backtest/research orchestrator that places no orders and touches no live capital. Each child persists its own BacktestRecord independently, so only the parent summary/digest is lost — an operational annoyance, not a capital-safety defect.


### [ ] LOW — Sweep run permanently replaces the process SIGINT handler and never restores it

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:5841`  ·  _reviewer: cli-2_

- **Mechanism:** _run_sweeps_async installs signal.signal(SIGINT, _on_sigint) and never restores the previous handler after the sweeps finish. In the interactive mmr REPL (a long-lived process), every subsequent Ctrl-C in the same session goes to the stale closure: it sets the old sweep's local cancel dict and prints 'SIGINT received — waiting for in-flight jobs to finish' instead of raising KeyboardInterrupt. Commands that rely on KeyboardInterrupt to exit — `sweep watch` (except KeyboardInterrupt at line 6507), `watch`, `listen` — become uninterruptible for the rest of the session.

- **Failure scenario:** In a REPL session the user runs `sweep run nightly.yaml` (completes normally), then `sweep watch 13` on another sweep. Ctrl-C prints the misleading 'waiting for in-flight jobs' message and the watch loop keeps running; the user has to kill the whole mmr process from another terminal.

- **Suggested fix:** Save the previous handler (signal.getsignal) and restore it in a finally block around the sweep loop.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. mmr_cli.py:5841 installs signal.signal(SIGINT, _on_sigint) with no restore anywhere before the function ends at line 5912 (no finally/getsignal). The REPL is long-lived and dispatches commands in-process (10001-10043), and `sweep run` runs `_run_sweeps_async` in-process via asyncio.run (5808). `_on_sigint` (5832-5838) only sets an out-of-scope dict and prints the "waiting for in-flight jobs" message — it never raises KeyboardInterrupt. So after a `sweep run`, a subsequent `sweep watch` loop (6489-6511, `while True: _time.sleep`, `except KeyboardInterrupt`) swallows Ctrl-C and never breaks; same for other KeyboardInterrupt-reliant loops. prompt_toolkit only owns signals during session.prompt(), not during dispatch(), so the stale handler is active during command execution regardless. Real but low severity: it degrades interruptibility (forces process kill) and cannot affect trade correctness or capital — the handler's only effects are a flag and a print.


### [x] LOW — strategies available: project-root detection probes 'configs/trader.yaml', a path that doesn't exist anywhere

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:3626`  ·  _reviewer: cli-2_

- **Mechanism:** _handle_strategies_available resolves a relative strategies directory by walking up from __file__ looking for `(cur / 'configs' / 'trader.yaml')`. The repo ships `config_defaults/trader.yaml` (verified: no configs/ directory in the repo, Dockerfile, or start scripts; user config lives in ~/.config/mmr). The marker never matches, so the walk falls through and the relative 'strategies' dir resolves against os.getcwd(). Inside the container the CLI's cwd is /home/trader (the exact problem _resolve_strategy_path at line 5603 was written to fix), so `mmr strategies available` reports 'Strategies directory not found' or scans an empty dir instead of the install root's strategies/.

- **Failure scenario:** An LLM agent inside the container runs `mmr --json strategies available` from /home/trader to enumerate deployable strategies; it gets a directory-not-found failure (or an empty list) and concludes no strategies exist, even though strategies/ is populated at the mmr install root.

- **Suggested fix:** Reuse the trader.__file__-based root resolution from _resolve_strategy_path (or probe 'config_defaults/trader.yaml').

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. trader/mmr_cli.py:3626 probes 'configs/trader.yaml' as the project-root marker; repo-wide grep shows that string exists ONLY there and no configs/ dir exists anywhere — the shipped file is config_defaults/trader.yaml. Config default strategies_directory='strategies' (config_defaults/trader.yaml:15) is relative, so the walk-up loop (3624-3629) never matches, never breaks, and strategies_dir stays cwd-relative Path('strategies'). is_dir() (3631) then resolves against os.getcwd(); the sibling _resolve_strategy_path docstring (5609-5610) documents containerized cwd is /home/trader, so /home/trader/strategies misses → line 3632 'Strategies directory not found'. The correct trader.__file__ root resolution already exists at 5626-5628, confirming the fix. Severity LOW: read-only enumeration command, no capital impact — worst case a false 'no strategies' report.


### [ ] LOW — Dead cleanup branch in data download's trader_service probe — failed probe leaks the RPC client

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:7323`  ·  _reviewer: cli-3_

- **Mechanism:** In the soft-probe block (lines 7310-7326), `rpc_mmr` is assigned only as the final statement of the try (`rpc_mmr = candidate`, a plain name bind that cannot raise). Therefore in the except handler `rpc_mmr is not None` is always False: the `rpc_mmr.close()` cleanup is unreachable dead code, and the intended target — `candidate`, which was constructed and possibly connect()ed before get_status() failed — is never closed. Each failed probe leaks the MMR client's ZMQ DEALER socket/context for the remainder of the process. In a one-shot CLI this is cleaned at exit, but `data refresh --all` invokes _handle_data_download once per job in the same process, accumulating one leaked client per job whenever trader_service is down.

- **Failure scenario:** trader_service is down during a nightly `mmr data refresh --all` with several jobs: candidate.connect() succeeds (ZMQ connect is lazy) but get_status() times out for each job; each job leaks an unclosed RPCClient/socket. Beyond the resource leak, the except branch's intent (close the half-open client) never executes, so the process exits with lingering sockets and, if reused as a library entry point, they persist indefinitely.

- **Suggested fix:** Close `candidate` in the except handler (guarding for it being unbound if MMR() itself raised), e.g. initialize candidate=None before the try and close candidate on failure instead of rpc_mmr.

- **Verifier:** Control flow verified end-to-end. mmr_cli.py:7310 inits rpc_mmr=None; the try's final statement rpc_mmr=candidate (7321) is a name bind that can't raise, so if get_status() (7320) throws, rpc_mmr stays None and the except guard `if rpc_mmr is not None` (7323) is always False. candidate — a live RPCClient whose connect() (sdk.py:184) sets up a ZMQ socket — is never closed. The intended cleanup is dead code; the leaked object is candidate, not rpc_mmr. Accumulation confirmed: _handle_data_refresh reuses _handle_data_download per job in one process (mmr_cli.py:7724), so `data refresh --all` leaks one client per job while trader_service is down. Real but low: pure resource leak, no capital/order/data-correctness impact, reclaimed at process exit. Low is the appropriate ceiling.


### [ ] LOW — Options buy/sell emit non-JSON console lines to stdout, corrupting --json output

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:8718`  ·  _reviewer: probe-0:Options live-order path: contract constr_

- **Mechanism:** In _handle_options the buy/sell branches call console.print('[dim]Using expiration: ...') unconditionally (mmr_cli.py:8715-8719, 8732-8736). console = Console() writes to stdout. Unlike _print_trade_result, these prints are not gated by _json_mode, so `mmr --json options buy/sell` (relative expirations always trigger the print) emit a human-readable line before the JSON object, breaking machine parsing in the LLM/automation path.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr --json options buy AAPL -e 3m -s 250 -r C -q 5 --market` outputs 'Using expiration: 2026-09-30' then the JSON result; a consumer doing json.loads(stdout) fails to parse the combined output.

- **Suggested fix:** Gate these informational prints behind `if not _json_mode:` (or route them to stderr), consistent with the rest of the CLI.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed. `console = Console()` (mmr_cli.py:31) writes to stdout and is never redirected for JSON mode. The options buy/sell branches call `console.print(f'[dim]Using expiration: {expiration}[/dim]')` at lines 8718-8719 and 8735-8736 with no `_json_mode` guard. This fires whenever `expiration != args.expiration`, which is true for any relative expiration (`_resolve_expiration` returns a resolved date != the `'3m'` input, lines 8211-8214) and for the default None case; only an exact YYYY-MM-DD returns as-is and skips it. `_print_trade_result` (2201-2219) does gate on `_json_mode` and emits only JSON, so the un-gated dim line precedes the JSON object, breaking `json.loads(stdout)`. Severity stays low: it corrupts only `--json` feedback framing, not the order that gets placed (the print precedes `buy_option`); parse failure aborts rather than mis-trades.


### [x] LOW — propose --group registers un-uppercased symbol, causing case-mismatch exclusion from budget

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:1164`  ·  _reviewer: probe-2:position_groups store and group-budget e_

- **Mechanism:** The propose parser defines the `symbol` positional with no normalization (mmr_cli.py:1164), and _handle_propose passes args.symbol through verbatim to mmr.propose (mmr_cli.py:2339), which registers membership via gs.add_member(group, symbol) using that raw string (sdk.py:1194). By contrast `group add` uppercases (mmr_cli.py:2636 `sym.upper()`) and portfolio positions carry IB's uppercase contract.symbol (sdk.py:479). Group-budget compliance tests membership with `p['symbol'] in group.members` (portfolio_risk.py:152), an exact case-sensitive comparison, so a lowercase-registered member never matches the uppercase portfolio symbol.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator runs `mmr propose bhp BUY --market --group mining` (group already exists). Membership row 'bhp' is written. Position fills as 'BHP'. In portfolio-risk, 'BHP' in ['bhp'] is False, so the position contributes $0 to the mining group_value and the mining budget is silently under-counted / never flagged as over budget.

- **Suggested fix:** Uppercase/normalize the symbol in propose() before add_member (and ideally store all group members in a canonical case), matching the `group add` path.

- **Verifier:** Traceable end-to-end. propose's `symbol` positional (mmr_cli.py:1164) is passed verbatim to mmr.propose (mmr_cli.py:2339); no `.upper()` exists in the propose path. sdk.py:1194 calls gs.add_member(group, symbol) and position_groups.py:175-178 inserts the raw string with no canonicalization. By contrast `group add` uppercases (mmr_cli.py:2636), and portfolio positions carry IB's uppercase con['symbol'] (sdk.py:479). Budget compliance uses case-sensitive `p['symbol'] in group.members` (portfolio_risk.py:152), so a lowercase-registered member ('bhp') never matches an uppercase position ('BHP'), silently under-counting group_value. Real bug.
