Severity low, not medium: group budgets are soft limits producing warnings (not trade rejections) per CLAUDE.md, the trigger needs atypical lowercase input, and the only effect is an under-counted advisory warning — no wrong trade or direct capital loss.


### [x] LOW — budget '<=1' heuristic silently turns tight budgets (1%, 0.5%) into huge ones (100%, 50%)

- **Location:** `trader/mmr_cli.py:2595`  ·  _reviewer: probe-2:position_groups store and group-budget e_

- **Mechanism:** Both `group create` (mmr_cli.py:2595) and `group set` (mmr_cli.py:2652) normalize with `budget = args.budget/100.0 if args.budget > 1 else args.budget`. Values <= 1 are treated as already-fractional. So `--budget 1` (user intending 1%) is stored as 1.0 = 100%, and `--budget 0.5` (intending 0.5%) is stored as 0.5 = 50%. PositionGroupStore.create_group/update_group perform no validation (position_groups.py:55-79,133-157). portfolio_risk then compares group_pct against this fraction (portfolio_risk.py:156), so an intended very-tight cap becomes effectively unlimited enforcement.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator wants to cap a speculative group at 1% of the book and runs `group create punts --budget 1`. It stores 1.0 (100%). The group can grow to the entire portfolio and over_budget never triggers, so the concentration guardrail the operator set is silently absent.

- **Suggested fix:** Interpret --budget strictly as a percent (always divide by 100), or reject/clamp ambiguous values; validate range in the store rather than relying on a magnitude heuristic.

- **Verifier:** Confirmed at code level. `--budget` is documented as a percent (mmr_cli.py:1247/1261), but the `if args.budget > 1` heuristic (mmr_cli.py:2595/2652) leaves values <=1 unscaled: `--budget 1` stores 1.0 (100%), `--budget 0.5` stores 0.5 (50%). The store does no validation (position_groups.py:55-79/133-157). portfolio_risk.py:154-156 computes group_pct as a fraction <=1.0 and only flags over_budget when it exceeds max_allocation_pct, so a stored 1.0 can never trigger — the tight cap is silently absent. Two mitigants argue for LOW, not medium: the create message echoes the misread value ("budget 100%", mmr_cli.py:2598-2604), giving the operator a visible cue, and group budgets are advisory-only warnings that never block or size an order (CLAUDE.md soft-limit design). So capital is never moved by this; it only weakens a warning.


### [x] LOW — close_position does not cap the requested quantity at the position size, so an oversized 'close' flips the position

- **Location:** `trader/sdk.py:1462`  ·  _reviewer: sdk_

- **Mechanism:** close_qty = abs(quantity) is used verbatim with action derived from the position sign; there is no check that quantity <= \|pos_size\|. A quantity larger than the holding places a market order that closes the position and opens an opposite one -- the executioner's SANITY_CHECK/risk gate has no 'do not flip on close' rule. For a method named close_position (and the CLI 'close' command built on it), silently establishing a new short is wrong-trade behavior, and skip_risk_gate=True (close-all path) removes even the generic guards.

- **Failure scenario:** User holds 80 AMD, types 'close' with quantity 100 (stale mental note of position size). SELL 100 MKT executes: position is now short 20 AMD with no stop, accruing unbounded risk until noticed.

- **Suggested fix:** Clamp close_qty to abs(pos_size) (or fail with an explicit error when quantity exceeds the position).

- **Verifier:** Traceable end-to-end. trader/sdk.py:1462 sets close_qty=abs(quantity) with no clamp to abs(pos_size); action (1463) comes only from position sign, so a quantity exceeding the holding flips the position. The CLI 'close' command exposes --quantity (mmr_cli.py:514) and passes it raw to close_position (mmr_cli.py:2781), so a user typing `close N --quantity 100` on an 80-share holding sends SELL 100 MKT, leaving short 20. risk_gate.py:61-66 only checks concentration vs portfolio, with no anti-flip rule, and a small opposite position passes; close-all uses skip_risk_gate=True. Severity stays low: only reachable via explicit --quantity override (default close and close-all can't flip), and the CLI shows a confirmation prompt echoing the share count (mmr_cli.py:2776) before submitting. Still a real un-stopped-short/wrong-trade hazard worth a clamp.


### [ ] LOW — total_trades counts individual fills (BUY+SELL) rather than round trips, halving every trade-count reliability gate

- **Location:** `trader/simulation/backtester.py:679`  ·  _reviewer: backtester_

- **Mechanism:** `BacktestResult.total_trades = len(trades)` where `trades` contains one entry per fill, so a position that is opened and closed counts as 2. Every downstream reliability gate is calibrated in 'trades': `_bt_composite_score` (mmr_cli.py:4867-4875) penalizes <10/<30/<100 trades, and the deploy heuristic `trades_ok = r.total_trades >= 30` (mmr_cli.py:4840). The statistical layer meanwhile counts round trips (`n_trades` from `round_trip_pnls`), so the two 'trade counts' shown to the user differ by ~2x for the same run.

- **Failure scenario:** A lucky strategy with only 5 round trips (10 fills) reports total_trades=10, escaping the intended 0.2 reliability multiplier (gets 0.6 instead) and outranking better-sampled runs in `backtests list`; a 15-round-trip run passes the `>= 30 trades` confidence gate that was designed to require 30 independent trades.

- **Suggested fix:** Either report round trips in total_trades (count SELL fills / matched lots) or add a separate `round_trips` field and re-point the composite-score and `trades_ok` gates at it.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. backtester.py:428 appends one BacktestTrade per fill (BUY and SELL), so backtester.py:679 total_trades=len(trades) counts fills. The statistical layer counts round trips: backtest_stats.py:76-115 FIFO-matches SELLs to BUYs, n_trades=len(pnls) (line 294) ~= half of total_trades. The reliability gates read total_trades (fills): _bt_composite_score thresholds <10/<30/<100 (mmr_cli.py:4867-4875) and trades_ok = r.total_trades >= 30 (mmr_cli.py:4840), whose own comments (mmr_cli.py:4808) describe thresholds in "round-trips" — confirming the ~2x calibration mismatch. No guard corrects it. However this only affects backtest ranking/display and the "strong" flag; CLAUDE.md states the composite score is explicitly not a deploy/reject metric and the deploy decision uses the statistical-confidence block, which correctly counts round trips. So it weakens a guardrail with a correct backstop rather than causing bad trades — low severity for a capital-safety lens.


### [ ] LOW — Per-conid data-load exceptions are swallowed; a multi-conid backtest silently proceeds on a subset of instruments

- **Location:** `trader/simulation/backtester.py:311`  ·  _reviewer: backtester_

- **Mechanism:** In `run()`, each conid's history load is wrapped in `except Exception as e: logging.warning(...)` and the loop continues; the run only fails if ALL conids are empty (line 313). The BacktestResult and the persisted BacktestRecord are still labeled with the full requested conid list, and nothing in the result records which conids actually loaded. This violates the project's 'fail loudly, not silently' principle: an infra error (DuckDB IOException under sweep concurrency, schema mismatch, corrupt rows) is indistinguishable from 'strategy chose not to trade that symbol'.

- **Failure scenario:** A nightly sweep runs 20 children concurrently; DuckDB read throws IOException for 4 of 10 conids in one child. That child persists a 'successful' run over 6 instruments, tagged as a 10-instrument run. Its metrics land in the sweep leaderboard next to true 10-instrument runs; the user deploys the winning params believing they were validated on the full universe.

- **Suggested fix:** Raise on load errors (distinguish 'no rows in range' from 'read failed'), or at minimum record loaded-vs-requested conids on BacktestResult/BacktestRecord and surface a warning in --json output and the sweep digest.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. backtester.py:310-311 swallows any per-conid load exception with only a warning and continues; the run aborts only if ALL conids fail (313). duckdb_store.py:208-211 returns an empty DataFrame for no-rows (routed to the 309 warning branch) but lets real infra errors raise from execute_atomic (IOException after retries, schema/corrupt-row errors), which are then swallowed — so an infra failure on a subset is indistinguishable from "no trades." BacktestResult (56-76) carries no loaded-vs-requested conids field, and run()/CLI persist the full requested conid list onto the record, so a subset run is mislabeled as full-universe and can contaminate the sweep leaderboard. Not refutable. Severity downgraded to low vs reporter's medium: this is offline validation with no direct live-capital exposure, warnings are logged, and it requires an infra-level exception (transient IOException is retried ~32x) to trigger.


### [ ] LOW — next_open fills feed the fill bar's completed OHLCV to the slippage model — lookahead in cost modeling

- **Location:** `trader/simulation/backtester.py:455`  ·  _reviewer: backtester_

- **Mechanism:** When a queued signal fills at bar t+1's open, `_execute_signal` is passed `bar.iloc[-1]` — the COMPLETED bar t+1 — as `bar_row`, and the slippage model reads its high/low/volume (slippage.py:43-49, 63-67). At the moment of an open fill, that bar's range and volume are future information. FixedBPS (default) ignores the bar so the default path is unaffected, but SquareRootImpact and VolatilitySlippage compute impact from data unavailable at fill time.

- **Failure scenario:** A backtest configured with `slippage_model=VolatilitySlippage()`: entry fills at the open of a bar that subsequently has a huge intrabar range are charged k·range/price slippage derived from the not-yet-observed range — modeled costs correlate with the fill bar's future volatility, biasing per-trade P&L in a way no live execution would experience (typically penalizing entries into bars that later moved, i.e., distorting exactly the trades being evaluated).

- **Suggested fix:** Pass the previous (signal) bar, or the fill bar's open-only view, to the slippage model on next_open fills.

- **Verifier:** The lookahead exists as described. At backtester.py:455, `bar.iloc[-1]` — the fully-completed fill bar t+1 — is passed as `bar_row`, while `fill_basis`/`open_price` (bar t+1's open, correct) is separate. At line 384 that `bar_row` flows into `slippage_model.calculate`. SquareRootImpact reads high/low/volume (slippage.py:43-49) and VolatilitySlippage reads high/low (slippage.py:63-67) of that completed bar — values not observable at the open-fill instant. So a non-default slippage model derives cost from the fill bar's future intrabar range/volume. The default is FixedBPS (backtester.py:158-159), which ignores `bar`, so the shipped default path is unaffected; `fill_policy='next_open'` is the default (line 40). Severity is correctly low for a capital-safety lens: this is backtest cost-estimation only (never touches live execution or the propose/approve pipeline), and only on an opt-in non-default slippage model. It can spuriously bias parameter selection but cannot lose real money.


### [x] LOW — SIGINT handler calls loop.run_until_complete inside the running loop — RuntimeError, and the is_stopping latch then blocks all further stop attempts

- **Location:** `trader/strategy_service.py:45`  ·  _reviewer: strategy-rt_

- **Mechanism:** stop_loop is registered via loop.add_signal_handler, so it executes as a callback inside the running loop. With pending tasks present (the runtime task always is), it calls loop.run_until_complete(asyncio.wait(...)), which raises 'This event loop is already running'; the exception aborts the callback before loop.stop()/exit(0), and because is_stopping was already set True, every subsequent SIGINT is ignored. The service cannot be stopped cleanly and must be SIGKILLed, skipping any graceful ZMQ/DuckDB teardown.

- **Failure scenario:** Operator hits Ctrl+C (or pycron sends SIGINT) to stop strategy_service; nothing happens, an asyncio 'Exception in callback' traceback is logged, further Ctrl+C presses are no-ops, and the process must be killed with SIGKILL.

- **Suggested fix:** In the handler, cancel pending tasks and call loop.stop() (or schedule an async shutdown coroutine with loop.create_task) instead of run_until_complete; reset or remove the is_stopping latch on failure.

- **Verifier:** Real bug. strategy_service.py:58 registers stop_loop via loop.add_signal_handler(SIGINT), so it runs as a callback inside the live loop.run_forever() (line 95) and overrides the default SIGINT→KeyboardInterrupt (making the except at line 96 dead). On Ctrl+C: line 34 passes, line 35 latches is_stopping=True, and with the runtime task always pending (line 91) line 45 calls loop.run_until_complete → RuntimeError "This event loop is already running" (verified empirically). The exception aborts before loop.stop()/exit(0) (46-47); asyncio logs it and keeps running; is_stopping now True makes every later SIGINT no-op (line 34). Service needs SIGKILL. Correction: pycron does NOT send SIGINT — stop_job uses psutil kill()=SIGKILL (pycron/pycron.py:255-256), so supervised shutdown is unaffected; only interactive Ctrl+C is broken. stop_loop does no order/ZMQ/DuckDB-safe teardown, so no capital risk — LOW is correct.


### [x] LOW — News sentiment fallback attributes another ticker's sentiment to the scanned ticker

- **Location:** `trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:856`  ·  _reviewer: idea-scanner_

- **Mechanism:** In IdeaScanner._fetch_news, if no insight in the article matches the queried ticker exactly (or the matching insight has an empty sentiment string), lines 856-858 fall back to a.insights[0] — the sentiment and sentiment_reasoning for whichever ticker Polygon listed first in a multi-ticker article. That sentiment is then stored under the scanned ticker's 'sentiment'/'catalyst' columns with no indication it belongs to a different company. This contradicts CLAUDE.md's 'no fake or estimated sentiment' principle: mislabeled sentiment is worse than none.

- **Failure scenario:** Scanning SMCI with --news returns an article covering NVDA/AMD/SMCI whose insights list starts with NVDA but whose SMCI insight is absent (or the ticker string differs, e.g. class-share formatting). The scan row shows sentiment='positive', catalyst='strong datacenter demand for NVDA GPUs' attributed to SMCI; the LLM cites this as an SMCI catalyst when proposing a BUY.

- **Suggested fix:** Only use the exact ticker-matched insight; if none exists, leave sentiment/catalyst empty (the headline alone is still useful).

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end in trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:849-858. The exact-ticker loop (851-854) only sets sentiment when an insight's `ticker` equals the queried ticker. When no match exists, or the matched insight has an empty sentiment string, `not sentiment` is true and lines 856-858 fall back to `a.insights[0]` — the first insight in a multi-ticker Polygon article, which can belong to another company. That value is stored under the scanned ticker's `sentiment`/`catalyst` keys (870-871, 882) with no cross-ticker marker, contradicting CLAUDE.md's "no fake or estimated sentiment." No downstream guard was found. The scenario hinges on Polygon returning multi-ticker articles lacking the queried ticker's own insight (plausible; not verifiable from code), but the code path itself is unconditional given that data shape. Severity lowered to low: this is an advisory enrichment field (headline stays correct), only active with `--news`, and sits behind the propose→review→approve gate — not a direct trade trigger.


### [x] LOW — Over-broad warrant filter endswith('W') silently excludes legitimate tickers (SNOW, DOW, LOW, GLW, TROW)

- **Location:** `trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:608`  ·  _reviewer: idea-scanner_

- **Mechanism:** IdeaScanner._build_candidates skips any ticker where any(ticker.endswith(s) for s in ('W','WS','.U','.R')) intending to drop warrants/units. But endswith('W') matches ordinary common stocks: SNOW, DOW, LOW, GLW, TROW, PLOW, WOW, etc. The same filter is duplicated in TwelveDataIdeaScanner._build_candidates (line 1668). These names can never appear in any Massive or TwelveData scan result, whether from movers, --tickers, or --universe — and an explicit `ideas momentum --tickers SNOW` returns an empty result with no explanation, violating fail-loudly.

- **Failure scenario:** User runs `mmr ideas momentum --tickers SNOW DOW LOW` — all three are silently dropped in _build_candidates and the command prints 'No ideas found', which the user/LLM interprets as 'none met the criteria' rather than 'the filter ate them'. Market-wide scans permanently omit these large caps.

- **Suggested fix:** Polygon warrant/unit tickers follow specific patterns (5+ chars ending in W, or explicit '.WS'/'.U' suffixes); use ticker-type metadata from the snapshot (snap.type) or restrict the W heuristic to length>=5, and never apply the heuristic to explicitly user-supplied tickers.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. `scan()` with `source='tickers'` calls `_discover` (idea_scanner.py:569-572) → `get_snapshot_all(tickers=[...])` → unconditionally `_build_candidates` (line 492). At line 608 `any(ticker.endswith(s) for s in ('W','WS','.U','.R'))` uses `continue`, dropping any ticker ending in 'W'. SNOW, DOW, LOW, GLW, TROW are all-uppercase (so the separate lowercase-'p' preferred check at 610 doesn't apply) yet end in 'W', so they're silently skipped; scan returns an empty DataFrame → "No ideas found". No `snap.type`/metadata guard and no exemption for user-supplied `--tickers`. The TwelveData path duplicates the identical bug at line 1668. So `mmr ideas momentum --tickers SNOW DOW LOW` yields nothing, and market-wide scans permanently omit these large caps — a real fail-loudly violation. Severity lowered to low: this is a discovery/completeness defect that suppresses candidates; it never misdirects an order or risks capital, which is what matters most for this low-frequency system.


### [x] LOW — NameError: exchange_hint referenced in the IB scanner-discovery branch but only defined in _resolve_symbols

- **Location:** `trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:1084`  ·  _reviewer: idea-scanner_

- **Mechanism:** In IBIdeaScanner.scan, the scanner-discovery branch (no --tickers/--universe) evaluates `raw_exchange = r.get('exchange','') or exchange_hint or 'SMART'` at line 1084, but exchange_hint is never assigned anywhere in scan() (verified via AST: no Store of that name in the function); it is a local of the separate _resolve_symbols method (line 1226). Due to or-short-circuiting the bug is latent while every scanner row has a non-empty 'exchange', but scanner_data populates that field as `c.primaryExchange or c.exchange` (ibreactive.py line ~1178) which can be empty for some scanner results, at which point the entire scan crashes with an unhandled NameError instead of results or a meaningful IdeaScannerError.

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr ideas momentum --location STK.AU.ASX` (scanner path) returns a row whose contractDetails carry neither primaryExchange nor exchange → line 1084 raises NameError: name 'exchange_hint' is not defined, aborting the whole scan with a stack trace unrelated to the actual cause.

- **Suggested fix:** Compute the exchange hint from the location code once at the top of scan() (via the same — fixed — mapping used by _resolve_symbols) and pass it explicitly.

- **Verifier:** The bug is real. In IBIdeaScanner.scan (idea_scanner.py:985), line 1084 references `exchange_hint`, but grep/AST over the whole function body (985–1096) shows it is never assigned there — it exists only as a local in the separate `_resolve_symbols` (idea_scanner.py:1226). The scanner-discovery branch (no --tickers/--universe) is reachable, and scanner rows come from ibreactive.py:1180, which sets `'exchange': c.primaryExchange or c.exchange`. When a scanner contractDetails carries neither field (common for minimal IB scanner contracts on some locations/secTypes), `r.get('exchange','')` is `''`, so `'' or exchange_hint` evaluates the undefined name and raises NameError, aborting the scan with a misleading traceback instead of a clean IdeaScannerError. The trigger (empty exchange) is broker-data dependent, but the undefined-name defect is unconditional once reached. Severity is low for a capital-safety lens: it only crashes a read-only discovery path with a confusing error; it cannot produce a wrong order or risk capital.


### [x] LOW — Per-symbol resolution failures swallowed at DEBUG level — requested tickers silently vanish from results

- **Location:** `trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:1274`  ·  _reviewer: idea-scanner_

- **Mechanism:** _resolve_symbols catches all exceptions per symbol (line 1274-1275) and logs unresolved symbols only at logger.debug (lines 1245, 1275), then continues. The all-failed case raises IdeaScannerError, but partial failures — a typo'd ticker, a transient RPC timeout for one symbol — leave no visible trace: the symbol simply doesn't appear in the output. The user explicitly asked for these symbols; per the fail-loudly principle a partial drop should be surfaced. The same silent-omission pattern applies to get_snapshots_batch failures (logged only in the trader_service log, invisible to the CLI caller).

- **Failure scenario:** `mmr ideas momentum --location STK.AU.ASX --tickers BHP CBA CSLL` (typo for CSL): CSLL fails resolution, is debug-logged and dropped; results show two rows and the user/LLM never learns their third candidate was never scanned — they assume CSL didn't rank.

- **Suggested fix:** Collect unresolved symbols and either raise, or attach a warnings list to the result / log at WARNING with the unresolved names.

- **Verifier:** Accurate and traceable. trader/tools/idea_scanner.py:1245 and :1275 log unresolved/errored symbols only at logger.debug then continue; the caller raises IdeaScannerError only when ALL symbols fail (lines 1053-1058), so a partial failure (typo'd/transient one ticker) is dropped with no WARNING and no output trace — invisible in default CLI runs. Contrast the history path, which logs at WARNING (line 1130). This is intentional (test_unresolvable_symbols_skipped, tests/test_idea_scanner.py:1570-1592, asserts "silently skipped") yet conflicts with the fail-loudly principle the code comment itself cites (lines 1046-1049). Severity low: `ideas` is a research/discovery command, not an order path — no capital moves directly; harm is a user/LLM misreading a dropped candidate as un-ranked, an observability gap rather than a mis-trade.


### [ ] LOW — OrderValidator.sanity_check_order is an unconditional no-op, so SANITY_CHECK orders sized off IB's -1/NaN bid sentinel go straight to IB

- **Location:** `trader/trading/order_validator.py:34`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** place_order_simple routes through ExecutorCondition.SANITY_CHECK, but sanity_check_order returns True unconditionally — the check advertised by the enum does not exist. Meanwhile helper_create_order (executioner.py:216) computes `quantity = equity_amount / (latest_tick.bid * multiplier)` where the snapshot path explicitly accepts IB's -1 'no quote' sentinel and NaN partial tickers as valid (ibreactive.py:740-748, 'returning partial data is better than timing out'). bid=-1 yields a negative totalQuantity; NaN bid yields totalQuantity=nan. Nothing validates quantity > 0 or price sanity before placeOrder; IB rejects these asynchronously after the RPC has already returned the placed Trade as success.

- **Failure scenario:** After hours, `buy XYZ --market --amount 5000` on a thinly-quoted symbol: snapshot returns bid=-1, quantity computes to -5000, MarketOrder(action=BUY, totalQuantity=-5000) is submitted. IB rejects it asynchronously with an error event, but the CLI already reported the order as placed — the user believes they hold a position they don't, and only spots the rejection by reading logs.

- **Suggested fix:** Validate quantity (finite, > 0) and tick prices (finite, > 0) in helper_create_order, and implement or delete the no-op sanity_check_order so SANITY_CHECK isn't a false safety claim.

- **Verifier:** Traced end-to-end. trading_runtime.py:1246 feeds get_snapshot's ticker into helper_create_order; ibreactive.py:740-748 deliberately accepts IB's -1 sentinel and returns NaN-bid partial tickers. executioner.py:216 computes quantity = equity_amount/(latest_tick.bid*multiplier) with no finiteness/positivity guard (the 218 clamp only handles 0<q<1), so bid=-1 yields -5000 and bid=NaN yields nan. The risk gate (executioner.py:137, risk_gate.py:38-83) never receives the quantity — evaluate only checks order count/daily loss/signal rate with position_value=0. sanity_check_order (order_validator.py:35) returns True unconditionally. The order is then submitted (executioner.py:165) and the Trade returned as success. So the SANITY_CHECK enum is a false claim and bad quantities reach IB. Severity is genuinely low: IB rejects negative/NaN BUY quantities asynchronously, so no bad fill or capital loss — the harm is a misleading success report, not lost money.


### [x] LOW — Group-budget analysis swallows all exceptions, silently dropping over-budget warnings

- **Location:** `trader/trading/portfolio_risk.py:179`  ·  _reviewer: risk-math_

- **Mechanism:** The entire group-allocation block is wrapped in `try: ... except Exception: pass`. Any failure in group_store.list_groups() (DuckDB lock contention — explicitly a known condition in this codebase, schema issue, etc.) silently produces a report with empty group_allocations and no over-budget warnings, indistinguishable from 'no groups defined'. Same fail-loudly violation pattern as the correlation block.

- **Failure scenario:** A concurrent backtest sweep holds the DuckDB lock past the retry budget when the LLM runs portfolio-risk before approving a mining trade; list_groups() raises IOException, the except swallows it, group_allocations is [] and the 'mining at 26% exceeds budget 20%' warning never appears — the trade is approved into an over-budget group.

- **Suggested fix:** Catch narrowly, log the error, and append a warning dict (level='critical', message='group analysis failed: ...') to the report instead of passing.

- **Verifier:** Accurate: portfolio_risk.py:179-180 is `except Exception: pass` around the whole group block. list_groups() (position_groups.py:116) calls db.execute, which per CLAUDE.md retries IOException 32x then raises — a genuine propagation path under DuckDB lock contention. When swallowed, report.group_allocations stays [] and the over-budget warning is never appended, a real "fail loudly" violation. Severity stays LOW: the per-symbol concentration (>15%/>10%) and HHI warnings are computed BEFORE the try (lines 121-143), so gross over-concentration is still flagged; group budgets are explicitly soft limits (warnings, not rejections); empty allocations are observable rather than fully silent; and the trigger needs a ~45s retry-exhausting lock burst to coincide with a pre-approval portfolio-risk call. Fix as suggested (log + critical warning), but not a capital-safety-critical gap.


### [ ] LOW — connected_event runs twice concurrently on every reconnect, duplicating book event handlers and subscriptions

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:579`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** In disconnected_event, connect_async() restores the preserved trader.connected_event handler onto the fresh IB before ib.connectAsync() runs (ibreactive.py:334). ib_async's connectAsync ends with `self.connectedEvent.emit()` and eventkit `asyncio.ensure_future`s coroutine handlers (verified in installed eventkit/event.py:106), so connected_event is already scheduled as a task when line 579 then explicitly `await self.connected_event()` — two concurrent executions. Each disposes self.disposables, clears pnl_subscriptions, and runs setup_subscriptions; interleaving at any await point means: (1) book.subscribe_to_eventkit_event uses a bare `+=` with no dedupe and its attachment is never in disposables, so after a reconnect each order event is delivered to the book ~3x (1 restored + 2 setup runs); (2) the second run clears pnl_subscriptions entries the first run just claimed, producing duplicate reqPnLSingle subscriptions; (3) two schedule_periodic pnl.post_all timers and duplicate ZMQ dataclass publishes.

- **Failure scenario:** IB Gateway restarts; reconnect succeeds. From then on every orderStatus/openOrder event is processed 2-3x by BookSubject and published in duplicate/triplicate over ZMQ; duplicate PnL subscriptions are issued per conId. On a subsequent order fill the dashboard and any pubsub consumer see repeated conflicting updates, and duplicate periodic pnl posts run for the rest of the session.

- **Suggested fix:** Either don't call connected_event() manually after connect_async (rely on the event), or remove connectedEvent from the preserved-handler list so only the explicit call runs. Add an idempotency/serialization guard (asyncio.Lock) inside connected_event, and dedupe subscribe_to_eventkit_event attachments.

- **Verifier:** The double-execution is real. `connectedEvent` is in `_PRESERVED_IB_EVENTS` (ibreactive.py:59) and restored to the fresh IB before connecting (ibreactive.py:332-334); `connectAsync` emits it (ib_async/ib.py:2103) and eventkit `ensure_future`s the coroutine (event.py:105-106) → run #1. Line 579 then awaits `connected_event()` again → run #2. `connected_event` has no re-entrancy guard (trading_runtime.py:516-535); `subscribe_to_eventkit_event` uses bare `+=`, returns no disposable, and eventkit never dedupes (event.py:205-206), so book handlers stack. The line-574 `not in` guard only stops duplicate registration, not duplicate execution. Downgrade to LOW: consequences are duplicate telemetry (ZMQ book/pnl publishes), duplicate IB PnL subscriptions (partly bounded by the first-claim lock at 397-400), and a second post_all timer — all only after a Gateway reconnect and cleared on the next disconnect (disposables.clear, 531). No traced path to wrong orders or capital loss; book/orderStatus events are idempotent per order id and feed display, not the risk gate/event store.


### [x] LOW — connect() backoff retry decorator is dead code — inner except rewraps ConnectionRefusedError into TraderConnectionException

- **Location:** `trader/trading/trading_runtime.py:206`  ·  _reviewer: runtime_

- **Mechanism:** @backoff.on_exception is configured to retry on (ConnectionRefusedError, TimeoutError), but the method body's `except Exception as ex: raise trader_exception(self, TraderConnectionException, ...)` (line 286-287) converts every failure — including a refused socket while IB Gateway is still booting — into TraderConnectionException, which is a plain TraderException subclass (verified in trader/common/exceptions.py), not a subclass of either matched type. The decorator therefore never retries: max_tries=10/max_time=120 is inert.

- **Failure scenario:** Host boots; pycron starts ib-gateway and trader_service in parallel. Gateway takes 40s to open port 4003. trader_service's first connect() gets ConnectionRefusedError, which is rewrapped and propagates immediately — the service crashes on first attempt instead of retrying for up to 120s, leaving the whole trading stack down (or in a pycron restart loop) after every deploy/reboot.

- **Suggested fix:** Re-raise ConnectionRefusedError/TimeoutError unwrapped before the generic except, or make backoff match TraderConnectionException.

- **Verifier:** Verified end-to-end. connect() (trading_runtime.py:206-287) wraps its whole body in try/except; the socket call self.client.connect()→ibreactive.py:282 self.ib.connect() raises ConnectionRefusedError on a boot race, but line 286-287 `except Exception` rewraps every failure into TraderConnectionException. exceptions.py:67 shows TraderConnectionException(TraderException(Exception)) is NOT a subclass of ConnectionRefusedError/TimeoutError, and backoff.on_exception only retries instances of its matched types — so it re-raises immediately and max_tries/max_time are inert. Dead code confirmed. Caller trader_service.py:80 has no retry loop and only catches KeyboardInterrupt/SystemExit, so the service exits on first refused connection. Severity lowered to low: this is a startup-availability/latency issue (mitigated by pycron auto-restart), not a capital-safety or wrong-trade risk — no path leads to bad orders or fills.


### [x] LOW — Shared module-global Markdown converter is not thread-safe under FastAPI threadpool

- **Location:** `web/app.py:53`  ·  _reviewer: web_

- **Mechanism:** _MD is a single module-global markdown.Markdown instance. _render_md does _MD.reset() then _MD.convert(...). Route handlers are plain def, so FastAPI runs each request in a threadpool worker, and fetch_proposals calls _render_md in a loop AFTER _call has returned (outside _mmr_lock). Python-Markdown instances hold mutable per-conversion state and are documented as not thread-safe; two concurrent dashboard requests (the page auto-reloads every 15s and multiple tabs/CSRF requests are possible) can interleave reset()/convert() on the same _MD, producing corrupted/mixed reasoning HTML or raising mid-parse. The comment 'A shared converter is fine as long as we .reset() it' is only true single-threaded.

- **Failure scenario:** Two browser tabs auto-refresh within the same ~100ms window; both worker threads enter _render_md on _MD, one thread's reset() wipes state mid-convert of the other, yielding garbled reasoning HTML for a proposal or an exception that blanks the proposals section (caught at line 201).

- **Suggested fix:** Construct a fresh markdown.Markdown per call, or guard _render_md with a lock, or use markdown.markdown() (which builds a throwaway instance) instead of a shared converter.

- **Verifier:** Real, traceable race. Shared _MD (app.py:45) is reset+converted without a lock in _render_md (app.py:53-54), called in a loop in fetch_proposals (app.py:171) OUTSIDE _mmr_lock (lock only spans m.proposals(), app.py:167/97). Endpoints are sync def (app.py:184) so uvicorn (app.py:257) runs them on the anyio threadpool; GIL allows a thread switch mid-convert. Concurrency is realistic via 15s auto-reload (dashboard.html:315) across multiple tabs. Python-Markdown instances are not thread-safe, so interleaved reset()/convert() can garble or raise. No guard exists anywhere — cannot refute. Severity lowered to low: _render_md only affects reasoning_html; proposal id/action/quantity come from _records and approve/reject POSTs never call it, so no capital-safety impact. Failure is cosmetic (garbled/blank reasoning), caught at app.py:201, and self-heals on the next refresh.


## Refuted (traced and dismissed — do not chase)

- `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:149` — EXT_DATETIME round-trip mutates naive datetimes into tz-aware UTC and silently falls back to local time for non-IANA tz names

- `trader/messaging/clientserver.py:452` — Fire-and-forget asyncio.create_task for RPC request handling holds no reference — tasks can be garbage-collected mid-flight

- `trader/data/duckdb_store.py:192` — NULL bar_size rows match every bar_size read filter but are never removed by the bar_size-filtered DELETE, producing duplicated bars that grow on each merged rewrite

- `trader/data/data_access.py:526` — Default DateRange end uses dt.datetime.now() evaluated once at import — reads in long-lived processes are truncated at process start time

- `trader/listeners/ibreactive.py:588` — pnl_cache is checked but never written, so its dedup guard is inert and cancel_single_pnl is a permanent no-op

- `trader/common/contract_sink.py:91` — ContractSink.on_next calls DataFrame.append, removed in pandas 2.x — crashes on the second tick if ever used

- `trader/listeners/twelvedata_history.py:107` — Non-benign TwelveData chunk failures (429, outage, plan limit) are swallowed and the download is reported successful

- `trader/mmr_cli.py:7000` — backtest --json emits invalid JSON (Infinity/NaN) for sortino/sharpe/calmar — only profit_factor is sanitized

- `config_defaults/logging.yaml:113` — 'propogate: no' misspelling — service loggers still propagate; multi-process RotatingFileHandlers share files

- `scripts/docker-entrypoint.sh:44` — chown failure fallback does chmod -R 777 on the bind-mounted host data directory

- `trader/trading/executioner.py:96` — Event-store write failure after placeOrder converts an already-placed live order into a reported failure

- `strategies/opening_drive_fade.py:77` — Hardcoded 390 bars/session makes ATR NaN (no signals) on non-1min or short-history data

- `trader/simulation/backtester.py:493` — close_by_time EOD-flat exit compares UTC bar time-of-day against an ET target, firing hours early


## Uncertain (hinge on runtime/broker behavior)

- `trader/data/duckdb_store.py:192` — NULL-bar_size rows leak into every bar-size library and are duplicated on each write_resolve_overlap cycle

- `trader/listeners/ib_history_worker.py:131` — IBHistoryWorker.connected flag goes stale after a Gateway restart, so history requests fail forever without reconnecting

- `trader/listeners/ibreactive.py:679` — The snapshot 'fast path' is unreachable for both of its only callers, so the dedupe-stall mitigation it documents never engages

- `skills/mmr-skill/scripts/mmr_helpers.py:2834` — close_all_positions() (and universe_delete) run blocking subprocess.run on the event loop and raise uncaught TimeoutExpired mid-liquidation
